**Symptom (two faces):** (a) ordering — delete the old folder's files before the new copy is fully written+verified (or rewrite `assetRef` to the new path before the new files exist) and a mid-operation crash/quota-fail leaves a live `GltfAsset.assetRef` pointing at a now-missing path → the renderer load-errors with no recovery. (b) residue — `storage.delete` is FILE-only; deleting every file under a folder leaves the now-EMPTY directory (and empty subdirs) behind, so a "renamed"/"deleted" asset's folder handle still resolves (`getDirectoryHandle` succeeds on the empty dir) — the asset looks half-deleted and a later same-name import suffix-collides against the ghost.

**Trap (wrong fix / false green):** assert only `exists(newPath/file) === true` after rename — green while the old folder + old assetRefs still linger. Or test delete with `exists(file)` only (MemoryStorage deletes the file AND has no dir concept, so the unit test passes) while OPFS in the browser leaves an empty dir the unit env never sees (the backend-asymmetry blind spot — observe the REAL backend's dir, not just MemoryStorage's file map).

**Real fix:** the fail-safe lifecycle is **copy-all-new → verify-all-new (`exists` each) → rewrite assetRefs in ONE `dispatchAtomic` (K6, undoable) → delete-old → bump** (see [[K14]]). NEVER delete-old before new is verified: a crash then leaves a recoverable DUPLICATE, never a dangling ref. The assetRef rewrite is a single `dispatchAtomic` so it is all-or-nothing. For residue: a `deleteOpfsTree` helper removes files, THEN every now-empty subdir deepest-first, THEN the root — `removeEntry` removes an EMPTY directory too (`OpfsStorage.ts:83-90`), and the dir-deletes are harmless no-ops on MemoryStorage. Observe BOTH backends: the unit test asserts file-absence (MemoryStorage), the e2e asserts the OPFS _directory handle_ no longer resolves (`getDirectoryHandle` throws). Asymmetry (CONTEXT D-03): glTF persists `assetRef` → rewrite required; BVH/FBX leave NO ref → folder-move only (`nodesReferencingImport` returns []).

**Detection signal:** grep an asset rename/delete for `storage.delete(old…)` reached before an `exists(new…)` verify, or a delete loop that removes files but never the parent dir. Runtime fingerprint: a renamed asset whose old folder still appears in OPFS, or a GltfAsset that load-errors right after a rename.

**Five-limbed argument:**

1. **Claim:** with no move primitive, rename/delete must be copy→verify→rewrite-refs→delete + an explicit empty-dir prune, or it orphans a ref or leaves residue.
2. **Reason:** the capability exposes only per-file delete and no atomic move; the OPFS dir lingers after its files are gone; a half-completed sequence with the wrong order leaves a live ref pointing at deleted bytes.
3. **Universal principle:** when the substrate offers no atomic move, the only crash-safe order writes+verifies the destination fully BEFORE mutating the source, and a "remove" must remove the container, not just its contents.
4. **Application:** `renameImportedAsset`/`deleteImportedAsset` copy→verify→rewrite(1 dispatchAtomic)→`deleteOpfsTree` (files+dirs+root); BVH/FBX skip the ref step.
5. **Conclusion:** the bug is a substrate-capability-gap bug, not an import bug. The fix is the fail-safe order + dir prune; the proof observes BOTH the moved/cleared OPFS dir AND the followed/removed assetRef on BOTH backends.

**Sibling:** [[K6]] (one dispatchAtomic per mutation — the rewrite is one atomic). [[H57]]/[[V13]] (the break-refs removeNode chain roots its closure on the referencing nodes). The backend-asymmetry blind spot is the same shape as [[H40]] (observe the real surface, not the convenient proxy — here MemoryStorage's file map vs OPFS's directory tree).

Provenance: ORIGIN = #112 (P7.14 Wave B), 2026-06-01 — the first e2e of `renameImportedAsset` passed its unit test (file present) but the OPFS old-dir handle still resolved (empty dir left behind), and a naive delete-before-verify would orphan the assetRef. WHY = without this entry the next storage-backed move/delete repeats the delete-before-verify order or the file-only delete, and "verifies" it with a MemoryStorage unit test that can't see the lingering OPFS dir. HOW = copy→verify→rewrite-refs(atomic)→deleteOpfsTree(files+empty-dirs+root); observe the real OPFS directory handle, not just the file map. REF: `src/app/asset/importCommon.ts` (`renameImportedAsset`/`deleteImportedAsset`/`deleteOpfsTree`/`listFilesDeep`), `src/app/asset/importRefs.ts` (`nodesReferencingImport`), `src/core/storage/StorageCapability.ts:17-42` (no move primitive), `tests/e2e/p7.14-my-imports-mgmt.spec.ts` (OPFS-dir-handle observation on the real backend). Issue #112.

### H61 — A fixed-timeout e2e assertion on a CPU-heavy async-completion UI passes locally and fails DETERMINISTICALLY on a ~3× slower CI runner — and reads like a logic bug, not a flake

**Span:** any e2e assertion of the form `await expect(locator).toBeVisible({ timeout: <short> })` (or any single fixed-timeout wait) that gates on the completion of a multi-step, CPU-bound async chain — React re-render + three.js/glTF (re)load + store re-enumeration — not just a single IO op. Instantiated at `tests/e2e/p7.14-my-imports-mgmt.spec.ts:121-123` (#112): the renamed-asset row appears only AFTER copy-all → verify-all → assetRef rewrite → viewport glTF RELOAD → delete-old → bump → React re-enumerate; a 5 s window held locally and missed on CI (e2e job ran ~21 m vs ~6.8 m local — ~3×).

**Symptom:** the test fails ONLY on CI, on EVERY attempt (initial + retry), while green on every local run — so it reads as a deterministic regression, not a timing flake. The failure screenshot/error-context shows the pre-operation state (here: the OLD "flat-asset" row still present, no error banner), which looks exactly like "the operation never happened / silently broke."

**Trap (wrong fix / false diagnosis):** conclude from the snapshot that the feature is BROKEN (the row never renamed → hunt for a logic bug in `renameImportedAsset`, a storage backend-asymmetry, a stale-closure on the rename input, an OPFS consistency lag). All plausible, all wrong — the operation completes correctly given time. Burning the budget proving a non-bug is the real cost. The deeper trap: the fixture is tiny (~3.5 KB), so "the copy is slow" is dismissed — but the latency is CPU-bound (React + three.js reload competing for the main thread), NOT IO-bound, so file size is a red herring in BOTH directions.

**Real fix:** reproduce the slow runner DETERMINISTICALLY with CDP CPU throttling (`client.send('Emulation.setCPUThrottlingRate', { rate: 8 })`) — a throwaway spec that throttles, runs the exact flow, then dumps the REAL post-operation state (OPFS dir listing + the DAG assetRefs). Observation here: under 8× throttle the rename COMPLETES perfectly (`user-imports/` = `[renamed-asset]`, old dir `THREW NotFoundError`, assetRef followed) — it just takes >5 s. That proves "calibration, not logic," so the fix is to widen the ONE heavy assertion's timeout to match the operation's real worst-case latency (here 15 s), consistent with the file's sibling assertions that already use auto-retrying `expect.poll`. Widening a timeout to match a genuinely-completing async op is NOT the [[base-layer]] "setTimeout to paper over ordering" anti-pattern — there is no ordering bug; the order is correct and observed.

**Detection signal:** a test that is green locally + red on CI on every attempt (not 1-in-N), whose failure artifact shows the PRE-operation UI with no error surfaced, and whose gated operation involves a viewport asset (re)load or other CPU-heavy work. Quick discriminator: CDP CPU-throttle the flow locally and inspect the backend's ground truth after a generous wait — if the state is correct, it is calibration; if wrong, it is a real bug.

**Five-limbed argument:**

1. **Claim:** the rename e2e failed on CI because a 5 s `toBeVisible` is shorter than the rename's CPU-bound completion time on a ~3× slower runner, not because the rename is wrong.
2. **Reason:** under 8× CPU throttle the rename's full OPFS + DAG outcome is observably correct, only later than 5 s; the same chain finishes <5 s on fast local hardware.
3. **Universal principle:** a fixed assertion timeout encodes an assumption about hardware speed; an assertion gating on CPU-heavy async completion must budget for the slowest target environment, or it tests the runner's speed, not the feature.
4. **Application:** widen the renamed-row assertion to 15 s (the heaviest mgmt op — it triggers a viewport glTF reload the two delete tests do not); leave the lighter delete assertions (sync banner / BVH delete, no reload) at 5 s, which held on CI.
5. **Conclusion:** the bug is a test-calibration bug, not an import/storage/UI bug; the proof is the throttled run's correct OPFS ground truth, never the un-throttled local pass alone.

**Sibling:** [[H60]] (the rename op this test covers — also a "observe the real backend, not the proxy" entry; here the proxy was the un-throttled local run). [[H58]] (e2e must drive the real affordance) — complementary: H58 says drive the real button, H61 says budget the real latency. The CDP-CPU-throttle technique is the [[base-layer]] Lokāyata gate applied to CI-only failures: reproduce the slow environment, then observe ground truth instead of inferring a logic bug from a pre-operation snapshot.

Provenance: ORIGIN = #126 / P7.14 follow-up, 2026-06-01 — after the #125-vs-#126 catalogue merge resolved CI's long-red `lint`, the e2e job surfaced the NEW `p7.14 (rename)` test failing on CI (both attempts) while green locally; the failure snapshot showed the old row + no banner, inviting a logic-bug hunt. WHY = without this entry the next CI-only e2e failure on a viewport-loading flow gets diagnosed as a feature regression and the budget is spent proving a non-bug; the CDP-throttle repro short-circuits that. HOW = CPU-throttle the flow → dump backend ground truth → if correct, widen the one heavy assertion; reserve the widening for the asset-reload-gated assertion, not blanket every timeout. REF: `tests/e2e/p7.14-my-imports-mgmt.spec.ts:121-123` (the widened assertion + rationale comment), `src/app/asset/importCommon.ts` (`renameImportedAsset` — the correct, completing op), `src/app/AssetsPopover.tsx` (the `tick`-keyed re-enumeration the row waits on), [[feedback-ci-lint-superset]] / [[project-ci-gating-rot]] (the sibling CI-truth lessons). Issue #112 (test), #126 (PR).

---

### H62 — An opaque-only contrast audit composited against the BEST-CASE fixed background silently passes translucent chrome that sits over a VARIABLE backdrop — the green CI gate is a lie for exactly those surfaces

**Span:** any contrast-audit that composites a semi-transparent surface (`bg-*/N`) down to one opaque hex against a single assumed page background, when the surface physically sits over a backdrop the audit does not control — a WebGL canvas, an `<img>`/`<video>`, a user-themed region, a backdrop-filter pane. Instantiated at `src/a11y/contrastMatrix.test.ts` (D-W8-1): the matrix composites every row against `bg #0a0a0a`; R8 (`FloatingViewportToolbar`) and ModeBadge (`bg-2/90`) sit over the GL canvas, whose color is scene-dependent. For them `#0a0a0a` is the BEST case (the backdrop can only get brighter), so their PASS bounded nothing.

**Symptom:** the audit is green and looks total ("every (fg,bg) pair audited"), but a whole class of surfaces was measured against a backdrop they never actually have. No test fails; the gap is invisible until a user loads a bright HDRI/matcap and reports washed-out glyphs (or never reports, and the regression ships).

**Trap (wrong fix / false diagnosis):** (a) trust the green gate and declare contrast "done" — the coverage drift-gate even reinforces the illusion by proving every token class is _enumerated_; (b) when the gap is noticed, over-correct by killing the translucency (make the surface opaque) to force the `#0a0a0a` composite TRUE — sacrificing the aesthetic to fix a problem that may not exist; (c) reach for a per-frame pixel-probe that adapts fg opacity — adding exactly the per-frame readback cost other work fought to remove. All three skip the cheap first move: compute the WORST-case backdrop and observe the real pixels.

**Real fix:** two cheap layers. (1) FORMULA — recomposite the over-canvas surfaces against the worst-case displayable backdrop `#ffffff` (a white blowout) and assert AA there, not only against the best-case page bg. The `/N` alpha does the masking: `bg-2/90` over `#ffffff` composites to `#2d2d2d`, and `fg-dim #a3a3a3` on it holds 5.44:1 ≥ AA. (2) OBSERVATION — drive the real backdrop to the worst case (a DEV-only `__basher_setSceneBackground` seam) and pixel-sample the actually-composited overlay (screenshot → in-page Image→canvas→getImageData; the browser decodes the PNG, no decoder dep), measuring the SURFACE (the only scene-dependent value) and using the opaque fg token (scene-independent, read via getComputedStyle). Formula + observation agreed: predicted 5.44:1, measured 5.47:1. Critically, the e2e carries a FALSIFICATION guard — the bright scene must measurably lighten the surface vs the dark scene — or a no-op seam would make the gate vacuously green (the H62 trap recurring inside its own fix).

**Detection signal:** a surface whose Tailwind bg carries a `/N` alpha AND whose DOM ancestor is a canvas / media element / themed region / backdrop-filter pane, while the contrast row composites it against a fixed token bg. Quick discriminator: ask "what is ACTUALLY painted behind this element, and did the audit composite against that or against an assumption?" If the answer is "an assumption (the page bg)," the PASS is unbounded for that row.

**Five-limbed argument:**

1. **Claim:** R8 + ModeBadge's contrast PASS was an inference, not a bound, because the matrix composited them against `#0a0a0a` while they render over a variable GL canvas.
2. **Reason:** alpha-over compositing means the surface color = `fg.a·token + (1-fg.a)·backdrop`; with the backdrop assumed `#0a0a0a` but actually up to `#ffffff`, the measured ratio differs from the real ratio for any `/N < 100` surface.
3. **Universal principle:** a contrast audit is only valid against the WORST-case backdrop the surface can actually have; compositing against the best case proves nothing about readability.
4. **Application:** recomposite the two over-canvas rows against `#ffffff` (formula) AND pixel-sample them over a real bright scene (observation), with a falsification that the scene change actually moved the surface.
5. **Conclusion:** the surfaces are verified safe (≥5.44:1 over any displayable backdrop) without changing the design — the inferred risk did not survive observation, and a regression now fails CI.

**Sibling:** [[H58]] (e2e must drive the REAL affordance, not a proxy) — H62 extends it to "audit against the REAL backdrop, not an assumed one." Shares the [[base-layer]] Lokāyata gate with [[H61]] (observe ground truth instead of trusting the convenient case: H61 = the fast runner, H62 = the dark scene). The falsification-guard discipline mirrors the `p7.13` material-override falsification test. REF: `src/a11y/contrastMatrix.test.ts` (worst-case-`#ffffff` `it()` block), `tests/e2e/p57-bright-scene-contrast.spec.ts` (real-pixel gate + falsification), `src/viewport/SceneBgTestSeam.tsx` (the DEV-only bright-scene seam), `docs/UI-SPEC.md` §8.4.1 + §1 D-W8-1 (the reworded contract). Issue #57.

### H63 — A shared commit chokepoint with asymmetric callers — a later caller wires only PART of the seam's contract — so a feature works through one surface and silently no-ops through its sibling

**Span:** any chokepoint a mutation is _supposed_ to route through, that gains callers at different times. Consolidating the seam guarantees its BODY is shared — NOT that every caller invokes it correctly. Instantiated at the Auto-Key seam (`src/app/animate/autoKeyCommit.ts`): the seam is two functions — `routeAnimatedGrab` (the animated-param GUARD: keys an already-animated param, no-op for an un-animated one) and `autoKeyCommit` (the COMMITTER: also runs `dispatchFirstKeyComposite`, the un-animated "first key"). The NPanel inspector caller invoked BOTH (`setParam` THEN `autoKeyCommit`); the Gizmo caller invoked only `routeAnimatedGrab` + a raw `setParam` — never `autoKeyCommit`. So editing a field recorded an animation; dragging the gizmo recorded nothing.

**Symptom:** a feature has two+ entry surfaces a user reasonably expects to be equivalent (gizmo vs inspector); it works from one and silently does nothing from the other. No error, no failing test (no test drove the broken surface THROUGH the seam). User-visible as "I drag and it snaps right back / nothing records" — the raw write lands but the keyframe the sibling surface would have created never does.

**Trap (wrong fix / false diagnosis):** (a) trust the consolidation — "we lifted it to one chokepoint (D-05), so all callers are covered" — the lift shares the body, not the call sites; (b) diagnose the snap-back as a proxy re-seed / timing bug and add a `setTimeout` or re-seed guard in the gizmo ([[base-layer]] setTimeout-papers-over-ordering anti-pattern — there is no ordering bug); (c) give the broken surface its OWN keyframe path — duplicating the seam, violating the single-path V1/V13 the consolidation existed to enforce.

**Real fix:** make the caller SYMMETRIC — route the broken surface through the SAME chokepoint with the SAME call shape its working sibling uses (inspector = `setParam` THEN `autoKeyCommit` ⇒ gizmo = `setParam` THEN `autoKeyCommit`, one per onObjectChange branch). The new call must be MUTUALLY EXCLUSIVE with the existing animated-path branch so it does not double-fire ([[H36]] anti-double-write): `routeAnimatedGrab` already returned `false`/early-returned on the un-animated fall-through, so the two are disjoint by construction. `autoKeyCommit` self-gates on Auto-Key OFF, so record-off stays byte-identical.

**Detection signal:** a feature has 2+ surfaces that should be equivalent; it works from one and not the other; the working surface's commit handler calls the chokepoint, the broken one calls only a PART of it. Quick discriminator: **grep every caller of the chokepoint and diff their call shape** — a caller that references the GUARD (`routeAnimatedGrab`) but not the COMMITTER (`autoKeyCommit`) is invoking a strict subset = the bug.

**Five-limbed argument:**

1. **Claim:** gizmo drag-to-record created no keyframe because the gizmo caller invoked only `routeAnimatedGrab` (the animated-route guard), never `autoKeyCommit` (the un-animated first-key committer) the inspector caller invokes.
2. **Reason:** `routeAnimatedGrab` returns `false` for an un-animated param and the gizmo stopped at a raw `setParam`; the first-key composite lives in `autoKeyCommit`, which the gizmo never called.
3. **Universal principle:** consolidating a mutation into one chokepoint guarantees the seam's body is shared, NOT that every caller routes through it correctly; a caller invoking a strict subset of the chokepoint's contract is a silent partial wiring.
4. **Application:** add `autoKeyCommit(selectedId, paramPath, value)` after the raw `setParam` in each gizmo onObjectChange branch (translate/rotate/scale, non-GltfChild), mutually exclusive with `routeAnimatedGrab`'s animated early-return.
5. **Conclusion:** drag-to-record now creates the first keyframe exactly like the inspector; the asymmetry is closed and a regression e2e drives the gizmo surface THROUGH the seam.

**Sibling:** [[H36]] (the inverse failure at the SAME seam — double-WRITE; H63 is partial-WRITE; the fix's mutual-exclusivity guard is the proof both concerns coexist at one chokepoint), [[H40]] (boundary-pair: observe both sides → H63 is its mutation-side twin: _wire_ both callers, not just observe both). Shares the consolidation lineage with the `autoKeyCommit` lift (P7.3/D-05, dharana B1.1 line 28). Reinforces dharana **B1.1**.

Provenance: ORIGIN = #141, 2026-06-03 — user reported drag-to-animate with record armed "snaps right back / records nothing"; the inspector path worked, exposing the asymmetry; an e2e (`gizmo-autokey-record.spec.ts`) drove the gizmo through the seam and observed 0 channels (red), then 1 channel / 2 keyframes (green). WHY = without this entry, the next surface added to a shared chokepoint (a future canvas/DAG-editor edit, or the v0.6 unified-mesh-model surfaces that must route every model through the same edit seams) silently wires a subset and the feature works on some surfaces only, invisibly — exactly the failure the unified-model Uniformity gate is meant to prevent. HOW = grep all callers of a chokepoint, diff their call shape vs the canonical caller; a strict-subset caller is the bug; fix by matching the shape + verifying mutual-exclusivity with sibling branches. REF: `src/app/Gizmo.tsx` `onObjectChange` (the three `autoKeyCommit` calls), `src/app/animate/autoKeyCommit.ts` (`routeAnimatedGrab` guard vs `autoKeyCommit` committer), `tests/e2e/gizmo-autokey-record.spec.ts` (the regression gate), [[H36]] [[H40]]. Issue #141, PR #142.

---

### H64 — A capability `isAvailable()` that feature-DETECTS the symbol (not capability-PROBES the call) returns true in a context where the API exists but THROWS, so the fallback chain is never reached and boot dies

**Span:** any `StorageCapability.isAvailable()` (and any capability-selection probe behind `pickStorage` / `core/storage/index.ts`). Instantiated at `src/core/storage/OpfsStorage.ts:isAvailable` (#146): pre-fix it returned `typeof navigator.storage?.getDirectory === 'function'` — a SYMBOL-presence check, never a call.

**Symptom:** boot fails outright with `boot failed: Security error when calling GetDirectory` (surfaced by `App.tsx`). `navigator.storage.getDirectory` EXISTS as a function but CALLING it rejects with a `SecurityError` — opaque origins, sandboxed iframes, blocked site-data, some private-browsing modes. The presence check returns true → `pickStorage` selects `OpfsStorage` → the first real op (`getRoot()` → `getDirectory()`) throws → the IndexedDB→Memory fallback (which would have served) never runs.

**Trap (wrong fix / false green):** "harden" by widening the presence check (also test `navigator.storage`, also test secure-context) — still a presence check, still lies, because presence ≠ permission-to-execute. Or special-case the SecurityError at the call site in `OpfsStorage.getRoot` — patches one op while the WRONG backend stays selected (every other op is still on a dead capability). Or assume localhost is always fine (it is a secure context, yet a sandboxed-iframe/partitioned/private context on localhost STILL throws). The unit env hides it: happy-dom has no `navigator.storage`, so a presence-only check returns false there and "passes" without ever exercising the throwing-but-present shape.

**Real fix:** make the probe test the CAPABILITY, not the symbol — attempt `navigator.storage.getDirectory()` inside try/catch and return the boolean. Keep the presence check ONLY as a fast pre-gate before the call. This mirrors the sibling `IndexedDbStorage.isAvailable` (`src/core/storage/IndexedDbStorage.ts:58-67`), which already opens the DB in try/catch with the comment "private-browsing modes occasionally throw on open" — OPFS had ignored the exact lesson IDB learned. With the real probe, a throwing context reports OPFS unavailable → IDB serves (it survives private/partitioned contexts) → boot succeeds.

**Detection signal:** an `isAvailable()` whose body is a `typeof … === 'function'` / `in` / truthy-property check with NO call into the underlying API; or a capability whose first real method can throw a `SecurityError`/`NotAllowedError`/`QuotaExceededError` that the availability probe cannot have seen. Runtime fingerprint: boot or first-use throws an environment-permission error while a lower-priority fallback capability sits unused.

**Five-limbed argument:**

1. **Claim:** a capability probe at a boundary that can refuse at call time must CALL the operation (try/catch), not just confirm the symbol exists.
2. **Reason:** the symbol's presence is independent of permission to execute it; OPFS `getDirectory` is present-but-throwing in opaque/sandboxed/private contexts, so a presence check mis-selects a dead backend and skips the working fallback.
3. **Universal principle:** feature-detection ≠ capability-detection. When an API can throw on invocation for environmental reasons, only invocation answers "is it available?".
4. **Application:** `OpfsStorage.isAvailable` now `await`s `getDirectory()` in try/catch (presence as pre-gate); `pickStorage` then flows OPFS→IDB→Memory honestly.
5. **Conclusion:** the bug is a probe-semantics bug, not an OPFS bug; the proof is an e2e that overrides `getDirectory` to reject BEFORE boot and observes the app mount anyway (falsified: it fails on the presence-only code, passes on the probe).

**Sibling:** `IndexedDbStorage.isAvailable` is the pre-existing correct instance of this pattern in the SAME module — H64 is a RECURRENCE (OPFS repeated a mistake IDB had already solved), which is exactly the promotion-to-catalogue trigger. Boundary-pair kin of [[H60]] (observe the REAL backend, not the convenient proxy: there MemoryStorage's file map vs OPFS's dir tree; here the unit env's absent `navigator.storage` vs the browser's present-but-throwing one). Shares the [[base-layer]] Grounding check: a presence check is inference ("the symbol is here so it works"); the call is observation.

Provenance: ORIGIN = #146, 2026-06-03 — user opened the dev app and hit `boot failed: Security error when calling GetDirectory`; tracing `pickStorage` showed OPFS selected despite the throwing context because `isAvailable` was presence-only. WHY = without this entry the next capability (Tauri fs in v0.6, or any future storage/permission-gated API) repeats the presence-only probe and "verifies" it in a unit env that can't reproduce the present-but-throwing shape, so the fallback chain silently never engages. HOW = capability-probe (call in try/catch) not feature-detect; falsify with a pre-boot override that makes the call reject. REF: `src/core/storage/OpfsStorage.ts:isAvailable` (the probe), `src/core/storage/IndexedDbStorage.ts:58-67` (the sibling pattern it now mirrors), `src/core/storage/index.ts:pickStorage` (the fallback chain it unblocks), `src/core/storage/storage.test.ts` (#146 probe unit tests: reject/throw/absent→false, resolve→true, pickStorage≠opfs), `tests/e2e/opfs-fallback-boot.spec.ts` (real-symptom: boot survives a rejecting getDirectory — falsified against the old code). Dharana boundary B2. Issue #146.

### H65 — A production code path reaches its data through a DEV-only seam (`import.meta.env.DEV`-gated window getter) → it silently NO-OPS in the production build while every dev test passes

**Span:** any non-React production helper that needs a runtime artifact (a mounted three.js clone, a live render object, a computed scene state) which is currently exposed ONLY through a DEV-gated observation seam (`window.__basher_*` getters guarded by `import.meta.env.DEV`). The seam was built for tests/Lokayata observation, so it is correctly stripped from the production bundle — but if a SHIPPING feature reaches its data through that same getter, the data is `undefined` in prod and the feature silently does nothing. #151 instantiation (the Wave 4 crux): `dispatchApplyTransform`'s glTF-child path needs the mounted SkeletonUtils clone to read the child's resolved geometry + post-override material (`geometryRegistry.get()` returns null for gltf — the bytes live in the loaded asset, not the box/sphere builder). The OBVIOUS reach is `window.__basher_gltf_meshes` / `__basher_gltf_skin` — the existing live-clone accessors. But those are `import.meta.env.DEV`-only: Apply would work in `npm run dev` + every e2e (which run the dev build), then silently no-op for a real director on the production build.

**Symptom:** a feature is green across the entire dev + e2e suite, then does nothing (no error, no toast) in the deployed production build — Apply produces no BakedMesh, the dispatch helper read `undefined.getObjectByName` (optional-chained to null) and returned early. The dev/prod divergence is the tell: e2e cannot catch it because Playwright drives the dev server. A `console.error` would help but the optional-chaining that made the DEV path "safe" is exactly what swallows it.

**Trap (the wrong fix):** reach through the DEV seam anyway "because it already exists and works in my testing" (Chesterton misread — the seam exists for OBSERVATION, its DEV gate is load-bearing, not incidental). A second wrong fix: drop the DEV gate on `__basher_gltf_meshes` so the production path can use it — that ships a debug surface (and its global-window pollution + perf walk) to every user.

**Real fix:** a SEPARATE, production-safe accessor for the production need — `src/app/asset/gltfCloneRegistry.ts`: a module-level `Map<assetRef, Group>` that `GltfAssetR` registers on mount / unregisters on unmount (newest-mount-wins, matching the single-asset-per-ref assumption the DEV seams already make). It MIRRORS the live-clone access pattern of the DEV getters but is ALWAYS ON (not `import.meta.env.DEV`). The capture then reads the RESOLVED, POST-override render state directly off the registered clone (bake-what-renders, no parallel re-resolution — [[H40]]/[[H58]]/[[H59]]).

**Detection signal:** a production (non-test) module imports or references a `window.__basher_*` getter, OR reaches data only available behind one. Ask: "is this seam DEV-gated? Does my feature SHIP? If both, my prod build has `undefined` here." Grep `src/` (excluding tests/`*.test.*`) for `__basher_` references in shipping code paths.

### H66 — A multi-step "create-then-use" composite mints its product with a DETERMINISTIC id and ALWAYS runs the create step — so calling it twice for the same target collides; it silently assumes "first call ever"

**Span:** any dispatch composite that derives a deterministic node/resource id from its target (`${target}_layer`, `${target}_<x>_channel`, `${asset}_group`) and unconditionally runs an `addNode`-style CREATE for that id before the USE step. It works for the FIRST call (the id is free) and breaks on the SECOND call for the SAME target — the create collides (`addNode: id already exists`) OR the underlying Mutator only reuses-vs-rejects on a narrow case (e.g. `addLayer` rejects wrapping-a-wrapper but NEVER reuses an existing wrapper). The bug is latent for as long as the composite is only ever called once per target. #149 instantiation: `dispatchFirstKeyComposite` (`src/app/animate/dispatchMutator.ts`) always ran `addLayer` with `${targetId}_layer`. The single-param diamond / "Animate this" only ever keyed ONE band per target, so it never recurred — until the #149 whole-transform `K` keyed position+rotation+scale in one tick: position (animated → keyframe path, no addLayer) succeeded, rotation (first un-animated → addLayer `n_box_layer`, NEW) succeeded, scale (second un-animated → addLayer `n_box_layer` AGAIN) → collision → scale silently dropped. Observed: `K` keyed `["position","rotation"]`, scale missing.

**Symptom:** the Nth (N≥2) invocation for the same target silently no-ops or drops part of its work, while the 1st invocation and every single-invocation test pass. The composite's own unit suite (which keys ONE param) stays green — the gap only appears when a NEW caller batches multiple invocations against one target, or a user keys a 2nd band on an already-animated object.

**Trap (the wrong fix):** make the new caller key only ONE band (narrow the feature to dodge the collision) — that abandons the locked "whole transform" behavior and leaves the latent bug for the next caller. Second wrong fix: catch-and-ignore the addLayer rejection — the channel then has no layer to attach to.

**Real fix:** the composite DETECTS the existing product and REUSES it instead of always creating. `dispatchFirstKeyComposite` now scans for an `AnimationLayer` already wrapping the target (normalize `inputs.target` like `resolveEvaluatedTransform`); if found, SKIP `addLayer` (empty layer ops/closure/label) and `addChannel` into the existing layer (validated against base); else mint `${target}_layer` as before. One layer per target — the create step becomes create-or-reuse. This fixes the #149 caller AND the latent "key a 2nd band on any object" bug. REF: `src/app/animate/dispatchMutator.ts` (`dispatchFirstKeyComposite` existing-layer detection), `src/app/animate/dispatchMutator.test.ts` (11/11), `tests/e2e/p149-commit.spec.ts` (`K` keys all 3 bands, persists). Cross-ref [[H34]] (the layer-wrap rewire this rides on), [[V31]] (the transient the commit captures). Issue #149.

**Detection signal:** a composite/dispatch helper computes a deterministic id from its target and the FIRST step is an unconditional CREATE. Ask: "what happens if this runs twice for the same target?" If the answer is "collision / silent drop" and a caller exists (or is being added) that batches invocations, it needs create-or-reuse.

**Five-limbed argument:**

1. **Claim:** a shipping feature that reaches its runtime data through a `import.meta.env.DEV`-gated seam silently no-ops in production while passing every dev test.
2. **Reason:** the DEV gate strips the getter from the production bundle (by design — it is an observation seam), so the production code reads `undefined`; optional chaining (added to make the DEV path "safe") converts the missing data into a silent early-return rather than a throw.
3. **Universal principle:** a debug/observation seam and a production data path are different concerns; a production need must be met by a production-safe surface, never by a development-only one.
4. **Application:** `gltfCloneRegistry` is an always-on module-level accessor populated by `GltfAssetR` mount/unmount, mirroring the DEV getters' access pattern without their DEV gate; `dispatchApplyTransform` reads the clone from it.
5. **Conclusion:** the structural defense is one production-safe accessor per production need + a grep gate that no shipping path references a `__basher_*` DEV getter; reaching through the DEV seam is the silent-prod-no-op class.

**Cross-ref:** [[H58]] (the sibling class — an e2e green while the feature is unreachable BY USERS; H65 is the build-time twin: green while unreachable IN PRODUCTION), [[H64]] (capability-probe vs feature-detect — same "the thing exists in my context but not the real one" family), [[H45]]/[[H59]] (the clone boundary the registry serves — read-only, clone-before-mutate), [[V20]] (single-writer — the registry is the one production accessor). Provenance: ORIGIN = #151 Wave 4, 2026-06-04 — the crux brief weighed reaching through `__basher_gltf_meshes` (DEV-only) and recognised it would make Apply a silent prod no-op; the registry was built to avoid it. WHY = without this entry the next production feature needing live three.js data (a future export, a snapshot, a bake variant) reaches through the convenient DEV seam and ships a silent-no-op that no e2e catches. HOW = a production-safe accessor mirroring the DEV seam's access pattern minus the DEV gate; grep that shipping code never references `__basher_*`. REF: `src/app/asset/gltfCloneRegistry.ts` (the production-safe accessor + the comment naming this exact trap), `src/viewport/SceneFromDAG.tsx` GltfAssetR (the populator + the mirrored DEV seams `__basher_gltf_meshes`/`__basher_gltf_skin`), `src/app/animate/dispatchApplyTransform.ts` (the consumer), `tests/e2e/p151-gltf-child-apply.spec.ts` (the real-render proof), dharana boundary `gltfCloneRegistry`. Issue #151.

### H73 — `git checkout/restore <file>` to undo a falsification edit NUKES all uncommitted wave work in that file (not just the falsification line)

**Span:** any "observe-then-revert" falsification loop (H40 discipline) where the file under test ALSO carries uncommitted wave changes. The falsification is a deliberate temporary break ("does the e2e go RED if I sabotage X?"); the revert is meant to restore ONLY that break. `git checkout <file>` / `git restore <file>` reverts the file to **HEAD** (the last commit) — so every uncommitted edit vanishes, not just the falsification. v0.6 #2 instantiation (W2): falsified `usePrimitiveMaterial` by perl-editing `m.roughness` out, ran the e2e (correctly RED), then `git checkout src/viewport/SceneFromDAG.tsx` to "undo" — which wiped the ENTIRE W2 renderer consolidation (the usePrimitiveMaterial hook, the Box/SphereR rewrite, the seam extensions, the import) back to W1. Had to re-apply all of W2.

**Symptom:** after a falsify→revert cycle the wave's feature is silently gone; `git status` shows the file clean (== HEAD) when you expected your wave's diff.

**Trap (the wrong fix):** re-do the work AND keep the same falsify-via-checkout loop — it nukes the NEXT wave too.

**Real fix (TWO-PART):** (1) **commit the wave BEFORE falsifying.** Then `git restore <file>` reverts only to the just-committed wave state — SAFE (the falsification is the only uncommitted change). This made every later falsification (W3/W4/W5) safe: commit → falsify → observe RED → `git restore` → back to the committed wave. (2) If you must falsify pre-commit, undo with a TARGETED reverse-edit (re-apply the exact line), never a whole-file checkout.

**Detection signal:** about to run `git checkout/restore <file>` while that file has uncommitted work to keep. Ask: "is this file == HEAD plus ONLY my falsification edit?" Commit-first removes the hazard.

**Cross-ref:** [[H40]] (the falsification discipline this serves), the AnviDev atomic-commit rule (commit-before-falsify = atomic commits applied to the observe loop). Provenance: ORIGIN = v0.6 #2 W2, 2026-06-07 — falsified leaf-material roughness, used `git checkout`, lost the whole W2 SceneFromDAG consolidation. WHY = the next falsification on a file with uncommitted wave work silently deletes the wave and `git status` looks "clean". HOW = commit-before-falsify makes `git restore` precise. REF: this session's W2-W5 commits (each committed before falsifying), [[H40]].

### H74 — A paramPath rename's consumer span includes the AGENT layer (write + identify + LLM prompt) + the e2e corpus + sibling renderers — far beyond the "evaluator + N renderers" the V10/H14 guard enumerates

**Span:** any rename/move of a `setParam` paramPath an established convention uses (`material.color`, `position`, …). The V10/H14 guard enumerates the SCHEMA consumers (zod default + migration + evaluator + the EvaluatedMesh resolver + leaf renderers). But a paramPath is ALSO a string spoken by: (a) **agent mutators that WRITE it** (`setMaterialColor`, `randomize` emit `paramPath: '...'`) — after a rename zod STRIPS the now-unknown key, so the agent op silently no-ops; (b) **agent identify/read** (`identify.ts`); (c) **the LLM-facing docs** (`orchestrator.ts` prompt + `strategy/catalog.ts` table) that TEACH the path to the model; (d) the **e2e corpus** (channels/transients seeded at the old path — p149 animated `material.color`); (e) **sibling render consumers** the schema-walk misses (`DiffOverlay`, the Apply-bake `bakedSpecFromInline`). v0.6 #2 (W1): widening `material.color → material.base.color` touched all five — the plan's "5-consumer span" enumerated only (e)-partial; the agent layer + e2e were found by grep.

**Symptom:** unit tests green (schema consumers updated) but an agent "make it red" silently no-ops, identify-by-colour stops matching, an existing e2e animating the old path renders the static value, a DiffOverlay/bake reads `undefined`. The break is OUTSIDE the wave's own tests.

**Trap (the wrong fix):** update only the schema-walk consumers and call it done — leaves the agent write/read/teach path + e2e on the dead paramPath.

**Real fix:** before renaming a paramPath, `grep -rn '<old.path>'` across ALL of `src/` AND `tests/` AND the LLM doc strings, and update every WRITE site (mutators), READ site (identify), DOC site (orchestrator/catalog — the model emits what you teach), e2e seed, and sibling renderer. The grep is the span; the schema list is a subset.

**Detection signal:** moving/renaming a paramPath. Ask: "who WRITES it (mutators)? READS it (identify)? TEACHES it (LLM prompt/catalog)? SEEDS it (e2e)? which renderers besides the leaf read it?" A paramPath is a cross-layer vocabulary, not just a schema field.

**Cross-ref:** [[V10]]/[[H14]] (the schema-consumer guard this is a SUPERSET of), [[V28]] (the override/agent paramPath convention), dharana B19. Provenance: ORIGIN = v0.6 #2 W1, 2026-06-07 — the plan's B-1 span for `material.color→material.base.color` omitted the agent write/identify/LLM-prompt sites + DiffOverlay + dispatchApplyTransform + p149; all found by grep, all required for green. WHY = the next paramPath rename ships an agent layer / LLM prompt / e2e on a dead path, hidden outside the renaming wave's tests. HOW = grep all of src+tests+doc-strings for the old path first; write/read/teach/seed/sibling are the real span. REF: `src/agent/mutators/builders/{setMaterialColor,randomize}.ts`, `src/agent/identify/identify.ts`, `src/agent/{orchestrator,strategy/catalog}.ts`, `src/viewport/DiffOverlay.tsx`, `src/app/animate/dispatchApplyTransform.ts`, `tests/e2e/p149-transient-boundary-pair.spec.ts`, commit `6b43dda`. Issue #178.

### H75 — A conditional-render chrome control that hides when its visibility precondition lapses can STRAND a persisted value it owns, with no affordance to reset it

**Span:** any inspector/chrome control that (a) is rendered only when a precondition holds (`if (cond) return null`) AND (b) writes a PERSISTED optional param. When the precondition later lapses while the value is still set, the control vanishes but the value remains — and because the control was the only way to change it, the value is stranded. v0.6 #2 W6 instance: `SlotSelector` (`src/app/NPanel.tsx`) rendered only when the target glTF has ≥2 material slots (`if (slotCount < 2) return null`); a stale `slotIndex` (e.g. the asset later dropped below 2 slots, or was swapped) then matches NO render slot → the `MaterialOverride` silently tints nothing AND the selector is gone, so the director cannot click "All" to recover. Found in the 2nd self-review pass, not by a failing test (the e2e fixtures always have ≥2 slots).

**Symptom:** a feature "stops working" with no error — the persisted value is non-default but the surface that would explain/reset it is absent. The renderer is CORRECT (range-safe no-op); the gap is purely the missing recovery affordance. Invisible to tests whose fixtures keep the precondition true.

**Trap (the wrong fix):** "the renderer already handles out-of-range safely (no-op), so we're done" — true for correctness, false for usability: a silent no-op the user can't undo is a worse failure than a visible error.

**Real fix:** render the control when `precondition OR value-is-set` — i.e. `if (slotCount < 2 && current === undefined) return null;`. A set value ALWAYS keeps its reset affordance reachable (here: the "All" button clears `slotIndex` back to whole-child). General rule: a conditional-render control that owns a persisted value must stay visible whenever that value is non-default, independent of the precondition that first revealed it.

**Detection signal:** any `if (<precondition>) return null` in a component that ALSO dispatches `setParam`/persists state. Ask: "if the precondition becomes false while the value is set, can the user still reset it?" If no → widen the render guard to `precondition || value-is-set`.

**Cross-ref:** [[H40]] (observe the real persisted state, not the happy-path UI), dharana [[B19]]. Provenance: ORIGIN = v0.6 #2 W6, 2026-06-07 — 2nd critical self-review pass on the SlotSelector diff (the first pass filed #179; this gap was a separate, fixable footgun). WHY = without this entry the next conditional-render control over a persisted optional param ships the same strand-with-no-reset, invisible to fixtures that hold the precondition true. HOW = guard on `precondition || value-set`; one cheap observation (set the value, lapse the precondition, confirm a reset is still reachable). REF: `src/app/NPanel.tsx` (`SlotSelector` guard `slotCount < 2 && current === undefined`), `src/app/resolveOverrideSlots.ts` (`countOverrideSlots`), commit `f86927a`. Issue #178.

### H76 — Mutating a per-renderer property on a SHARED, content-cached resource (a Texture cached by hash) cross-contaminates every other consumer; CLONE before mutating

**Span:** any place that reads a resource from a content-addressed/instance cache and then sets a PER-CONSUMER property on it. v0.6 #3 W2 instance: `useBakedTexture` returns ONE `THREE.Texture` per OPFS hash (`bakedTextureLoader.ts` `textureCache`) — the same instance is handed to EVERY material using that image. Setting the material-specific `uvTransform` (`texture.repeat`/`.offset`/`.rotation`) directly on that shared instance silently changes the mapping of every OTHER material pointing at the same image. (The pre-#3 code already shared the instance, but only ever set `.colorSpace` — identical across consumers — so the bug was latent until a per-material property arrived.)

**Symptom:** edit one mesh's tiling → a DIFFERENT mesh's texture tiling jumps too. Invisible to any single-mesh test; only a two-consumers-share-one-hash fixture reveals it.

**Trap (the wrong fix):** "the texture loader already caches/dedupes by hash, so just assign it" — correct for the IMAGE bytes (share those), wrong for the transform STATE (must be per-consumer). Conflating "share the expensive image" with "share the whole Texture object" is the error.

**Real fix:** `const c = tex.clone()` per material before applying the per-consumer properties; `clone()` shares the underlying `.source`/image (cheap — no re-decode) but gives independent `repeat/offset/rotation/center/colorSpace`. The single writer that creates the clone OWNS its disposal (`Material.dispose()` does NOT free textures — dispose the clones alongside the material). Mirrors the standard three.js KHR_texture_transform pattern.

**Detection signal:** a value read from a `Map`/cache keyed by content/hash, then a `.someProp = ...` / `.set(...)` on it that varies per call site. Ask: "do two consumers with the same key need DIFFERENT values here?" If yes → clone first.

**Cross-ref:** [[V20]]/[[H36]] (single writer owns the material AND its cloned-texture lifecycle), [[H45]] (clone-before-mutate — the sibling for glTF scene clones / Object3D), [[V30]] (the content-hash texture cache this reads from), dharana [[B19]]. Provenance: ORIGIN = v0.6 #3 W2, 2026-06-07 — caught at DESIGN time (CONTEXT A-5), not by a failing fix, because the shared-cache structure made the contamination foreseeable; proven by the p06-3 SC-3 two-boxes-one-image e2e ([4,1] vs [7,7] stay independent). WHY = without this entry the next per-consumer property on a shared cached resource (a per-material wrap mode, a per-instance anisotropy) re-discovers the cross-contamination one support ticket at a time. HOW = clone before mutate; observation = two consumers same hash, different values, assert independent. REF: `src/viewport/SceneFromDAG.tsx` (`usePrimitiveMaterial` `prep()` clone + `userData.__uvClones` disposal), `src/app/asset/bakedTextureLoader.ts` (the shared `textureCache`), `tests/e2e/p06-3-texture-placement.spec.ts` (SC-3), commit `02d1668`. Issue #181.

### H77 — A substrate LEAK: an expedient shortcut keeps domain state OUTSIDE the one DAG/Op/IR (a side-channel, a live stochastic call, a bolted-on "advanced" UI, an Op-set explosion) → it works in isolation but silently drops out of undo / replay / multiplayer / agent-authoring / determinism

**Span:** any NEW domain, feature, AI/generative node, cache/store, or "advanced/Pro" UI surface added on top of the substrate ([[V34]]). The leak is INVISIBLE in a single-feature test; it surfaces only when a CROSS-domain operation runs — undo the new thing, the agent drives it, reload/replay it, two users edit it, the data-flywheel tries to learn it.

**Symptom:** the feature works when used alone, but one of: undo of it no-ops or corrupts; the agent can't author it (only chat/old surfaces can); reload/replay produces a DIFFERENT result; multiplayer diverges; a generated output won't reproduce. "It works in this one panel / on my machine."

**Trap (the wrong fix):** "just store it here / cache it locally / add a quick separate panel for the power-user / call the model live — it's faster, simpler, and isolated." Isolation is EXACTLY the leak: state the Op system doesn't own can't be undone/replayed/agent-driven, and superlinearity ([[V34]], `docs/PLATFORM-VISION.md` §9.3) silently downgrades from N×1 back to N×N for everything that touches it.

**Real fix:** route the datum through an Op on the DAG (no authoritative state outside the IR, §18/§50); for a stochastic/AI output PIN the seed + CONTENT-HASH the result as an asset so the GRAPH is reproducible though the model isn't (the [[V30]] pattern); keep "advanced" as the SAME projected graph revealed (projection §59a + progressive disclosure §17a), never a second UI; keep the Op vocabulary small (a new domain REUSES Ops).

**Detection signal (ask at design + at every Write to a leak-prone seam):** (1) state assigned to a module/store/object the Op system doesn't own; (2) a `Math.random`/model/API output referenced as if stable across reloads; (3) a component branch keyed on "mode/advanced/pro" that renders a DIFFERENT control set rather than MORE of the projection; (4) a PR minting many new Op types for one domain; (5) hand-authored inspector/UI where the node schema could project it (the `MATERIAL_LOBES` tell). The one question: **"if I undo / reload / let the agent drive / add a 2nd user — does THIS still hold?"** If no → it is a leak; route through the substrate before shipping.

**Cross-ref:** [[V34]] (the invariant this violates — faces [[V20]]/[[V29]]/[[V30]]/[[V32]]/[[V33]]), [[H76]] (shared-cache per-consumer-state sibling leak), [[H65]] (DEV-only-seam silent-noop sibling), dharana [[B-substrate-purity]] (the seams + the leak-check, injected contextually by the hook). Provenance: ORIGIN = north-star consolidation 2026-06-08 (`docs/PLATFORM-VISION.md` §9.4) — promoted as a FORWARD guard (single articulation, not yet a recurring fix) because the superlinearity thesis makes the leak-class foreseeable and high-cost; the `MATERIAL_LOBES` sections are the already-present early tell. WHY = each leak silently converts the platform's N×1 advantage back to N×N for the leaked domain; without this catalogued, every new domain re-discovers it one regression at a time. HOW = the detection-signal question, run at design + on every Write to a [[B-substrate-purity]] seam. REF: `docs/PLATFORM-VISION.md` §9.3/§9.4; THESIS §50 (Op = only mutation) / §48–51 (determinism) / §18 (agent = privileged) / §59a (projection) / §17a (progressive disclosure).

### H78 — A SCOPE PREMISE inherited from a handoff / memory / prior plan is STALE at the source: you plan AROUND "X works like Y" or "X doesn't exist yet" without re-reading the code → the whole wave is built on a false assumption, surfacing only when a test exercises the deleted/renamed/already-existing thing

**Span:** any planning / discuss / scoping step that consumes a handoff, a memory file, a prior-session decision, or an upstream doc as its premise — ESPECIALLY a multi-session feature where the codebase moved under the notes. The error is in the FRAMING, so it propagates into every downstream wave/task/sub-agent prompt built on it.

**Symptom:** the plan names a thing to build/remove/change that, at the source, is already gone, already built, or shaped differently than the note says. Invisible until execution hits the file and finds the assumption false (a deleted enum, an existing CRUD surface, a renamed field). Twin tells from v0.6 #4: "the doc says we'll remove Simple/Director/Pro" (already removed — `modeStore.ts:23` holds operational modes) and "we should build a demo + picker" (project CRUD + ProjectsMenu/ProjectTabs already shipped).

**Trap (the wrong fix):** trust the handoff because it's recent and detailed, hardcode its premise into the issue + the plan + the sub-agent prompts, and discover the drift two waves later. Detail and recency make a stale premise MORE convincing, not less.

**Real fix:** before planning AROUND any inherited premise, VERIFY it at the source — grep/read the actual code for the capability or structure the premise asserts (or denies). One `Explore`/grep pass per load-bearing premise. Treat "X doesn't exist" as a claim to FALSIFY (it often half-exists), and "X works like Y" as a hypothesis to CONFIRM at `file:line`. Correct the upstream doc immediately so the false premise doesn't re-enter next session.

**Detection signal:** the plan asserts the presence/absence/shape of an existing system WITHOUT a `file:line` citation for that assertion; a premise repeated verbatim from a handoff into N sub-agent prompts; "as the memory says…" standing in for "as the code shows…". The one question: **"have I read the SOURCE for this premise this session, or am I trusting the note?"**

**Cross-ref:** [[H25]] (decision locked from stale memory at authoring — the recurrence sibling), [[H27]] (re-validation-cycle drift), memory `feedback_verify_own_framing` (the orchestrator's own premise propagated to sub-agents — the originating single occurrence). Provenance: ORIGIN = v0.6 #4 planning, 2026-06-08 — RECURRED TWICE in one session (the audit found Simple/Director/Pro already removed → operational modes; the workspace exploration found multi-project CRUD already production-ready → the planned "demo + picker" was half-redundant). Single occurrence was `feedback_verify_own_framing`; two more instances → promoted to hetvabhasa. WHY = a stale premise is the cheapest bug to catch (one grep) and the most expensive to miss (an entire wave built wrong, discovered at execution); without this catalogued, every multi-session feature re-learns it. HOW = verify each load-bearing premise at the source before it enters the plan; cite `file:line` for presence/absence claims. REF: `docs/UI-REVIEW.md` (caught premise #1, `modeStore.ts:3-16,23,55-59`), the project-management exploration (premise #2, `boot.ts:561-653` + `ProjectsMenu.tsx` + `io.ts`), `.planning/phases/v06.4-director-ux/CONTEXT.md` (D-05 amended, D-08 revised).

---

### H79 — Removing a SHARED enabling-state (a mode, a flag) has a test-corpus blast radius WIDER than the plan enumerates, AND a blanket find-replace across that corpus breaks wherever the old token meant something DIFFERENT from its replacement — because one removed datum carried multiple behaviors that the test setups conflated

**Span:** any wave that deletes a piece of shared UI/app state (an enum, a global mode, a feature flag) that the TEST corpus uses as a SETUP convenience — `selectOption('animate')`, `setMode('x')`, a `data-mode` attr — across many specs the planner never opened. The error has two stages: (1) the plan's "files to update" list undercounts the span (a grep finds 2-3× more); (2) the fix-by-substitution then mis-fires wherever the removed token bundled ≥2 behaviors that the new code SPLITS.

**Symptom:** stage 1 — typecheck/prod is green but a swathe of e2e fail at the OLD token (gone testid/attr). Stage 2 — after a mechanical `old→new` substitution, a NEW cluster fails because the substitution did the wrong thing in some specs: e.g. v0.6 #4 `mode='animate'` meant BOTH "reveal the timeline slot" AND "enable keyframe ops"; the new design splits these (slot always-mounted; keyframes gate on drawer-OPEN). Specs that used `selectOption('animate')` as a slot-reveal AND separately toggled the drawer now DOUBLE-TOGGLE (open→close) → "toolbar hidden" failures, indistinguishable at a glance from a real regression.

**Trap (the wrong fix):** (a) trust the plan's file list and skip the grep → discover the extra specs only when the suite runs (slow, late). (b) Worse: write ONE `sed`/`python` blanket replacement over all hits → it's right for the single-behavior specs and WRONG for the multi-behavior ones, converting a clean "N broken" into a confusing "M differently-broken," and you can't tell the substitution-induced failures from genuine regressions without reading each spec's setup.

**Real fix:** (1) Before the wave, `grep -rn` the EXACT old token across `tests/` — that count, not the plan's, is the true span (v0.6 #4: plan listed ~6, grep found 18). (2) Classify the hits by INTENT before substituting: what did the old token actually DO in THIS spec, and does the new code preserve that as one action or split it? Single-behavior + 1 downstream toggle → straight substitute. Multi-behavior OR the spec already drives the split-out affordance → DELETE the now-redundant setup line, don't substitute (the always-on surface needs no reveal step). (3) Run the converted cluster as its own batch and read each NEW failure against the spec's setup — confirm it's substitution-shaped, not a real regression, before moving on.

**Detection signal:** a state-removal plan whose "update these specs" list was written from memory/the surface map, not a fresh `grep tests/`; a single bulk find-replace touching >5 spec files; a post-substitution failure cluster where the assertion is about a DIFFERENT surface than the token you replaced (toolbar hidden when you changed a timeline reveal = the double-toggle tell). The one question: **"did this old token do ONE thing here, or did it bundle the reveal AND the enable — and does my replacement preserve the right one?"**

**Cross-ref:** [[H74]] (a rename's consumer span includes layers beyond the obvious — the SIBLING of this; H74 = identifier span, H79 = behavioral-token span + the substitution hazard), [[H27]] (same-wave test update is mandatory — H79 is what goes WRONG when you do the same-wave update mechanically), [[H73]] (commit-before-falsify — the commit boundary is what lets you `git restore` after probing a substitution-shaped failure). Provenance: ORIGIN = v0.6 #4 W2 execution, 2026-06-08 — the mode enum's `selectOption('animate')` lived in 18 specs (plan listed ~6); a blanket `animate→timeline-drawer-toggle.click()` sub broke the multi-toggle specs (p3/p6-w5/w6/w9/p7-animation/p7.12) by double-toggling, because old-animate bundled slot-reveal + keyframe-enable which v0.6 #4 splits. Single occurrence → memory-then-promote; promoted now because the blast-radius half already recurred within the same wave (data-mode in 4 specs, mode-badge in 2, mode-switcher in 18 — three separate undercounts in one task). WHY = a state-removal is a recurring milestone shape (modes, flags, density axes all get removed); without this, every removal re-discovers the undercount AND re-makes the blanket-substitution mistake, turning a 1-pass test update into a 3-pass debug. HOW = grep-for-true-span + classify-by-intent-before-substitute + run-the-cluster-and-read-each-new-failure. REF: `tests/e2e/p6-w2-no-modes.spec.ts` (the falsifiable proof the split works), the 18 converted specs, W2 commit `b5af221`, `.planning/phases/v06.4-director-ux/PLAN.md` W2-T11 (the under-counted list).

### H80 — Reclaiming viewport/screen space by COLLAPSING an always-visible bar hides a load-bearing indicator the bar was silently HOSTING — the space is not disposable chrome, it is the only home of a safety/status surface, and hiding it re-opens the exact failure that surface existed to prevent

**Span:** any "calm UI / reclaim N px" move that hides a persistently-visible container (a status bar, a transport strip, a toolbar) to free viewport area. The trap is the inference "this bar is just chrome → collapse it when idle" made WITHOUT enumerating what the bar hosts. A bar that looks like passive chrome can carry an always-on indicator whose entire design contract is "unmissable / global" — e.g. a record/Auto-Key armed light, a dirty-state marker, a connection-status dot, an unsaved-changes warning.

**Symptom:** the space-reclaim works and looks cleaner, BUT a cluster of tests that assert the hosted indicator is VISIBLE (`expect(indicator).toBeVisible()`, `data-autokey=on` reachable) fail — not because the indicator logic broke, but because its container is now `display:none` when "idle." The failures point at a DIFFERENT subsystem (auto-key / save-state) than the layout change, so they read as unrelated regressions until you trace the indicator's DOM home back to the collapsed container.

**Trap (the wrong fix):** (a) "the tests are stale — the bar is hidden now, update them to expect hidden" → this SILENCES the footgun: the indicator existed precisely so the user never misses the armed/dirty state; hiding it for space is the regression, not the test. (b) Add a workaround (a second mini-indicator elsewhere, a tooltip) → a parallel surface for state that already has a home (duplication, the thing consolidation was eliminating).

**Real fix:** Chesterton — before collapsing an always-visible container, ENUMERATE what it hosts (grep its component for indicators/`data-*`/aria-live). If it carries a surface whose contract is always-visible (safety/footgun/status), the space is LOAD-BEARING: do not collapse it. If reclaiming the space is still wanted, RELOCATE the indicator to a surviving always-visible surface FIRST (its own task), then collapse. The reveal/convenience affordance (e.g. a pill toggle for the drawer body) can still be added — it just must not be the indicator's only home.

**Detection signal:** a layout change justified by "reclaim ~N px / calmer" that flips a persistent container to conditional `display`; a test failure cluster whose assertions name a status/record/dirty indicator rather than the layout; the question to ask BEFORE the collapse: **"what does this bar HOST that the user must see at all times — and would hiding it re-open a footgun?"** If you can't answer without opening the component, you haven't earned the collapse.

**Cross-ref:** [[V35]] (sibling — V35 keeps a REVEAL affordance reachable while a body collapses; H80 keeps a SAFETY indicator reachable, i.e. some hosted surfaces forbid the collapse entirely, not just relocate the toggle), Existence Check / Chesterton's fence (understand WHY the bar is always visible before hiding it), [[H77]]/[[V34]] (the no-second-UI discipline — the wrong fix's "mini-indicator elsewhere" is a duplication leak). Provenance: ORIGIN = v0.6 #4 W1 execution, 2026-06-08 — the carry-over plan said "collapse the timeline slot when the drawer is closed to reclaim ~39px"; observation (5 failing p7-animation-authoring autokey specs) showed the always-visible Timebar hosts the Auto-Key record indicator (`autokey-dot`/`autokey-toggle`), a footgun mitigation designed to be unmissable. Collapsing the slot hid it → reverted the collapse, kept the pill reveal. Single occurrence → would normally be memory; promoted because it is a named UX-pattern trap (calm/reclaim is a recurring milestone driver) and the wrong fix actively re-opens a safety hole. WHY = "make it calmer / reclaim space" is a standing director-UX pressure across this milestone; without this entry every such move re-risks hiding a hosted safety surface. HOW = enumerate-what-the-bar-hosts + relocate-before-collapse, never silence-the-test. REF: `src/app/Layout.tsx` (timeline slot kept always-visible), `src/timeline/TimelineDrawer.tsx` (Timebar + Auto-Key indicator), `tests/e2e/p7-animation-authoring.spec.ts` (the autokey specs that caught it), W1 commit `bda0cac` (the DEVIATION note).

---

### H81 — Code AFTER a shared, MANDATORY tail-setup block (test seams, subscriptions, registrations) must run on EVERY branch; an early `return` added upstream silently STRANDS that setup on its path

**Root cause:** a long init function ends with a block every consumer depends on — in `boot()`, the `if (import.meta.env.DEV) { window.__basher_* = … }` seam block + the dirty-tracking subscription. A new feature adds branches earlier in the function (W4 first-run routing) and reaches for the natural-looking `return` to short-circuit the home path. The early `return` skips everything below it — so on the home route the `__basher_*` e2e seams are never installed and the WHOLE editor e2e suite breaks the moment it touches one (and worse, since `boot()` is promise-cached, opening a project from the home never re-runs boot, so the seams stay stranded for the session).

**Detection signal:** an `if (…) { … ; return; }` inserted ABOVE a block that does global registration / window-seam install / store subscription; an e2e failure that isn't "wrong value" but "`window.__basher_*` is undefined" / "seam missing" on one route only; a function whose tail was always-reached and is now conditionally reached.

**The trap:** model the new branch as "this path is done, return early" — clean-looking, and the happy (resume/editor) path still runs the tail so local testing of THAT path passes. The stranded path only breaks when a test (or a later user action) exercises it.

**The real fix:** when a function has mandatory tail setup, branch with `if/else` (or set a result variable) so execution FALLS THROUGH to the tail on every path; never early-`return` above shared setup. If the tail genuinely must be skipped on some path, lift it ABOVE the branch.

**Cross-ref:** [[H65]] (a shipping path reading a DEV-only `__basher_*` getter → undefined in prod — sibling: both are "the seam isn't there when read"), Sequence/krama base check (tail order is load-bearing). Provenance: ORIGIN = v0.6 #4 W4 execution, 2026-06-09 — the first-run/stale `return`s in `boot.ts` sat above the `if (import.meta.env.DEV)` seam block; caught by reasoning before run (would have stranded `__basher_dag` on the home route). Rewrote the routing to if/else falling through to the seams. Single occurrence → promoted because it is a structural trap any future boot/init branch can re-trigger and its blast radius is the entire e2e harness. WHY = boot's tail installs the contract every spec depends on; an early return there is invisible until a route is exercised. HOW = if/else with fall-through, never early-return above mandatory tail setup. REF: `src/app/boot.ts` (the W4 if/else routing + the `installDirtyTracking()` + DEV seam block below it), W4 commit `ff374ec`.

---

### H82 — Changing a BOOT-RESOLUTION DEFAULT (what `/` opens) inverts an IMPLICIT contract the entire test harness silently relied on; re-establish it ONCE at the fixture, CONDITIONALLY, not per-spec

**Root cause:** every e2e spec does `page.goto('/')` and assumes the editor loads — an implicit contract guaranteed by the OLD boot resolving `lastId ?? DEFAULT_PROJECT_ID` (always an editor on a clean store). A new feature changes that default (first-run with no `lastProjectId` → HOME). Now a CLEAN CI store (fresh per test) lands on the home, and ~50 editor specs fail at once — not because their assertions are wrong, but because their unstated precondition ("`/` is the editor") was silently revoked.

**Detection signal:** a routing/boot-default change where the new entry state differs from what tests assume; a mass e2e failure cluster across UNRELATED specs all failing at the FIRST assertion (`layout`/`viewport` not visible); the realization "the suite never SET up a project — it depended on boot creating one."

**The trap:** fix it per-spec (add setup to each failing test), or detect first-run by storage-emptiness (which examples-seeding defeats). Both are wrong: per-spec is ~50 edits + drift; storage-emptiness couples first-run to an unrelated signal.

**The real fix:** re-establish the implicit contract at the SINGLE harness chokepoint — the shared fixture (`_fixtures.ts` `page` fixture) registers an `addInitScript` seeding the resume target (`lastProjectId='default'`). Make it CONDITIONAL (set only when ABSENT) so a spec that creates/switches projects and then RELOADS still resumes ITS project — an unconditional set would clobber the persisted value on every navigation and silently break reload-resume tests. The new-surface spec overrides per-test (init scripts run in registration order; the spec's later script wins). Keep the boot first-run detector on the ORIGINAL signal (key absence), guarded so it doesn't self-persist (see [[H78]] sibling / the `:137` persist-on-boot trap).

**Cross-ref:** [[H79]] (state-removal test-corpus blast radius — sibling: both are "one change ripples across the whole spec corpus"; H79 = a removed datum's assertions go stale, H82 = a changed default revokes an unstated precondition), [[H78]] (the persist-on-boot one-shot-signal trap that the first-run path must guard), [[H73]] (commit-before-falsify). Provenance: ORIGIN = v0.6 #4 W4 execution, 2026-06-09 — first-run→home would have broken every editor spec; fixed with the conditional `_fixtures.ts` init seed (proven: p26 12/12 + p6-w8 8/8 still resume the editor). WHY = the whole e2e harness encodes "`/` = editor" implicitly; any boot-default change must re-establish it centrally. HOW = conditional fixture init seed (only-when-absent preserves reload-resume), per-test override for the new surface. REF: `tests/e2e/_fixtures.ts` (the conditional lastProjectId seed), `src/app/boot.ts` (first-run routing on key-absence), `tests/e2e/p6-w4-home.spec.ts` (per-test override), W4 commit `ff374ec`.

---

### H83 — A pixel-sample that reads the "surface" via a modal/percentile over a translucent or gappy element's BOUNDING BOX degenerates when the backdrop shows through gaps/rounded-corners — it measures the BACKDROP, not the surface

**Symptom:** an observation-grounded contrast test (p57 over-canvas, the [[V36]] Lokayata proof) flips polarity for the dark redesign (Wave A) — worst case now a BRIGHT scene. The re-grounded `it()` fails not on a real AA violation but on the FALSIFICATION: `bright.glyphLum (0.957) !> bright.surfaceLum*2` — i.e. the measured "surface" AND "glyph" both read ~0.957 (near white). Physically impossible: a `bg-2/90` pill (90% opaque dark) over a white scene composites to ~`#333`, not white.

**Root cause:** the sampler took the toolbar's `boundingBox()` and computed the SURFACE as the modal 5-bit color bucket over that whole box. The floating pill is a rounded rect inside a rectangular bbox; its corners + any inter-control transparent gaps show the GL scene behind it. On a DARK scene those backdrop pixels ≈ the surface, so the modal was the surface (the test "worked" for years / for the W3 dark-backdrop case). On a BRIGHT (`#ffffff`) scene the corner/gap pixels are pure white and OUTNUMBER the surface in the bbox → the modal bucket = white → "surface" measured as the backdrop. The brightest-grayish glyph pick then also lands on white. Both degenerate to the scene color. The test wasn't wrong about AA; the MEASUREMENT WINDOW included non-surface pixels, and the failure mode only surfaces when the backdrop is far from the surface (the exact worst case the test exists to check).

**The trap (wrong fix):** chase the falsification THRESHOLD (loosen `*2`, change the percentile) — treats a measurement-window bug as a tuning problem. Or brighten the glyph token (it's already correct). Or conclude the surface genuinely fails AA and over-opaque the pill (changes the design to fix a test artifact). All paper over a sampling window that doesn't isolate the thing being measured.

**The real fix:** sample a SOLID sub-element that is guaranteed to be entirely ON the surface, not the gappy container bbox. p57 now samples an idle tool button's box (`floating-toolbar-move`) — an idle button has no fill, so its pixels = the pill surface (`bg-2/90` over scene) + its own glyph, with NO rounded-corner / inter-group scene bleed in the window. Surface modal + brightest-glyph pick both isolate correctly. General rule: **when measuring a translucent surface's composited color from real pixels, clip to a region that is 100% covered by that surface — never a bounding box whose corners/gaps expose the backdrop you're trying to measure AGAINST.** The reusable diagnostic question: "does my measurement window contain ANY pixels that are not the thing I'm measuring?"

**Cross-ref:** [[V36]] (the inversion re-grounding this surfaced under — Wave A light→dark; the polarity flip is what exposed the latent sampling bug, dormant while the dark-backdrop case kept gaps ≈ surface), [[H40]] (boundary-pair observation — "which side did I actually observe": here, the surface vs the backdrop-through-the-gaps). Provenance: ORIGIN = Spline-redesign Wave A, 2026-06-09 — re-grounding p57 dark→bright worst case; the bright-scene sample read white because the pill bbox exposed corners/gaps. Single occurrence → catalogued because the wrong-fix (threshold-chasing) is seductive and the rule (clip to a fully-covered region) is reusable for any real-pixel surface measurement. WHY = a degenerate measurement window makes an observation test lie in EXACTLY the worst case it guards. HOW = sample a solid sub-element; assert the window contains only surface+glyph. REF: `tests/e2e/p57-bright-scene-contrast.spec.ts` (`sampleOverlay(page, 'floating-toolbar-move')` — solid idle-button box, not `'floating-viewport-toolbar'` bbox), Wave A commit `38c925c`.

### H72: "Feature broken/missing in the live app" = wrong branch checked out (dev server serves the WORKING TREE)

**Symptom:** while juggling several feature branches/PRs in one session, the user reports a just-shipped feature is absent or broken in the running app ("I still can't collapse the right panel"), even though its code is committed and its e2e passed. Also surfaces as: a bug investigation reproduces against code that does NOT contain the fix.

**Trap:** treat it as a NEW bug in the feature and start re-debugging the code — when the code on disk (what `vite` serves via HMR) is simply a DIFFERENT branch than the one that has the feature. The dev server serves the **working tree**, i.e. whatever is `git checkout`'d right now, not "the branch where I wrote the feature."

**Root cause:** branch-hopping for parallel PRs (here: feat/173 collapse ↔ fix/175 timeout ↔ feat/165 camera) leaves the working tree on whichever branch was last checked out. The live app silently reflects that branch. The feature isn't broken; it isn't compiled in.

**Real fix:** before debugging "the app is wrong," verify WHICH branch is checked out and that the served module actually contains the code — `git branch --show-current` + `curl -s localhost:5180/src/<file> | grep -c <testid/symbol>`. If 0, `git checkout <feature-branch>` and refresh. One grep settles "is the feature even present" before any code hypothesis.

**Sub-lesson (same episode) — observe the RIGHT artifact before diagnosing.** A gizmo bug report ("arrow heads point wrong") was first investigated against the bottom-right nav widget (`GizmoViewport`) when the user meant the on-object transform gizmo (`TransformControls`) — a whole observation pass wasted on the wrong surface (no object was even selected, so the transform gizmo wasn't visible). When a UI element is named ambiguously, get the user's screenshot / pin the exact element BEFORE forming a hypothesis. And: a camera-race hypothesis (two `makeDefault` cameras) was DISPROVEN by observation — the suspected-broken view was pixel-identical on main and the camera-decoupled branch. Verdict: the transform gizmo is geometrically CORRECT — three.js `TransformControls` orients handles from `controls.eye` (the render camera), and its arrows point to world-positive by design (they do NOT flip to face the viewer; Blender's nav gizmo is the same). "Heads always point +X/+Y/+Z" is stock behavior, not a bug — flipping handles to the camera-facing side or adding negative handles would be a FEATURE (custom gizmo), not a fix.

**Five-limbed:**

1. **Claim:** a feature reported "missing/broken" in the live app, when its code is committed + tested, is almost always the wrong branch checked out — not a code defect.
2. **Reason:** the dev server serves the working tree; multi-branch sessions leave it on an unrelated branch; the feature module on disk lacks the code.
3. **Universal principle:** observe the actual artifact in play (the served bytes, the named element) before hypothesizing about logic — the cheapest discriminator first.
4. **Application:** `git branch --show-current` + `curl | grep -c <symbol>` (0 ⇒ wrong branch); for ambiguous UI, get the screenshot before debugging.
5. **Conclusion:** a 5-second branch/served-code check precedes any code-level debugging when juggling parallel PRs; and a stock-library behavior is not a bug until the spec says otherwise.

**Cross-ref:** [[H65]] (DEV-seam vs production — "exists in my context but not the real one" family; H72 is the branch-context twin), the Lokayata base-layer rule (observe, don't infer — here: observe which branch/element). Provenance: ORIGIN = 2026-06-05 session — inspector-collapse "didn't work" because the tree was on fix/175; gizmo "bug" was stock TransformControls + initially the wrong widget. WHY = without this, a parallel-PR session burns time re-debugging present-and-correct code, or fixing the wrong surface. HOW = the branch + served-code grep + screenshot-before-hypothesis triple. REF: `src/app/NPanel.tsx` (collapse, feat/173), `src/viewport/Viewport.tsx:170` (GizmoViewport), `node_modules/three/examples/jsm/controls/TransformControls.js` (handle orient from `eye`). Issues #173 (collapse), gizmo = no-bug (no issue filed).

### H71: Heavy e2e flake at the test-timeout BOUNDARY — undersized budget, not a race

**Symptom:** CI e2e job fails intermittently, always at **~31s** (the 30s test timeout + teardown), with `page.waitForFunction: Test timeout of 30000ms exceeded`. The _failing test varies run-to-run_ — `p151-gltf-child-apply.spec.ts:339` (M8 bake→delete→reload→re-render), `p7.14-my-imports-mgmt.spec.ts:126` (︙rename: copy-all→assetRef-rewrite→glTF-reload→delete-old), `p1-acceptance.spec.ts:411` (drag-drop) — whichever heavy test the loaded runner pushes over the line. Re-running clears it ~half the time (whack-a-mole); it blocks merges.

**Trap:** Read it as a logic race in the specific failing test (it's always the OPFS/reload tests, so "OPFS reload is racy") → add a workaround await, or bump that ONE test's inner `expect` timeout (the rename test already did → 15s) → it still times out at the 30s TEST level because the inner bump wasn't the binding constraint. Whack-a-mole per test never converges because the cause is shared, not local.

**Root cause:** the un-tuned 30s Playwright default (boilerplate since the P0 scaffold `a1083be`, never deliberately chosen) is simply too small for the heaviest three.js+OPFS chains on a constrained CI runner. Local: ~6 cores (`581% cpu`), ~7s/test, **11/11 deterministic, never near 30s** → no race. CI: ~2 vCPU + software-GL (SwiftShader) for three.js → 4-5× slower → ~30s, straddling the limit. A flake that _hovers at the budget boundary_ (rather than failing hard or hanging forever) is the signature of an undersized budget, NOT a logic race (a race fails nondeterministically; a missing-await hangs the full timeout EVERY time on CI).

**Real fix:** raise the budget on CI only, at BOTH timeout layers in `playwright.config.ts` — `timeout: process.env.CI ? 60_000 : 30_000` (test-level: M8/rename, proven to need ~34s) AND `expect: { timeout: process.env.CI ? 15_000 : 5_000 }` (assertion-level: the `expect.poll(opfsDirExists)` after break-refs+deleteOpfsTree in p7.14 delete-referenced — the test-level bump structurally cannot reach it, it has its own 5s poll window).
