One config covers the whole span (every heavy e2e + every OPFS-mutation poll, present + future); local keeps the tight budgets for fast hang-detection. Calibration, not race-papering: race-papering masks nondeterminism with time; here there is none to mask (proven deterministic — M8/rename pass at 34s, p7.14 delete-referenced completes <5s locally), only budgets mis-sized vs the real work on a software-GL/software-OPFS runner. **The two layers are independent — a test-timeout bump does NOT extend a per-`expect`/`expect.poll` window; calibrate both or the assertion-layer flake surfaces next (it did: fixing the test budget exposed p7.14:190's 5s poll).** **Residual, SEPARATE root cause:** `p1-acceptance.spec.ts:411` drag-drop HANGS the full budget on ~half its first attempts then passes the retry in ~6s — a nondeterministic race (seed/drag), NOT a budget issue (a bigger budget just makes its first-attempt failure slower). Track + fix separately; do not conflate with this entry.

**Detection signal:** failures cap at exactly the test-timeout value (~31s, not an assertion message); the _set_ of failing tests is unstable across runs but always the heaviest ones; the same tests pass deterministically and fast locally (run `--repeat-each=5`, observe none approaches the budget). Distinguisher from a true hang: a hang fails 100% on CI (predicate never true headless) AND would still fail with a bigger budget; a budget-flake passes once given headroom.

**Five-limbed:**

1. **Claim:** raising the CI-only test timeout removes the boundary flake without masking any defect.
2. **Reason:** the tests are proven deterministic and complete in ~7s locally; CI only differs in speed (2 vCPU + software GL), so the predicates DO resolve, just past 30s.
3. **Universal principle:** a test-runner timeout is a budget that must be sized to the work's real wall-clock on the slowest target environment, not left at a boilerplate default.
4. **Application:** the heaviest ingest→bake→reload chains need ~30s on a software-GL 2-vCPU runner; 60s gives ~2× headroom; local keeps 30s for fast hang-detection.
5. **Conclusion:** the boundary flake disappears (budget now exceeds real need) while a genuine hang still fails (it would exceed 60s too) — the fix discriminates, it doesn't blanket-suppress.

**Cross-ref:** [[H16]] — sibling meta-pattern (CI reliability vs wall-clock slack). H16's lesson was "hunt the missing-await, not the speedup"; H71 is the OTHER branch of that fork: once you've PROVEN determinism (no missing await), the remaining boundary flake is budget, and the honest fix is a bigger budget, not another await. The two together: missing-await → fix the await (H16); deterministic-but-slow → fix the budget (H71). Provenance: ORIGIN = #175, 2026-06-05 — investigating the #164/#172 merge-blocking flake; observed 11/11 local determinism + ≥3 different heavy tests straddling 31s across runs → classified as budget, not race. WHY = without this entry the next budget-boundary flake gets mis-diagnosed as a per-test race and whack-a-moled per file (the rename test's 15s inner bump was exactly that dead end). HOW = CI-conditional global timeout; the boundary-cap symptom + cross-run instability + local determinism is the recognition triple. REF: `playwright.config.ts:10` (the CI-conditional timeout), `tests/e2e/p151-gltf-child-apply.spec.ts:339`, `tests/e2e/p7.14-my-imports-mgmt.spec.ts:126`, `tests/e2e/p1-acceptance.spec.ts:411` (the observed heavy tests), CI run `26964301818` (3-test boundary failure evidence). Issue #175.

### H67 — An editor "view" that IS a scene object can never be seen or selected as that object — the viewport renders THROUGH it

**Span:** any editor that mounts a scene-authored camera as the viewport's render camera (drei `<PerspectiveCamera makeDefault>` driven straight off the DAG). The viewport then looks THROUGH the scene camera: you sit at its apex, so it has no visible body and a click can't land on it; a SECOND camera node (not the active one) renders nothing at all because the render walk only mounts `scene.camera`. #165 instantiation: `SceneFromDAG`'s `CameraNode` mounted the DAG camera `makeDefault`; the user reported "I see the gizmo but not the camera, I can't select it."

**Symptom:** a first-class scene entity (camera) is invisible/unselectable in the viewport while its transform gizmo floats in space (the gizmo reads the DAG transform, but there's no body to click). The tell: "the gizmo is there but the object isn't."

**Trap (the wrong fix):** draw a frustum body for the active camera while STILL rendering through it — you're inside it, so the body is at your eye (invisible) and adds nothing. A second wrong fix: give BOTH an editor camera and the DAG camera `makeDefault` so you can toggle — they RACE (drei's `makeDefault` captures `oldCam` on mount and RESTORES it on flag-flip; two complementary `makeDefault` cameras fight over `state.camera` on every toggle, order-dependent).

**Real fix:** DECOUPLE the editor view from the scene cameras (Blender/Houdini model). The editor owns ONE always-default free orbit camera (`EditorViewCamera`); DAG cameras stop being `makeDefault` and become ordinary scene objects drawn as selectable wireframe frustums (`CameraHelpers`, mirroring `LightHelpers`). "Look through camera" (Numpad 0) = the ONE editor camera ADOPTS the DAG camera's pose+projection (orbit disabled) — never a second `makeDefault`, so no race. Architecturally: the viewport is a PROJECTION of the DAG, not the scene camera itself (production render uses the DAG camera independently).

**Detection signal:** a scene-authored entity is mounted as an editor singleton driven by the editor's own controls (camera-as-view, "the light you're standing in", an audio listener at the ear). Ask: "is this thing BOTH the scene's data AND the editor's instrument? If so, can the user see/select it AS data?" If no → decouple: editor owns its instrument, the data renders as a selectable proxy.

**Five-limbed argument:**

1. **Claim:** mounting the DAG camera as the viewport's `makeDefault` render camera makes that camera invisible and unselectable as a scene object.
2. **Reason:** the render camera IS the viewer's eye, so its own body projects to the eye (nothing to see/click), and the render walk only mounts the single active camera (others render nothing).
3. **Universal principle:** a thing cannot simultaneously be the instrument of observation and an observed object in the same frame — the observer and the observed must be distinct entities.
4. **Application:** split them — `EditorViewCamera` is the (only) instrument; DAG cameras are observed objects drawn as `CameraHelpers` frustums; look-through is the instrument adopting the object's pose, not a second instrument.
5. **Conclusion:** decoupling instrument from data is the structural fix; a single always-default editor camera also dissolves the `makeDefault` restore-race that any "toggle between two real cameras" approach would hit.

**Cross-ref:** [[H40]] (observe the RENDERED object, not the inferred params — the frustum/selection read the camera node, gizmo unchanged), [[H45]] (clone/own-vs-borrow boundary, same "who owns this object" family). Provenance: ORIGIN = #165, 2026-06-05 — user friction "camera not visible/selectable in the viewport." WHY = without this entry the next scene-entity-as-editor-instrument (listener, light-you-stand-in) repeats the conflation and ships an unselectable first-class object. HOW = decouple instrument from data; editor owns one always-default instrument; data renders as a selectable proxy; "look through" = adopt, never a second makeDefault. REF: `src/viewport/EditorViewCamera.tsx` (the one editor instrument + look-through adopt + drei makeDefault grounding at `node_modules/@react-three/drei/core/PerspectiveCamera.js:52-64`), `src/viewport/CameraHelpers.tsx` (the selectable frustum proxy), `src/app/activeCamera.ts` (pure pose helper), `src/viewport/SceneFromDAG.tsx` (camera no longer makeDefault; enumerates camera nodes), `src/viewport/Viewport.tsx` (orbit gated off in look-through + view persistence), `tests/e2e/p165-blender-camera.spec.ts` (frustum-click + look-through + persistence, falsified), dharana boundary `editor-view ↔ DAG-camera`. Issue #165.

### H68 — Capturing the live WebGL canvas (`toDataURL`/`drawImage`) returns a BLANK image because `preserveDrawingBuffer:false` — the call succeeds, so the blank ships silently

**Span:** any "save/export/render the viewport to an image" feature built on the LIVE R3F/three.js canvas. R3F creates the `WebGLRenderer` with `preserveDrawingBuffer:false` (the perf default — and `@react-three/postprocessing`'s EffectComposer overrides the gl context attributes too, e.g. flips `alpha`). After each composited frame the browser CLEARS the drawing buffer, so by the time a later microtask reads it (`canvas.toDataURL()`, `ctx.drawImage(canvas,…)`, `readPixels` on the default framebuffer) it's empty. #168 instantiation: the first naive path for "Render Image" was `viewportCanvas.toDataURL('image/png')`.

**Symptom:** the export "works" — no error, a valid PNG header, a plausibly-small file (≈12 KB for a 660×570 frame) — but the image is uniformly blank/transparent. Observed live: `drawImage` of the canvas onto a 2D scratch yielded center pixel `[0,0,0,0]`. The tell: a real render is tens-to-hundreds of KB and varies pixel-to-pixel; a blank is tiny and uniform.

**Trap (the wrong fix):** flip the live `Canvas` to `preserveDrawingBuffer:true` so `toDataURL` works. That taxes EVERY frame (the browser must retain the buffer) for a once-in-a-while export, it captures the WRONG camera (post-#165 the canvas renders the editor orbit view, not the production camera), the WRONG size (window/DPI, not the render resolution), and WITH editor chrome (grid/gizmo/helpers). Second wrong fix: `gl.render()` then `toDataURL()` synchronously — couples the export to the live render loop and still has the camera/size/chrome problems.

**Real fix:** never capture the live front-buffer. Render the scene OFFSCREEN into an explicit `WebGLRenderTarget` at the RenderOutput resolution, through a production camera built from the active camera node's pose, with editor chrome hidden (`userData.editorChrome`), then `readRenderTargetPixels` (auto-resolved from MSAA at `WebGLRenderer.js:1273`), flip GL's bottom-up rows, and encode via a 2D canvas. The live viewport is never touched; renderer state is saved/restored in a `finally`.

**Detection signal:** any code that reads pixels back from a canvas/renderer it did not create with `preserveDrawingBuffer:true`. Ask: "am I reading the DEFAULT framebuffer after a frame was composited? If so it's cleared." Always render to an explicit target you control and read THAT. Verify by OBSERVING the saved image (file size + a pixel sample + eyeball), never by "the call returned a data URL."

**Five-limbed argument:**

1. **Claim:** `canvas.toDataURL()`/`drawImage` on the live R3F canvas returns a blank image.
2. **Reason:** the context is created `preserveDrawingBuffer:false`, so the drawing buffer is cleared after compositing each frame; the later read sees an empty buffer.
3. **Universal principle:** a default WebGL drawing buffer is transient — its contents are only guaranteed DURING the frame that drew them; read-back after compositing requires either `preserveDrawingBuffer` or an explicit render target.
4. **Application:** render to a `WebGLRenderTarget` and `readRenderTargetPixels` from it — that buffer is owned, sized, and not auto-cleared.
5. **Conclusion:** the offscreen-target path also gets the right camera/size/chrome for free, so it's the correct architecture, not just the blank-fix.

**Cross-ref:** [[H40]] (observe the RENDERED output, not the inferred call result — a returned data URL is inference; the decoded pixels are observation), [[H65]] (the DEV-seam discipline used to expose the render for the falsifiable e2e). Provenance: ORIGIN = #168, 2026-06-05 — observed the naive `toDataURL` return a 12 KB blank on the live canvas. WHY = without this entry the next "screenshot/export/thumbnail" feature re-discovers the blank-buffer trap and ships a silently-empty image (the call never errors). HOW = render offscreen to an explicit target at an explicit resolution through the production camera with chrome hidden; observe the saved pixels. REF: `src/render/renderToImage.ts` (offscreen MSAA+sRGB target, chrome hide-pass, state restore; grounded `WebGLRenderer.js:1273` MSAA resolve), `src/app/renderImageAction.ts` (orchestrator), `src/viewport/Viewport.tsx` (the `preserveDrawingBuffer:false` Canvas), `tests/e2e/p168-render-to-image.spec.ts` (decoded-pixel asserts: not-blank, 1920×1080≠viewport, chrome-excluded — physically falsified 0 vs 221 grid pixels). Issue #168.

### H70 — A fallible/degradable operation whose OUTCOME the caller drops (`void result` / silent fallback) is a silent no-op — the user gets nothing and no reason

**Span:** any user-triggered action that can fail OR silently degrade, where the failure/degradation is REPRESENTED (a returned `{ ok, reason }`, a chosen fallback backend) but never SURFACED. Two instantiations shipped together: (1) #170 — `renderActiveProjectToPng()` returned `{ ok: false, reason: 'viewport-not-ready' }`, but the toolbar + menu callers did `void renderActiveProjectToPng()` → on failure the render produced no file and no message. (2) #148 — `pickStorage()` falls OPFS → IndexedDB → Memory; landing on Memory means nothing persists across reload, but boot continued silently → the user loses everything on refresh with no warning. The shape is identical: the system KNOWS the outcome, the caller throws it away.

**Symptom:** "I clicked it and nothing happened" / "I reloaded and my work was gone." No error in the console (the operation didn't throw — it returned a value or chose a fallback). The tell: a function returns a structured result/enum that some caller `void`s or ignores, OR a capability-selection chain that has a `return new FallbackThing()` with no notification at the selection site.

**Trap (the wrong fix):** make the operation THROW on failure so something gets logged. That turns a recoverable, expected outcome (viewport not ready yet; durable storage unavailable) into an exception the caller must try/catch, and a thrown error in a void handler is still invisible to the user. Second wrong fix: `console.error` at the failure site — invisible to a non-developer; the user is who needs to know.

**Real fix:** the outcome must be CONSUMED and SURFACED. Build a user-facing feedback surface (a transient toast / notification store) ONCE, then wire every fallible/degradable action's outcome into it: success → confirmation, failure → an error toast with a reason, degradation → a (sticky) warning. Keep the outcome→toast mapping a PURE function so it is unit-testable without the live operation, and keep the action's core return value intact (callers that need the result still get it). Domain-aligned: one notification boundary, N callers — do not invent a bespoke alert per action.

**Detection signal:** grep for `void someAction(` where `someAction` returns a non-void result, and for capability/fallback selection (`return new MemoryX()`, `?? defaultBackend`) with no adjacent user notification. Ask: "if this returns the failure/fallback branch, how does the USER find out?" If the answer is "they don't" or "console", it's this pattern. Verify the fix by OBSERVING the real toast in the running app (real DOM/pixels), not by asserting the function returned a result.

**Five-limbed argument:**

1. **Claim:** an action whose failure/fallback outcome the caller discards is a silent no-op to the user.
2. **Reason:** the outcome exists only as a return value / internal branch; with no surface consuming it, nothing reaches the UI, and the absence of a throw means nothing reaches the console either.
3. **Universal principle:** a fallible operation is only complete when its outcome is OBSERVABLE by the party who must act on it — representing the outcome is necessary but not sufficient; it must be surfaced.
4. **Application:** add a notification surface (notificationStore + ToastViewport) and wire #170's render result + #148's storage-kind through pure outcome→toast mappers; the toolbar/menu/boot consume the outcome instead of voiding it.
5. **Conclusion:** the user now sees success/failure/degradation, so neither the failed render nor the non-durable storage is silent — the symptom is eliminated by surfacing, not by throwing.

**Cross-ref:** [[H68]] (the sibling "silently ships a wrong/empty result" render trap — H68 was the render PRODUCING nothing valid; H70 is the render's outcome not being SURFACED), [[H64]]/[[H60]] (capability fallback selection — H70 adds "tell the user when the fallback is non-durable"), assetErrorStore (the persistent-error sibling surface; H70's toast is its transient complement). Provenance: ORIGIN = #170 + #148, 2026-06-05 — built the notification surface to serve both; observed the bare `void renderActiveProjectToPng()` and the silent Memory fallback. WHY = without this entry the next fallible action (export, publish, a future capability probe) re-ships a silent no-op — the result is "represented" so it looks handled, but no surface consumes it. HOW = one notification surface, pure outcome→toast mappers, callers consume the outcome; observe the real toast. REF: `src/app/stores/notificationStore.ts` (the surface), `src/app/ToastViewport.tsx` (renderer, App-root mount), `src/app/renderImageAction.ts` (`renderResultToToast` + `renderImageWithFeedback`), `src/app/boot.ts` (`storageFallbackWarning` + the boot notify), `src/app/{TopToolbar,MenuBar}.tsx` (callers consume the result), `tests/e2e/notify-surface.spec.ts` (real-DOM, physically falsified), [[V33]] (the invariant), dharana B18. Issues #170, #148.

### H69 — A boot-once latch (`useRef(false)` / `didInit`) scoped to component lifetime silently strands per-domain state when the component outlives the domain it guards

**Span:** any "do this exactly once, then let something else own it" guard implemented as a lifetime-scoped boolean ref in a component that mounts ONCE but represents a sequence of domain objects. The classic shape: `const didInit = useRef(false); useEffect(() => { if (!didInit.current) { initFromDomain(); didInit.current = true; } }, [domainDerivedValue])`. The effect re-runs when the domain changes, but the boolean — already `true` — gates the init branch off, so the new domain's state is silently ignored. #167 instantiation: `EditorViewCamera` booted the orbit view once via `didInit`; the R3F Canvas mounts once for the app lifetime, so switching projects in-session re-derived `pose`/`projectId` but the boot branch (`!didInit.current`, already true) no-op'd — the view stayed at the previous project's pose and ignored the new project's active camera AND its saved view. Reload "worked" only because remount reset the ref.

**Symptom:** a once-per-X initialization fires correctly on the FIRST X and never again, even though X changed without a remount. The tell: "reload fixes it" — because reload is the only thing that resets the lifetime-scoped ref. Looks like a stale-view / stale-state bug that mysteriously self-heals on refresh.

**Trap (the wrong fix):** add a separate `useEffect` that resets `didInit.current = false` on the domain-id change. This is a second guard racing the first: effect ordering decides whether the reset runs before or after the boot effect in the same render, and if the boot effect runs first it boots against the OLD ref value, then the reset clears it, then nothing re-boots until the next unrelated re-render. Two cooperating guards on one lifecycle is the same workaround-cascade smell as H40's parallel walks.

**Real fix:** make the guard's KEY match the domain it guards, not the component lifetime. Replace the boolean with the domain identity: `const bootedId = useRef<string|null>(null); … else if (bootedId.current !== domainId) { initFromDomain(domainId); bootedId.current = domainId; }`, and add `domainId` to the effect deps. One latch, keyed to the lifecycle. First boot (`null !== id`) and every domain switch (`oldId !== newId`) run the init; re-renders within one domain (`id === id`) no-op, preserving the "let X own it after boot" contract. (Safe here because `switchProject()` updates the project store + hydrates the DAG store synchronously back-to-back in boot.ts, so `domainId` and the domain-derived `pose` are consistent in the same React render — verify that consistency before relying on it.)

**Detection signal:** a `useRef(false)`/`didInit` boolean guarding a once-only init inside a component whose mount lifetime is LONGER than the thing it initializes from (app-lifetime Canvas/provider/singleton holding per-project / per-document / per-selection state). Ask: "what is the true SCOPE of this 'once' — the component, or a domain object that can change under it? If the domain can change without a remount, the boolean leaks the previous domain's state." Key the latch to the domain id.

**Five-limbed argument:**

1. **Claim:** a lifetime-scoped boolean boot guard fails to re-initialize when its source domain object changes without a remount.
2. **Reason:** the boolean records "have I EVER booted," not "have I booted for THIS domain"; once true it gates every subsequent domain's init branch off.
3. **Universal principle:** a latch guard must be keyed to the lifecycle it guards — a guard whose scope is wider than its subject leaks the subject's prior state across transitions.
4. **Application:** swap the boolean for `bootedProjectId` and compare against the live `projectId`; boot runs on first mount and on each project switch, no-ops within a project.
5. **Conclusion:** keying the guard to the project boundary re-frames the view on switch while preserving reload and intra-project orbit behavior — the symptom (stale view that only reload fixes) is eliminated structurally, not patched with a second reset effect.

**Cross-ref:** [[H67]] (same editor-view ↔ DAG-camera boundary — H67 decoupled instrument from data; H69 keys the decoupled instrument's boot to the project), [[H40]] (the "two cooperating guards / parallel mechanisms" smell the trap shares). Provenance: ORIGIN = #167, 2026-06-05 — found in #165 self-review: in-session project switch didn't re-frame; reload did. WHY = without this entry the next app-lifetime singleton holding per-domain state (a once-init provider keyed to project/document/selection) repeats the lifetime-scoped boolean and silently strands the new domain's state, masked by "reload fixes it." HOW = key the latch to the domain id (`bootedId.current !== id`), add the id to effect deps, verify the domain-id and domain-derived values update in the same render. REF: `src/viewport/EditorViewCamera.tsx` (the project-keyed boot guard), `src/app/boot.ts` (`switchProject`/`duplicateCurrentProject` synchronous setCurrent+hydrate), `tests/e2e/p167-project-switch-reframe.spec.ts` (orbit A → duplicate → assert reframe to active-cam pose; physically falsified by reverting to `=== null`), dharana boundary `editor-view ↔ DAG-camera` (B16). Issue #167.

### H84 — Two long-lived parallel branches independently allocate the SAME monotonic id (catalogue Vn/Hn/Bn, migration version, enum, D-UX number); a keep-both merge silently produces a DUPLICATE that is incoherent, not additive

**Symptom:** integrating two feature branches that both forked from the same point and each appended "the next" id. At the merge, the conflict region shows HEAD defining `V32 = material IR` and theirs defining `V32 = editorChrome` (and `V33` twice, etc.) — DIFFERENT content under the SAME number. A reflexive keep-both (strip the markers, keep both blocks) yields a catalogue with two `V32`s: every `[[V32]]` cross-reference is now ambiguous, and the duplicate reads as additive when it is a collision.

**Trap (the wrong fix):** treat EVERY catalogue/doc conflict in a big merge as the routine keep-both (which IS correct for genuinely-distinct entries — H67 vs H72, Home rows vs Toast rows). Blanket keep-both across a region that contains a same-number collision ships the duplicate. The tell that distinguishes the two: keep-both is right when the two sides have DIFFERENT ids; it is WRONG when they share an id with different bodies.

**Root cause:** monotonic id allocation (`V${max+1}`, `migrations[n+1]`, the next `D-UX-n`) is a SHARED counter with no coordination across branches. Two branches off the same base each see the same `max` and both take `max+1`. The longer the branches live in parallel, the more collisions accumulate (here: v0.6-#2/#3/#4 lineage took V32–V36 while the camera/render/notify lineage independently took V32/V33 — two collisions in one integration).

**Real fix:** at integration, before stripping markers, SCAN the conflict for same-id/different-body collisions. For each, keep the canonical lineage's number (the more-referenced / longer-established one) and RENUMBER the other to the next globally-free id, then update its references. Here: material/UV kept V32/V33; editorChrome→V37, surface-outcome→V38, with a comment at the definition recording the renumber. Then `grep -oE '^#+ V[0-9]+' | sort | uniq -d` (and the H/B/D-UX analogues) as the post-merge gate — duplicate-id detection is a one-line check that catches what keep-both hides. Reference fix-up (the dangling `[[V32]]` that now means V37) is prose-only debt: chase it where the meaning is unambiguous, flag the rest.

**Sub-lesson (same integration) — a redesign that DELETES a surface + a parallel branch that MODIFIES it = a modify/delete conflict whose resolution is "honor the deletion AND re-home the feature."** v0.6 #4 deleted `TopToolbar.tsx`/`ModeBadge.tsx`; the camera branch had added look-through affordances to them. Git left both files in-tree (modify/delete). Resolution: `git rm` them (the redesign's call stands) BUT verify the feature they hosted survives elsewhere — the look-through toolbar button had ALSO landed in the new floating pill (auto-merged), so the affordance lived; the CAMERA-VIEW badge did NOT survive (dropped, flagged as a follow-up). Always check: "what feature did the deleted surface host, and does it have another home?" before accepting the deletion.

**Detection signal:** a content conflict in a file with monotonic ids where both sides' headers carry the SAME number; OR a modify/delete conflict during a redesign-integration. Distinguisher from routine keep-both: run the duplicate-id grep after EVERY catalogue keep-both in a multi-branch integration.

**Five-limbed:**

1. **Claim:** keep-both is unsafe for a conflict region where both sides allocate the same monotonic id with different bodies — it must be a renumber, not a merge.
2. **Reason:** two branches off one base each take `max+1` with no shared counter, so the same number names two different things; keeping both makes every reference to that number ambiguous.
3. **Universal principle:** an uncoordinated monotonically-allocated id is a merge hazard — parallel allocation guarantees collision proportional to branch lifetime; the integration, not the authoring, is where uniqueness must be re-established.
4. **Application:** at the ux-overhall integration, V32/V33 each collided (material/UV vs editorChrome/notify); kept the canonical lineage's numbers, renumbered the other to V37/V38, gated with `grep '^#+ V[0-9]+' | uniq -d`.
5. **Conclusion:** scanning conflicts for same-id collisions + a duplicate-id grep after merge converts a silent incoherence into a caught-and-renumbered entry; the catalogue stays a bijection between number and meaning.

**Cross-ref:** [[H79]] (the sibling integration-hazard — removing shared state has a wider blast radius than enumerated, and blanket find-replace breaks where the token meant something different; H84 is the allocation-side twin: parallel ADDING collides as H79's parallel REMOVING over-reaches), [[H27]] (re-validation — both are "the merge/wave inherits a stale assumption"). Provenance: ORIGIN = ux-overhall integration, 2026-06-10 — merging the camera/render/notify lineage into the v0.6-#2/#3/#4 lineage surfaced V32 AND V33 same-number/different-body collisions in `vyapti.md` (plus clean keep-both for genuinely-distinct H/B/D-UX entries, which validated the distinguisher). WHY = without this entry the next long-branch integration blanket-keeps-both and ships duplicate-numbered invariants whose cross-references silently point at the wrong concept. HOW = scan-for-same-id-collision before stripping markers + renumber-the-non-canonical + `uniq -d` duplicate gate + re-home-on-modify/delete. REF: `.anvi/vyapti.md` (V37/V38 renumber + the renumber-provenance comment), `src/app/TopToolbar.tsx`/`src/viewport/ModeBadge.tsx` (the modify/delete-honored deletions), branch `ux-overhall`. No issue (integration-time learning).

### H85 — A full-page chrome surface that paints an OPAQUE page-level background token OCCLUDES a body-level fixed background (the Spline ambient glow); the surface looks "fine" in isolation but is visually disconnected from the lit dark stage every other surface shares

**Symptom:** the dark redesign's signature ambient glow (soft corner blooms) reads on the editor, but a different full-viewport route (the Home launcher) is a flat dead near-black — the same hex as the glow's base, minus the blooms. Nothing errors; the route renders; it just looks like a lower-fidelity, separate product. The glow is "missing" on that one surface only.

**Trap (the wrong fix):** add a SECOND glow to the offending route (re-declare the radial-gradient background on the Home root, or a decorative glow div). This works visually but forks the ambient treatment into two definitions that drift — change the editor glow and the home glow stays stale. It also reads as "the glow was missing" when it was never missing — it was COVERED.

**Root cause:** the ambient glow is painted ONCE on `body` (`src/index.css` — fixed radial-gradients over `#0e0e11`, `background-attachment: fixed`). Every floating panel reads as sitting ON that lit stage because the panels are translucent/transparent over the page body. A full-page surface that sets an OPAQUE page-level background token (`bg-bg` = the same `#0e0e11`, fully opaque) paints over the body exactly where the glow lives → the glow is occluded, not absent. The bug is OCCLUSION, not a missing asset.

**Real fix:** make the full-page surface TRANSPARENT (drop the opaque `bg-bg`; keep `text-fg`), so the body's fixed glow reads through — the surface joins the SAME stage (V34: one glow reused, not a parallel one — [[V39]]). Panels ON the surface stay translucent (`bg-2/90`, `bg/95`) so the glow also reads through them, which is the Spline "floating panel on a lit stage" look. The one-line tell at authoring: "does this surface paint an opaque page-level bg? then it occludes the body stage."

**Detection signal:** a new full-viewport route/surface in the dark redesign whose background is visibly flatter than the editor; OR a `className` on a route root containing `bg-bg`/`bg-[#0e0e11]`/any opaque page-token. Observation: screenshot the surface and look for the corner blooms — absent ⇒ occluded.

**Five-limbed:**

1. **Claim:** a full-page dark-redesign surface must be transparent over the body, not paint an opaque page-level background.
2. **Reason:** the ambient glow lives on `body` (fixed); an opaque page-level bg covers it exactly, so the surface is disconnected from the shared stage.
3. **Universal principle:** when a base layer owns a shared visual treatment, an opaque overlay at the same extent destroys it — share the base by being transparent, don't re-paint it locally (that forks one treatment into N drifting copies).
4. **Application:** Wave E Home — dropped the root `bg-bg` → transparent → the index.css blooms read through; cards stayed translucent (`bg-2/90`) so the glow reads through them too.
5. **Conclusion:** transparency reuses the one glow (no drift, no "missing-glow" misdiagnosis) and the home joins the editor's lit stage.

**Cross-ref:** [[V39]] (the invariant this fix establishes — dark full-viewport surfaces are transparent over the body stage), [[V34]] (one substrate / one treatment, reused not duplicated), dharana [[B20]]. Provenance: ORIGIN = Spline Wave E home restyle, 2026-06-10 — the Home root's opaque `bg-bg` occluded the Wave A body glow; observed live (flat home vs lit editor), fixed by transparency. WHY = without this entry the next new full-page surface (a settings page, a publish view) re-paints opaque, looks disconnected, and gets "fixed" by a second parallel glow that drifts. HOW = transparent surface + translucent panels; grep route roots for opaque page-bg tokens. REF: `src/index.css` (body ambient glow), `src/app/Home.tsx` (transparent root), `tests/e2e/spline-we-home.spec.ts` (the glow-reads-through assertion: root `backgroundColor === rgba(0,0,0,0)`). Branch `ux-overhall`. No issue (redesign-time learning).

### H86 — A scroll container (`overflow-y-auto`) inside a CSS-grid cell does NOT scroll: the grid item defaults to `min-height: auto` (= min-content), so it GROWS to its content instead of being bounded by the track — and because cells in a row share one height, one tall cell drags the whole row (and its siblings) past the viewport

**Symptom:** the user reports "I can't scroll the left/right panel when it overflows." The outliner / inspector already have `overflow-y-auto`, but with a tall scene (many nodes) or many inspector sections the panel does not scroll — it grows to its content height, pushing the layout past the viewport (which `body{overflow:hidden}` then clips). On a SHORT scene nothing reproduces because the content fits.

**Trap (the wrong fix #1 — inert observation):** "force overflow" by clamping the scroll CONTAINER's height in a probe/test (`el.style.height='60px'`). The container then scrolls — but this only proves the CSS `overflow-y-auto` _can_ scroll, NOT that the real layout _bounds_ the container. The bug is precisely that the layout does NOT bound it; clamping hides the bug. **Observe by injecting tall CONTENT (a 2000px child) and letting the natural layout decide** — then the broken container grows (`clientHeight ≈ scrollHeight`, `scrollTop` stuck at 0, `body.scrollHeight ≫ viewport`); the fixed one stays bounded (`clientHeight ≪ scrollHeight`, `scrollTop` moves, `body.scrollHeight == viewport`).

**Trap (the wrong fix #2 — wrong layer):** add `overflow-y-auto` / `min-h-0` to the scroll element itself or a nearby ancestor and stop. The `min-height:0` must be set on EVERY ancestor between the scroll container and the bounded track — most importantly the **grid-cell wrapper** (the `<div style={{gridArea:…}}>`). If any link in that chain keeps `min-height:auto`, the track grows.

**Root cause:** a grid item's automatic minimum size is `min-content` (CSS Grid spec — same rule as flex items). A grid item containing a tall `overflow-y-auto` panel therefore refuses to shrink below the panel's content; the `1fr` track's used size becomes `max(fraction, that min-content)` → the track grows to the content. Since `tree | viewport | inspector` share one row height, the inspector's growth enlarges the whole row, dragging the outliner's cell with it (that is why fixing only the inspector wrapper also un-broke the tree — observed: reverting the inspector cell's `minHeight:0` made the TREE test red).

**Real fix:** `minHeight: 0` on the grid-cell wrapper (`Layout.tsx` inspector cell) + `min-h-0` on the in-cell flex column (`LeftSidebar` `<aside>`). The CSS-grid analog of the well-known flex `min-height:0` rule. AFTER (inject 2000px @ 800px viewport): `body.scrollHeight 800 == viewport`; inspector `clientHeight 642 / scrollHeight 2230 / scrolledTo 1588`; tree `clientHeight 440 / scrollHeight 2091 / scrolledTo 1651` — both bounded and scrolling.

**Falsifier inertness — a recurring class (extends the [[B20]] font-mono-inert note):** a falsifiable assertion must bite the REAL mechanism, not a proxy that is inert on this platform/layout. Two inert proxies hit THIS session: (a) clamping the container (above) — tests CSS not layout; (b) a scrollbar-GUTTER check (`offsetWidth - clientWidth`) to prove "no visible scrollbar" — **inert on macOS/headless-Chromium overlay scrollbars, which reserve no gutter whether or not the bar is hidden.** The biting signal for a hidden bar is the COMPUTED `scrollbar-width` (`none` vs `auto`); the biting signal for the scroll bug is injected-content `clientHeight ≪ scrollHeight` + `body.scrollHeight ≤ viewport`. Always ask: "if I revert the fix, does THIS assertion actually go red here?" — run it red to confirm.

**Detection signal:** user says "can't scroll the panel"; OR a panel with `overflow-y-auto` whose `scrollHeight > clientHeight` yet `scrollTop` won't move; OR `document.body.scrollHeight > window.innerHeight` in a `body{overflow:hidden}` shell (the layout blew out and is clipping). Grep grid-cell wrappers for a missing `minHeight: 0`.

**Five-limbed:**

1. **Claim:** a scroll container in a grid cell scrolls only if its whole ancestor chain to the bounded track sets `min-height:0` — starting with the grid-cell wrapper.
2. **Reason:** a grid item's auto minimum is min-content, so without `min-height:0` the item (and its shared `1fr` row) grows to content instead of bounding the overflow.
3. **Universal principle:** `overflow:auto` only scrolls when the element has a BOUNDED height; flex/grid items default to a content-based minimum that must be explicitly zeroed to propagate an ancestor's bound.
4. **Application:** `Layout.tsx` inspector grid-cell `minHeight:0` + `LeftSidebar` aside `min-h-0` → the `1fr` row stays viewport-bounded → both panels scroll.
5. **Conclusion:** the overflow now scrolls inside the panel; the page no longer blows out.

**Cross-ref:** [[V40]] (the invariant: chrome panels overflow-scroll within a bounded chain, proven by injected content not clamping), dharana [[B20]] (the inert-falsifier discipline). Provenance: ORIGIN = user "can't scroll the left/right panel" on `ux-overhall`, 2026-06-11 — reproduced by injecting 2000px content (grew + blew out), fixed with grid-item `minHeight:0`. WHY = without this entry the next paneled-grid layout silently can't scroll, and the bug gets "verified away" by an inert clamp test. HOW = `min-height:0` down the cell→panel chain; observe by injecting content; confirm the falsifier bites red. REF: `src/app/Layout.tsx` (inspector grid-cell `minHeight:0`), `src/app/LeftSidebar.tsx` (aside `min-h-0`), `src/app/SceneTree.tsx` + `src/app/NPanel.tsx` (the `overflow-y-auto` + `.no-scrollbar` scroll roots), `src/index.css` (`.no-scrollbar`), `tests/e2e/spline-panel-scroll.spec.ts` (inject-content + computed-scrollbar-width, both falsified). Commit `791de2a` (+`3792699` no-scrollbar). Branch `ux-overhall`. No issue (live-friction fix).

### H87 — Round-tripping the SAME scene through export→import is an INERT falsifier: the DAG is identical whether or not the importer actually hydrated — you must DIVERGE the live scene first

**Span:** any "serialize → deserialize → assert it survived" test where the deserialize target is the SAME live state the serialize read from (project save/load, scene export/import, undo/redo into the current doc, clipboard copy-paste into the same selection). The intuitive test — "export the current scene, import it, assert the scene is unchanged" — passes EVEN IF import is a complete no-op, because the current scene was already there. The assertion never moves; it can't distinguish "import worked" from "import did nothing." A direct instance of the [[B20]] inert-falsifier class at the persistence boundary.

**Symptom:** the round-trip e2e is green, but reverting the importer's hydrate (or its asset-rehydrate write) leaves it green too — the falsifier doesn't bite. You "verified" import without ever exercising the path that changes state.

**Trap (the wrong fix):** trust the same-scene round-trip because it's the most obvious shape ("save it, load it, it's still there"). It's structurally inert.

**Real fix:** DIVERGE the live state between export and import so a working import is OBSERVABLE and a broken one is not. Capture bundle A of the baseline; mutate the live scene (add a glTF node + asset, so it differs from A); open bundle A → a working import REPLACES the divergence (the baseline id-set returns, the added node gone), a broken import leaves the divergence in place (id-set assertion red). For the asset direction: ingest an asset → export (embeds it) → DELETE the OPFS bytes → open → assert the bytes are rehydrated back (the bytes can only reappear if the open path wrote them). Each assertion then moves only when the real mechanism runs.

**Detection signal:** a persistence/round-trip test whose "before" and "after" read the same store with no mutation in between. Ask: "if import were a no-op, would this still pass?" If yes → diverge first. Confirm by reverting the mechanism and watching it go red (the [[B20]] Lokayata-on-tests gate).

**Cross-ref:** [[B20]] (the inert-falsifier discipline this instantiates), [[H86]] (sibling inert-falsifier: clamp-vs-inject), [[V41]] (the portable-bundle invariant these tests guard), [[H73]] (commit-before-falsify — committed the e2e first, then sabotaged hydrate + write-loop, watched test 1 + 3 bite red, `git restore`). Provenance: ORIGIN = `.basher` scene-file format, 2026-06-11 — the first-draft round-trip asserted "export current → import → nodes survive," which is inert (current scene already present); fixed by ingesting a glTF to diverge before opening the baseline bundle. WHY = without this, every persistence round-trip ships a test that can't tell working from no-op. HOW = diverge-then-restore; delete-then-rehydrate; revert-and-watch-red. REF: `tests/e2e/menu-scene-file.spec.ts` (diverge-before-open + delete-then-rehydrate, both falsified red before commit), `src/app/boot.ts` (`importSceneBundle`), commit `1ecda1a`. Branch `ux-overhall`. No issue (live-feature build).

### H88 — An import/open affordance ACCEPTS a file it cannot fulfill on its own (a multi-file `.gltf` via a plain file picker) → it writes a partial asset and dies DEEP in the pipeline with a cryptic low-level error instead of failing EARLY with guidance

**Span:** any affordance whose accepted input is a CONTAINER that references external siblings the affordance can't capture — multi-file `.gltf` (references `.bin`/textures by relative URI) picked via a plain `<input type=file>` (captures only the picked file, never siblings); also: a `.csv` referencing a sidecar, a project file referencing external assets, an HTML import referencing local images. The picker's `accept=".gltf"` PROMISES it works; the file picker physically can't gather the siblings; the import proceeds, writes the entry, then throws when it reads the first missing sibling — a `NotFoundError` ("A requested file or directory could not be found" on Chromium, "Entry not found" on WebKit) that names a low-level path, not the user's problem.

**Symptom:** user picks their model and gets `asset failed: user-imports/scene-2/scene.gltf — import failed: Entry not found` (or "…could not be found"). The path is suffixed (`scene-2`) because a partial folder from a prior attempt already exists; the message points at the entry even though a SIBLING is what's missing; there's no hint that the fix is "use the folder picker" or "select all the files together."

**Trap (the wrong fix):** treat it as a path/encoding bug in the sibling resolver and go spelunking in `opfsSiblingPath` — the resolver is correct; the siblings were never written because the picker never had them. OR: silence the error. The real gap is the affordance accepting an input it can't satisfy, then reporting the failure in pipeline-internal terms.

**Real fix:** validate the precondition at the ONE ingest chokepoint (so all entry points — both pickers + drag-drop — are covered, V34) BEFORE doing partial work: parse the entry `.gltf`'s external URIs, resolve each against the picked SET using the same join+decode+normalize as the loader (`missingGltfSiblings` reusing `opfsSiblingPath`), and if any are absent, surface an ACTIONABLE message ("scene.gltf needs scene.bin, texture.png — pick the .gltf together with those files, or use File ▸ Import Folder…") and abort before writing. `.glb` (self-contained) skips the check. The honest contract: an affordance either fulfills its accepted input or tells the user, in their terms, exactly how to make it fulfillable.

**Sub-trap (double-report):** when a lower layer already reports-then-rethrows (the ingest chokepoint's documented contract), an OUTER catch that ALSO reports produces two banners for one error. Guard the outer catch with the same `!message.startsWith('import failed:')` check the inner layer uses — the early-throw exposed a latent double-report that the old deep-failure path (which returned void, never threw out) had hidden.

**Detection signal:** a NotFoundError / "not found" naming an internal path surfaced to the user; an `accept=` list that includes a container type whose dependencies the affordance can't gather; a failure reported AFTER partial side-effects (a half-written asset folder). Ask: "can this affordance actually fulfill every file type it accepts? if not, does it fail early with guidance, or late with a path?"

**Cross-ref:** [[H77]] (substrate completeness — siblings ARE part of the asset), [[V41]] (the portable-bundle completeness sibling: there, embed the full span; here, refuse an incomplete pick with guidance), dharana [[B21]] (the importer↔OPFS boundary). Provenance: ORIGIN = user "i can't seem to import gltf model — …scene.gltf — Entry not found" on `ux-overhall`, 2026-06-11 — reproduced live (Import Folder works; Import glTF on a lone multi-file `.gltf` fails); my session's `.basher` work did NOT touch import code (the bug is pre-existing, exposed by the user). WHY = without this, every container-accepting affordance re-ships the cryptic-deep-failure UX and re-debugs it as a resolver bug. HOW = validate at the chokepoint, fail early with an actionable message, dedup the double-report; observe live across folder / single-file / multi-select. REF: `src/app/asset/opfsGltfResolver.ts` (`missingGltfSiblings`), `src/app/asset/importGltf.ts` (`ingestGltfFolder` guard), `src/app/asset/importPicker.ts` (double-report dedup), `src/app/asset/opfsGltfResolver.test.ts` (7 unit), `tests/e2e/menu-import-gltf.spec.ts` (actionable-error + multi-select-works, falsified). Commit `a52a4bb`. Branch `ux-overhall`. No issue (live user-reported friction).

**Evolution (2026-06-11, session 3 — actionable-error → AUTO-ESCALATE):** the actionable message was still a DEAD-END — the same user re-hit it (`asset failed: scene` + `asset failed: os-drop`) importing `cicada_retro_cartoon_car` and asked to actually fix it. The deeper principle: **an affordance that can't fulfill its accepted input should ESCALATE to the sibling affordance that can — within the same user-activation window — not just narrate the failure.** When `openGltfFilePicker` detects a multi-file `.gltf` whose siblings are absent (new pure `gltfImportNeedsFolder`, reusing `locateEntryFile` + `missingGltfSiblings` so the trigger can't diverge from the importer's own check), it re-opens the DIRECTORY picker so the user grants the whole folder and the `.bin`/textures come along — no menu-item guesswork. **Activation-window discipline:** the re-open `.click()` must happen before the ~5s transient-activation budget lapses; reading the small entry `.gltf` is fine, but a huge multi-select (e.g. a 100 MB sibling `.glb`) read first could blow it (known edge, lone-pick common case proven). **Cancel-fallback (V38):** the escalated dialog's dismissal fires the input `cancel` event (NOT `change` — no change event on cancel) → falls back to the actionable banner, so a dismissed escalation is never a silent no-op; `handled` guards against a double-fire. Scoped to the PICKER — a lone-file os-drop keeps the H88 banner (a drop can't sensibly auto-open a folder dialog; drag the FOLDER instead). Sub-trap proven: the e2e must assert the SECOND `filechooser` fires (escalation) and that completing it lands a `GltfAsset` — falsified RED by neutralising the trigger (no 2nd chooser → timeout). REF: `src/app/asset/importPicker.ts` (`gltfImportNeedsFolder` + `openDirectoryImport`/`onCancel` + escalation wiring), `src/app/asset/importGltf.ts` (`locateEntryFile` exported), `src/app/asset/importPicker.test.ts` (7 unit — the escalation decision), `tests/e2e/menu-import-gltf.spec.ts` (`AUTO-ESCALATES` 2nd-filechooser e2e, falsified). Commit `972f33f`.

### H89 — A 3D-gizmo visual defect debugged from CODE-READING + SYNTHETIC repro instead of the USER's actual object is a guess: the plausible root cause (proxy inherits the object's scale) was FALSIFIED by ground-truth, and a flaky local browser blocked the only repro that mattered

**Status: RESOLVED — NOT-A-BUG (2026-06-13, `fix/ux-friction-4`, UX-backlog #1). Root cause found by reading the CORRECT source + live Playwright intel. The two-session transform hunt was misdirected by a grounding error (wrong source file) — see RESOLUTION.**

**RESOLUTION (2026-06-13) — the real mechanism + the grounding error that hid it.**
The defect was debugged for two sessions against `three/examples/jsm/controls/TransformControls.js` — **the wrong file.** drei's `<TransformControls>` imports from **`three-stdlib`** (`node_modules/@react-three/drei/core/TransformControls.js:5`), whose translate gizmo is built differently: each axis has TWO arrowhead cones BOTH at the **+end** (`three-stdlib/controls/TransformControls.js:795-808` — `[0,1,0]` for both the `fwd` and `bwd` Y cones; NO cone at the −end). A per-frame `axis·eye` test (`:642-674`, `AXIS_FLIP_TRESHOLD=0` `:605`) lights the `fwd` cone when the camera is on the axis's positive side, the `bwd` cone (rotated π, SAME +position, pointing back toward centre) when on the negative side. So the head is **pinned to the +end forever**; orbiting only swaps which co-located cone lights. From below, the green +Y `bwd` cone points downward → the user's "+Y arrowhead points down." Stock three-stdlib behaviour (≈ Blender Move gizmo). **Decision: accept it (not-a-bug); UX-backlog #1 closed.**
**Live intel that proved it:** a headless-Chromium + fresh-vite Playwright probe read the live `gizmo.translate.children` off `useThreeRef.scene` on a plain primitive AND a real imported GltfChild driven through identity / rot`[180,0,0]` / scale`[1,-1,1]` / scale`[-1,-1,-1]`. Per axis = 1 Line + 2 Mesh, BOTH meshes at world `+0.527`, one `visible:true`(fwd) one `visible:false`(bwd) — **byte-identical across all four transforms.** Object transform has ZERO effect on the heads ⇒ every transform hypothesis below (proxy scale, mirror, rotation) chased a variable that provably never enters the translate/world-space path (handle orientation there = identity quaternion). **Deepest lesson: the Grounding Check failed — read `@react-three/drei/core/*.js` import lines to find the ACTUAL bundled library before tracing `three/examples` (the docs-default, NOT what runs). One grep at the start saves the session.**

--- ORIGINAL (2026-06-12) FALSIFIED-HYPOTHESIS NOTES below, kept for the process lessons ---

**Symptom (user, annotated screenshots):** the transform/move gizmo's **+Y arrowhead points DOWN** (opposite the +Y axis the nav-cube shows as up) on a specific selected object; the red (X) and blue (Z) arrowheads look flattened. Happens on the user's live scene (a large red box / a glTF-ish model with a camera in-scene), NOT on a fresh starter-scene primitive.

**The plausible-but-FALSIFIED hypothesis:** `Gizmo.tsx`'s seeding effect sets the unscaled gizmo PROXY group's `scale` from the object's evaluated/seed scale (`resolveEvaluatedTransform`→`evalT.scale`, else `manip.scaleSeed`). Reasoning: the proxy exists precisely to DECOUPLE the gizmo from the object's scale; copying the scale back in re-distorts it, and a mirrored (negative-determinant — common in glTF) or non-uniform scale would flip/squash the translate arrowheads. Attempted fix: gate the scale-seeding onto `effectiveMode === 'scale'` only (translate/rotate keep unit-scale proxy). **RESULT: user confirmed "still not fixed" → hypothesis FALSIFIED, fix REVERTED.**

**Why the synthetic repro never bit (the real lesson):** every reproduction was attempted on a STARTER-SCENE plain `BoxMesh`, which the catalogue should have flagged is the wrong probe — `resolveEvaluatedTransform` returns `scale: null` for a plain box (its rendered `SceneChild` value carries no `.scale` field; only the **GltfChild** path (`resolveEvaluatedTransform.ts:232`) and the **AnimationLayer-unwrap** path (`:284`) ever return a non-null scale). So the proxy stays `[1,1,1]` for plain boxes REGARDLESS of the fix → the fix is a no-op there AND the bug can't be reproduced there. The user's object is almost certainly a **glTF model / GltfChild** (they import the cicada car etc.), where `evalT.scale` IS non-null — but I never built that repro.

**Trap (the wrong process, not just the wrong fix):** (a) theorized the cause from reading `Gizmo.tsx` + three.js `TransformControls.js` source instead of getting the user's actual object's TRANSFORM (rotation+scale) values; (b) trusted **HMR-based before/after falsification** — `git stash` + the running dev server served STALE (Fast-Refreshed) code, so the "falsification" passed in BOTH versions and gave a false all-clear (a fresh `vite` boot is required for a real base comparison); (c) burned the whole session fighting a **flaky local browser** — headed Chromium crashes on repeated WebGL launches ("Target page… closed" at the first `waitForTimeout`), and the heavy glTF-ingest e2e crash INTERMITTENTLY (failures MOVE between runs = environmental, not a logic regression — do NOT read a moving e2e failure as a real regression).

**What WAS ruled out (synthetic, plain box — still valid):** TransformControls normalizes uniform object scale out of the gizmo (a `[1,0.3,1]` box flattens but arrows stay uniform); negative single-axis scale `[1,-1,1]` did NOT flip the arrow; rotation `[180,0,0]` did NOT (gizmo runs in drei default `space="world"`, arrows world-axis-aligned); this three.js version does NOT flip translate arrows toward the camera (`TransformControls.js:1241` sets POSITIVE `handle.scale`, no AxisFlip). So on a plain box the Y arrow is robustly UP — the bug needs a node carrying a real evaluated scale.

**Detection signal / next-session protocol:** a reported 3D-gizmo/viewport visual defect → FIRST get the user's exact node (type + inspector TRANSFORM rotation/scale) and reproduce on THAT object/asset, not a synthetic primitive; if the local browser thrashes, prefer headless Chromium (SwiftShader renders WebGL for screenshots — it worked when headed crashed) and a FRESH vite per base/fix comparison (never HMR-stash). Candidate causes still unexamined: (1) a glTF asset/child whose baked transform is a true negative-determinant MIRROR (decompose migrates the sign to a different axis → per-axis flip); (2) the gizmo proxy's `rotation` (not scale) when the object/parent carries one the resolver returns; (3) a defect in how `evalT.rotation/scale` is applied vs. drei `space`. The proxy-scale idea is plausible for the glTF path but UNPROVEN — re-test it ON a glTF child before re-attempting.

**Cross-ref:** dharana boundary `B-gizmo` (the gizmo↔evaluated-scene boundary, RESOLVED for the perf-edit case [[H48]] but NOT for this visual case — reopen it), [[H40]] (displayed≠rendered gizmo class — same boundary, different surface), the resolver `resolveEvaluatedTransform.ts` (the ONLY source of the proxy's evaluated scale). Provenance: ORIGIN = user annotated screenshots "the cone/head is pointing in the opposite direction" + "nope its still not fixed", `ux-overhall`, 2026-06-12. WHY = without this entry the next session re-runs the exact plain-box synthetic repro, re-trusts HMR falsification, and re-burns a session on the flaky browser before realizing the probe object is wrong. HOW = reproduce on the user's real glTF object first; headless + fresh-vite for verification; treat moving e2e failures as environmental. REF: `src/app/Gizmo.tsx` (seeding effect — the reverted scale-gate was here), `src/app/resolveEvaluatedTransform.ts:232,284` (the only non-null-scale paths), `node_modules/three/examples/jsm/controls/TransformControls.js:1241` (no camera flip in this version). NO fix committed; Gizmo.tsx reverted to base. NO test (the `ux1-gizmo-proxy-scale.spec.ts` written this session tested the wrong-mechanism plain-box path and was removed).

### H90 — Viewport drill-in (and per-child glTF overrides) match the hit mesh's `.name` against `GltfAsset.nodeNameMap` keys, but on a REAL export the two name spaces DIVERGE (dedup-suffix mismatch + material-split unnamed sub-meshes) so ~28% of meshes are unaddressable — a flat single-child fixture passes while the real model silently no-drills

**Status: RESOLVED — fixed by drilling on a stamped node-INDEX id, not by name (2026-06-14, `c5f18fc`; `fix/ux-friction-4` since fast-forward-merged into `ux-overhall` + pushed). Verified by direct observation on the real cicada: within the import, 374 meshes → 322 directly stamped + 52 via stamped ancestor = 0 orphans (was 273/379 by name); a real-raycast double-click on a named part now selects a GltfChild.**

**The fix (shipped):** the producer's KEY space and three's clone NAME space use different sanitizers + dedup separators (`buildNodeNameMap`: `sanitizeBoneName` + `__n`, `node_i` for unnamed; three `createUniqueName` GLTFLoader.js:3653: `sanitizeNodeName` + `_n`, `''` for unnamed), so name-matching is structurally doomed — UNNAMED nodes can never match at all. The glTF node INDEX is the one correspondence both sides agree on: three records it on `gltf.parser.associations` for EVERY loaded object (GLTFLoader.js:4311), and the import now PERSISTS `keyByGltfNodeIndex` (index → key) on the GltfAsset node (additive `.default({})`, no schema bump). `GltfAssetR` pairs the two via a lockstep original↔clone traversal (SkeletonUtils.clone preserves child array order + deep-copies userData) and stamps each clone object's `userData.basherGltfChildId` (the content-addressed childId is globally unique, so it alone scopes the hit to its asset — no separate asset stamp needed). `buildGltfDrillChain` now walks the hit object's ancestors reading those stamps — a material-split `<unnamed>` leaf resolves to its nearest stamped ancestor (its node Group, which carries a `.nodes` association → is stamped). Name-match retained as a FALLBACK for un-stamped (pre-UX#7) projects → zero regression; also removed the old multi-import name-overlap scoping heuristic. **Two traps the fix had to dodge:** (1) the obvious "stamp where overrides are applied by nodeNameMap key" only stamps the already-matching 273 — it must stamp by INDEX, not by the failing name lookup; (2) the cicada observation's first orphan count scanned the WHOLE scene and counted the starter `n_box`/`n_box_2` primitives — scope the orphan metric to the import subtree (walk a stamped probe up to its top-level scene child).

**FOLLOW-UP — RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (`54c249e`, UX #8 prep):** the per-child TRS + suppression paths in `GltfAssetR` now resolve the clone object by the stamped `userData.basherGltfChildId` (name fallback for pre-UX#7 saves), via the shared pure helper `src/viewport/gltfChildObjects.ts` (`buildChildIdToObject` + `resolveChildObject`). `nodeNameMap[name]` IS the childId (`hashId('gltfChild', assetRef, key)` on both sides), so the by-name lookup that silently dropped ~28% of children on a real export is gone. NOTE: the per-child MATERIAL override path was NOT a by-name bug — it is slot-INDEX based (the i-th isMesh in the override traverse), so it never had the divergence; only TRS + suppression were by name. Gate: `src/viewport/gltfChildObjects.test.ts` (5 unit — by-id resolves a name-divergent child that name-lookup misses; name fallback; undefined when neither). The same `basherGltfChildId` stamp is now also consumed by the UX #8 read-only material readout ([[V44]]).

**Original diagnosis (pre-fix, retained for the lesson):**

**Symptom:** `buildGltfDrillChain` (UX #7) maps a double-clicked sub-mesh to its GltfChild via `state.nodes[assetId].params.nodeNameMap[hitObject.name]`. On the flat fixture (one child "Box") this works end-to-end (e2e green). On the real cicada glb (706 GltfChild nodes / 706 nodeNameMap keys, a CountryLands farm scene — trees/barns/fields) a centre double-click stays on the Group through repeated tries: the chain builder returns null and the onDoubleClick fallback re-selects the whole import.

**Root cause (live headless intel — raycast the loaded clone, dump hit-ancestor names vs map keys):** the clone has 379 meshes but only **273 match a nodeNameMap key** (~72%). TWO independent name-space divergences:
1. **Dedup-suffix sanitization mismatch.** nodeNameMap keys (built at import by `buildGltfImportOps`/`buildNodeNameMap`) dedup as `…_Mat_CountryLands_0_003` (underscore before the suffix), but the SkeletonUtils clone keeps three.js GLTFLoader's OWN dedup `…_Mat_CountryLands_0003` (no underscore). Same node, two names → `nodeNameMap[mesh.name]` misses. This ALSO means per-child TRS/material overrides silently fail to apply to these children (pre-existing, wider than drill).
2. **Material-split sub-meshes are `<unnamed>`.** A glTF node with N primitives becomes N three.js meshes; only the parent carries a name. The diag's unmapped mesh chain was `<unnamed>[Mesh] → <unnamed>[Group] → <unnamed>[Scene]` — NO mapped ancestor, so even walking up to the nearest mapped parent (which the drill chain already does) can't recover an id.

**The trap (why a green e2e lied):** the `multifile/flat` fixture is a SINGLE child whose name round-trips cleanly, so the boundary-pair e2e passes — it samples the one case where the two name spaces happen to agree. Coverage on a flat fixture does NOT exercise dedup-suffixing or material-split, the exact shapes a real export hits. The reusable lesson: **a name-correspondence boundary must be tested on a model that actually exercises name DEDUP and multi-primitive splitting, not a 1-child fixture.** (Sibling of [[H40]] displayed≠rendered: here the producer's id space ≠ the rendered object's name space.)

**The fix (deferred):** stop matching by name. In `GltfAssetR` (`src/viewport/SceneFromDAG.tsx`), where `nameToObject` is built and per-child overrides are applied BY the same nodeNameMap key, ALSO stamp each resolved object `o.userData.basherGltfChildId = nodeNameMap[name]` and `o.userData.basherAssetId = <assetNodeId>`. Then `buildGltfDrillChain` walks the hit object's ancestors reading `userData.basherGltfChildId` (immune to sanitization drift) and `userData.basherAssetId` (also fixes the multi-import asset-scoping heuristic noted on `gltfDrillChain.ts`). For material-split `<unnamed>` leaves, the nearest stamped ancestor is the right drill target. SECONDARY: reconcile the two sanitizers so per-child OVERRIDES land too (the wider pre-existing bug) — but the userData stamp fixes drill independently and is the smaller change.

**Detection signal / next-session protocol:** load the REAL cicada (`~/Documents/CG/models/cicada_-_retro_cartoon_car/scene.glb`, 100MB — stage to `public/` and fetch in-page to dodge the CDP arg bridge; headed renders it, headless SwiftShader also works), then before any click dump `meshNamesInMap / sceneMeshCount` and the ancestor chains of a mapped vs unmapped mesh. Verify the fix by drilling onto a NAMED part (e.g. a tree/barn) AND a material-split part. Cross-ref: [[H40]] (id-space≠render-space boundary), `gltfDrillChain.ts` (the name-match site + the documented scoping heuristic), `GltfAsset.ts` (`nodeNameMap`/`buildNodeNameMap`), `SceneFromDAG.tsx` GltfAssetR `nameToObject`/`childOverridesForAsset` (the override-by-name twin). Provenance: ORIGIN = user "try it on the cicada, try to select a tree" → real model no-drills, 2026-06-13. WHY = without this entry the next session re-trusts the green flat-fixture e2e and ships a drill that silently fails on every real export. HOW = drill by stamped userData id, not by name; test on a model that dedups + material-splits. REF: `src/viewport/gltfDrillChain.ts`, `src/viewport/SceneFromDAG.tsx` (GltfAssetR), `src/nodes/GltfAsset.ts`, `src/app/stores/drillStore.ts`.

### H91 — A control's screen-position/anchor logic encodes the CURRENT chrome geometry as a hidden constant; when the chrome is later relocated, the anchor silently points to the OLD place — no error, just a menu rendered over its own trigger

**Status: pattern (first occurrence; UX-backlog #5, 2026-06-14, `5fd98d1`). Logged now because the chrome is being relocated item-by-item (the v0.6 #4 consolidation moved the toolbar bottom→top; floating-panels #2 will move more surfaces) so this class is LIVE, not hypothetical.**

**Symptom:** a popover/menu spawned from a chrome control opens in the wrong place — over its own trigger, off-screen, or upside-down relative to where the control now sits. The call succeeds, the menu is in the DOM and interactive; it's just visually wrong. #5 instantiation: the "+ Add" menu's anchor was `useAddMenuStore.openAt(r.left, r.top)` with a comment "AddMenu clamps to the viewport edges, so a bottom-pill anchor opens the menu upward automatically." That was TRUE when the FloatingViewportToolbar lived at the viewport BOTTOM. v0.6 #4 W1 moved the pill to `top-4` (top), but the anchor + its clamp (`cy = Math.min(y, innerHeight-320)`) were never revisited → the menu's top-left landed at the button's TOP edge (observed y=89.75) and rendered DOWNWARD over the toolbar row (toolbar bottom y=124), its "ADD" header covering the +Add button. The sibling Assets popover had been updated to `r.bottom + 4` so the two were also inconsistent.

**Root cause:** the anchor math is correct ONLY relative to an unstated assumption about where the chrome physically is. The assumption is invisible — it lives in a constant (`r.top` vs `r.bottom`), a clamp direction, or a now-false comment — and is NOT re-derived when the chrome moves, because the move happens in a DIFFERENT file (the layout/`className`), so nothing forces the anchor to update. A pure-positioning bug has no type error and no test unless a test asserts geometry.

**The trap (why it survives):** moving a surface is a `className`/layout edit that compiles clean and looks done; the anchor lives elsewhere and keeps using stale coordinates. Visual QA on the moved surface itself (does the toolbar look right at the top? yes) does NOT exercise the spawned menus. The stale COMMENT actively misleads ("opens upward automatically" — describing the old world as if current).

**The fix (shipped):** anchor relative to a SEMANTIC reference that travels with the chrome, not an absolute/edge constant. One shared `toolbarMenuAnchor(e)` reads the toolbar element's own rect (`e.currentTarget.closest('[role="toolbar"]').getBoundingClientRect().bottom + 6`) and left-aligns to the button — so "below the toolbar" stays correct wherever the toolbar is. Both Add + Assets consume it (consistency). Gate `tests/e2e/ux5-toolbar-menu-position.spec.ts` asserts each menu's top is ≥ the pill's bottom and left-aligned to its button (falsify by reverting to `r.top` → menu top crosses above the pill bottom).

**Detection signal:** any positioning constant (`r.top`/`r.bottom`, a hardcoded `top:`/`bottom:` px, a `Math.min`/`Math.max` clamp whose DIRECTION assumes "near the bottom/top edge") plus a comment that describes the chrome's location ("bottom pill", "opens upward"). When relocating ANY chrome surface, grep for code that anchors to it and re-derive against the new position; prefer anchoring to the moved element's live rect over an edge constant. Cross-ref: dharana B11 silent-failure (b) "decision was correct at authoring but adjacent chrome evolved → claim now false"; sibling of [[H78]] (stale scope premise) and [[H75]] (chrome control strands state when its precondition lapses) — all three are "chrome evolved, a dependent assumption didn't". Provenance: ORIGIN = user UX-backlog #5 "menus opening from the toolbar are off — position/behaviour" → observed the Add menu rendering over its own button, 2026-06-14. WHY = without this entry the next chrome relocation (floating panels #2) re-ships a misplaced spawned surface diagnosed from scratch. HOW = anchor to the moved element's live rect; geometry-asserting e2e as the gate. REF: `src/app/FloatingViewportToolbar.tsx` (`toolbarMenuAnchor`), `src/app/AddMenu.tsx` (the clamp), `tests/e2e/ux5-toolbar-menu-position.spec.ts`. (The `AssetsPopover.tsx` clamp this originally cited was deleted by UX #6 — the asset Library is now a left-panel tab, not a popover.)

**FOLLOW-UP (UX #5 reopened end-to-end, 2026-06-14) — RESOLVED `4f5ead1`+`ee1f9ed`:** the full menu pass shipped in two more slices after the `5fd98d1` open-position slice. (a) **submenu right-edge overflow** — FIXED by the shared `useFlyoutSide` hook (`src/app/menu/useFlyoutSide.ts`): it measures the trigger container on open and places the panel by preference (open right → flip left → CLAMP to the viewport edge). The CLAMP step was the non-obvious part: the left-aligned menu bar sits too near x=0 for a pure left-flip of a 220px submenu to fit, so flip-only (the naïve `right-full`) was insufficient — observed when the 640w test failed; both call sites (MenuBar `Submenu`, AddMenu `AddMenuGroup`) consume the one hook (V34, [[V45]]). AddMenu's root clamp also gained `Math.max(8,…)` lower bounds on both axes. (b) **behaviour** — FIXED: `MenuBar` now hover-switches (button `onMouseEnter` → switch IFF a menu is already open; first open still needs a click) and supports keyboard nav (`onMenubarKeyDown`: ArrowLeft/Right top-level, ArrowDown/Up/Home/End rove the open panel's ENABLED items — disabled items skipped, e.g. Edit ▸ Undo on a fresh scene). Gates: `tests/e2e/ux5-menu-submenu-edge.spec.ts` + `ux5-menubar-behaviour.spec.ts`. The H91 PATTERN itself (a placement constant encoding hidden chrome geometry) stands — it now has a grounded reusable fix (the flyout hook) for the next chrome relocation. Remaining minor follow-ups (not observed in use): submenu VERTICAL overflow near the bottom is unclamped (horizontal only); `ProjectsMenu.tsx` is dead code superseded by File ▸ Switch Project.

---

## H92 — A drei `<Environment>` from an OPFS blob URL silently fails the loader pick + skips PMREM; the texture must carry `EquirectangularReflectionMapping` and be passed as `map=`, not `files=`

**Symptom (would-be, AVOIDED by grounding):** an imported `.hdr`/`.exr` set as `<Environment files={blobUrl}>` either throws (no loader matched) or renders no lighting — because drei's `useEnvironment` picks RGBELoader/EXRLoader by the file EXTENSION of `files`, and an OPFS `URL.createObjectURL(blob)` has NO extension (`blob:http://…/uuid`). Separately, the `map=` path's `setEnvProps` assigns `scene.environment = texture` DIRECTLY — it does NOT run a PMREMGenerator — so an env texture handed in without `mapping = EquirectangularReflectionMapping` is not treated as an env map.

**Root cause:** two distinct drei behaviours at the same boundary. (1) loader selection is extension-driven (`Environment.js` → `useEnvironment` reads `files.split('.').pop()`); a blob URL defeats it. (2) the `EnvironmentMap` (`map=`) branch is a thin `setEnvProps(... map ...)` that sets the scene property verbatim and relies on three's built-in equirect env processing, which is gated on the texture's `.mapping`.

**The trap (the wrong fix):** pass the OPFS blob URL to `files=` and add an `extensions`/`encoding` guess, or assume drei PMREM-prefilters whatever you give `map=`. Both leave you debugging a black scene with no error.

**The real fix:** decode the bytes YOURSELF (RGBELoader/EXRLoader by the STORED extension, which you know from the assetRef path — not the blob URL), set `texture.mapping = THREE.EquirectangularReflectionMapping`, and hand it to `<Environment map={texture}>`. PMREM for the equirect map happens at render inside three. Presets (`<Environment preset=…>`) are unaffected — they go through `EnvironmentCube`/`useEnvironment` which loads + PMREMs a known asset.

**Detection signal:** an env/IBL feature that "binds" (you can log `scene.environment` non-null) but produces no lighting, OR a loader error mentioning an unmatched extension while the asset is sourced from `URL.createObjectURL`. Any time you feed a Texture you decoded to drei `<Environment map>`, check `.mapping`.

**Provenance:** ORIGIN = UX-backlog #9 (scene HDRI/IBL), 2026-06-15 — caught at design time by READING drei `Environment.js`/`setEnvProps` (Grounding check) BEFORE wiring, not by failing. WHY = the next person wiring an env texture (or a reflection probe, or a background-only skybox) from OPFS will reach for `files=` first; this entry routes them to `map=` + the mapping. HOW = decode in `envHdriStore.loadEnvHdri` (sets `EquirectangularReflectionMapping`), render via `EnvironmentFile.tsx` (`map=`). Sibling of [[V47]] (the env invariant). REF: `src/app/asset/envHdriStore.ts:loadEnvHdri`, `src/viewport/EnvironmentFile.tsx`, `node_modules/@react-three/drei/core/Environment.js` (`setEnvProps`, `EnvironmentMap`, `useEnvironment`).

---

## H93 — A glTF/texture fixture named "textured" is NOT necessarily BASE-COLOR textured; a `none` result from a map resolver is the FIXTURE's data, not always the consumer's bug

**The trap:** while building the UV-editor texture backdrop (UX-BACKLOG #10), the `__basher_uv_texture` seam returned `status: 'none', hasImage: false` for `public/assets/two-material-textured-quad.gltf` — a fixture whose very name says "textured." The reflex is "my resolver is broken: it's not finding the map." The actual cause: that fixture binds its one texture to BlueMat's `metallicRoughnessTexture`, NOT to any material's `baseColorTexture` — so in three.js it becomes a `metalnessMap`/`roughnessMap`, and `material.map` (base color) is correctly null. The resolver was right; the fixture had no base-color map to find.

**The wrong fix (what the trap pulls you toward):** start patching `firstBaseColorMap` / `isDrawable` / the traversal, suspecting an image-type or material-array bug — chasing a phantom in correct code.

**The real fix / discipline:** when a producer/fixture yields a surprising EMPTY, OBSERVE THE SOURCE DATA before suspecting the consumer (Lokayata at the boundary). Here: a 10-line eval dumping every clone mesh's `material.map`/`.image` type showed `hasMap:false` on RedMat — then `python3 -c` over the glTF JSON showed the texture is on `metallicRoughnessTexture`. Two minutes of looking at the actual bytes beat an hour of editing correct code. There are SIX map slots (base/normal/roughness/metallic/emissive/ao); "has a texture" says nothing about WHICH slot. The cure for the fixture gap was a NEW purpose-built fixture (`albedo-textured-quad.gltf`) with a real, asymmetric `baseColorTexture` — which then both proved the feature AND verified the flipY orientation.

**Detection signal:** a map/texture/material resolver returns empty/null/`none` for an asset you "know" is textured, and your first instinct is to edit the resolver. STOP — dump the resolved render object's actual material fields (and/or the source file's material JSON) first. The slot you want may simply not be bound.

**Provenance:** ORIGIN = UX-backlog #10 (UV texture backdrop), 2026-06-15 — the first observation cycle on the existing "textured" fixture returned `none`; the debug dump (clone material.map = false) + glTF JSON read located the cause in the fixture, not the code, in one cycle. WHY = every future texture-slot feature (normal-map preview, roughness inspect, an atlas picker) will hit a fixture/asset that binds a different slot than the one being read; this routes the next person to inspect source data before editing a correct consumer. HOW = inspect `mesh.material.<slot>` on the render clone + the glTF `materials[].pbrMetallicRoughness` bindings before touching the resolver. Sibling of [[H40]] (boundary-pair: observe BOTH sides), [[V48]] (the resolver this was building). REF: `public/assets/two-material-textured-quad.gltf` (the misleading fixture), `public/assets/albedo-textured-quad.gltf` (the purpose-built one), `src/app/resolveMeshTexture.ts`.

---

## H94 — A drag handler on an `<svg width=W height=H>` that is CSS-stretched to its container must convert client px → svg units by the live rect scale; using raw `clientX-rect.left` flakes until the ResizeObserver commits the real size

**The trap:** `EditableCurve` (UX #11 curve editor) renders `<svg width={w} height={h} className="absolute inset-0">` where `w/h` come from a `useState` measured by a ResizeObserver (default `{600,200}` until it fires). `absolute inset-0` makes CSS STRETCH the svg element to the container, but the svg's internal coordinate system stays `w×h` units. So a keyframe dot at `cx=timeToX(t)` (svg units) renders at a REAL pixel = `cx × (rect.width / w)`. Playwright's `boundingBox()` reports that real pixel; the test `mouse.move`s there; but the drag handler did `px = clientX - rect.left` (real px) and fed it to `xToTime` which divides by `w` (svg units). When `w !== rect.width` (the window before the ResizeObserver commits, OR any container whose width ≠ 600), the forward render and the inverse drag used different scales → the dot didn't follow the cursor → intermittent e2e failures (drag-up "didn't raise the value", "tracks didn't render", ~1 in 4 under load).

**The wrong fix (what the flake pulls you toward):** add `waitForTimeout`s, retries, or `--retries=1` to "stabilize" the drag test — papering over a real coordinate bug with timing. The test isn't flaky; the math is wrong whenever measure-timing or container size makes svg-units ≠ real-px.

**The real fix:** convert client pixels to svg units by the LIVE scale inside the handler: `px = (clientX - rect.left) * (w / rect.width)`, `py = (clientY - rect.top) * (h / rect.height)`. Now forward (render in svg units, CSS-stretched) and inverse (real-px → svg units) use the same scale, so the drag lands under the cursor regardless of whether `size` is still the default or has been measured. (Alternative: a `viewBox` + a getScreenCTM inverse — same idea, the rect-scale conversion is the lightweight version for a stretched svg.)

**Detection signal:** an SVG/canvas drag interaction that works "sometimes" or only at one window size; the dragged element lags/leads the cursor; a pointer-drag e2e that flakes under parallel load. Ask: "is the element's coordinate system the SAME scale as the client pixels I'm reading?" For a CSS-stretched `<svg>` with width/height attrs, it is NOT.

**Provenance:** ORIGIN = UX-backlog #11 slice 2b (drag bézier handles), 2026-06-15 — the keyframe-drag + handle-drag e2e flaked ~1/4 under back-to-back load; root-caused to the svg-unit↔real-px scale mismatch in the before-measure window, NOT timing. WHY = every future canvas/svg editor drag (dopesheet keyframe drag, the planned unified timeline canvas, gizmo-in-2D) will hit this the moment the drawing surface is stretched or measured async; this routes the next author to the scale conversion instead of a retry hack. HOW = `EditableCurve.onPointerMove` converts via `w/rect.width`, `h/rect.height`. Sibling of [[H40]] (observe both sides — here the render side vs the pointer side), [[V49]] (the editor this was building).
