REF: `src/timeline/EditableCurve.tsx` (onPointerMove scale conversion), `tests/e2e/ux11-curve-editor.spec.ts`.

## H95 — A canvas/SVG-drag e2e MIRRORS the component's geometry constants (gutter, diamond, row-height, ruler offset); change the component geometry and N specs silently target the wrong pixel until updated in lockstep

**The trap:** `TimelineCanvas` paints onto a 2D `<canvas>` with NO per-keyframe DOM (D-W9-4 forbids pixel-diffing per element), so the e2e that drag a diamond CANNOT `getByTestId` it — they recompute the diamond's pixel from a COPY of the component's geometry constants (`LABEL_GUTTER`, `DIAMOND`, `INSET`, `RULER_H`) and a copy of `keyframeToRect`'s math (`p7.1-keyframe-retime.spec.ts:39-55 diamondCx`; `p7.12-editable-imported-clips.spec.ts:70-72 + localY`). When UX #11 changed the dopesheet geometry (gutter 128→84, diamond 8→10, added a 17px ruler offset to every row's y), those mirrored constants went stale: the test computed a startX/startY a few px off the real diamond, the drag started in empty space (or the ruler band), and the assertion failed — `p7.1` "moved.value undefined", `p7.12` "rotation clip row not found"/no delta. Not a regression in the feature — the TEST's hard-coded geometry no longer matched the component's.

**The wrong fix:** widen the hit-slop, add retries, or loosen the drop-time tolerance to "make the drag land" — masks the constant drift and the NEXT geometry change silently mis-targets again.

**The real fix:** when changing any TimelineCanvas geometry constant, grep the e2e for its mirror and update ALL of them in the SAME commit (`grep -rn "LABEL_GUTTER\|DIAMOND\|ROW_HEIGHT\|RULER\|diamondCx\|localY" tests/e2e`). Keep the test's derivation a faithful copy of the component's mapping (the tests comment "the SAME math keyframeToRect uses"). Better still (deferred): export ONE geometry helper the tests IMPORT instead of mirror — then a constant change can't drift (the [[V50]] `timelineView` module is that shape; p7.12 already imports the real `keyframeToRect`/`appendSelectionClipRows`, which is why its *math* didn't drift — only its constant copies did).

**Detection signal:** after a canvas/svg layout change, a drag e2e fails with "element not found at computed coords" / "value unchanged" / "row not found" while the feature works by hand; the spec has a `const LABEL_GUTTER = …` or a `diamondCx`/`localY` helper duplicating component math. Ask: "does this spec hard-copy the geometry I just changed?"

**Provenance:** ORIGIN = UX #11 slice 1 (reze-fidelity dopesheet), 2026-06-15 — p7.1 then p7.12 went red the moment the gutter/diamond/ruler changed; root cause = the specs mirror the constants, not import them. Recurs every TimelineCanvas geometry change (slice 1 hit 2 specs across the gutter+diamond+ruler change). WHY = without this, the next dopesheet layout tweak burns a debug cycle re-discovering that the test, not the code, is stale; routes the author straight to the grep + lockstep update. HOW = mirrored constants live in `p7.1-keyframe-retime.spec.ts` + `p7.12-editable-imported-clips.spec.ts`; the durable cure is importing a shared geometry/`timelineView` helper. Sibling of [[H94]] (the other canvas-drag-coordinate trap — that one is render↔pointer scale; this one is component↔test constant drift), cross-ref [[V50]] (the shared view module that, if tests import it, dissolves this trap). REF: `tests/e2e/p7.1-keyframe-retime.spec.ts`, `tests/e2e/p7.12-editable-imported-clips.spec.ts`, `src/timeline/TimelineCanvas.tsx` (the constants), `src/timeline/timelineView.ts`.

## H96 — Viewport post-processing silently does nothing: an overlay component (drei `<GizmoHelper>`/`<Hud renderPriority=1>`) re-renders the RAW main scene over the EffectComposer every frame

**Symptom:** SMAA/ACES/DoF (any `<EffectComposer>` effect) appear to have no effect in the live viewport — the scene renders, orbits, looks fine, but the beauty pass never shows. No console error. Pixel tests written against the (accidentally) raw viewport pass; a "PostFx beauty matches reference" test fails.

**Root cause (Basher, found 2026-06-15):** drei's `<GizmoHelper>` (bottom-right orientation gizmo) mounts drei's `<Hud renderPriority=1>` internally. The Hud's priority-1 frame does `gl.autoClear = true; gl.render(defaultScene, defaultCamera)` — it renders the RAW main scene itself (so its gizmo overlay has a backdrop), THEN overlays the gizmo. Because R3F runs priority subscribers in ascending order and the Hud's main render runs at/after the composer's, the raw render OVERWRITES the composer output. Net: the composer's effects never reach the screen. (Compounding it here, drei's own `<EffectComposer>` built ZERO EffectPasses — it reads effects from `group.current.__r3f.objects`, which resolved empty in this fiber/drei/postprocessing combo — so even without the Hud, nothing composited. Both had to be fixed.)

**Detection signal:** in a `useFrame`, log `state.internal.priority` and `state.internal.subscribers.map(s=>s.priority)`. More than one positive-priority subscriber, and the "extra" one's source is `gl.render(defaultScene, defaultCamera)` → a second main-scene renderer. Also: render NOTHING in your composer's frame and orbit — if the scene still updates live, another renderer owns the frame.

**The trap (wrong fixes that don't work):** swapping `focusDistance`↔`worldFocusDistance` on the DoF effect (the params were never the issue); rewriting the composer drei→imperative ALONE (still overwritten by the Hud); bumping the composer's priority without addressing the Hud. The dep-bundle is also a diagnosis trap: Vite serves a CACHED optimized `@react-three/postprocessing` bundle, so patching `node_modules` to add probes shows stale behaviour — probe your OWN source instead.

**The real fix:** ONE component owns the main-scene render ([[V52]]). PostFx drives an imperative EffectComposer at `useFrame(cb, 1)`; the gizmo overlays via `<GizmoHelper renderPriority={2}>` (at priority ≠ 1 the Hud skips its main-scene render and only draws the gizmo, clearing depth only). REF: `src/render/PostFx.tsx`, `src/viewport/Viewport.tsx`, drei `core/Hud.js:18` (`if (renderPriority === 1)`), R3F `internal.priority` render gate. Branch `ux-overhall`.

## H97 — A `useEffect`/`useMemo` dependency written with the WRONG identifier passes tsc yet is a SILENT no-op; eslint's exhaustive-deps "outer scope value" warning is the tell

**Symptom:** a hook reads a value (e.g. `depNodeMap[childId]`) but a typo'd/wrong name (`depNodesById`) is used; the feature appears wired (compiles, types check) but does NOTHING at runtime — the effect never re-runs on the real value's change, or reads `undefined`. No type error, no runtime throw.

**Root cause (Basher, #178 S3, 2026-06-16):** the glTF-material overlay effect referenced `depNodesById` — a name defined NOWHERE in the file (the real memo is `depNodeMap`). `npx tsc --noEmit` returned 0 (a stale incremental `.tsbuildinfo` cache; an undefined name should error — re-run after deleting the cache to confirm). The reference resolved to an outer/global `any`, so the overlay silently no-op'd and the effect's dep array gained a phantom value.

**Detection signal:** eslint `react-hooks/exhaustive-deps` fired: *"Outer scope values like 'depNodesById' aren't valid dependencies because mutating them doesn't re-render the component."* For a value you BELIEVE is a local `useMemo`/`useState`, that exact phrase means the identifier is NOT what you think — it resolved to module/outer scope (wrong name, or a real global). Treat it as a correctness alarm, not a style nit.

**The trap (wrong reactions):** suppressing the exhaustive-deps warning (`// eslint-disable`) to "make it pass" — that buries a silent no-op; trusting a green `tsc` over eslint here (the incremental cache had hidden the undefined name). 

**The real fix:** grep the identifier across `src/` — if it's defined nowhere local, it's the wrong name; use the actual in-scope memo. Re-run `tsc` after `rm *.tsbuildinfo` to defeat the stale cache. Gate the wiring with a FALSIFIABLE observation that the value actually drives behaviour (the S3 e2e: edit `materials[0].base.color` → the rendered clone must repaint; with the no-op name it never would). REF: `src/viewport/SceneFromDAG.tsx` (`depNodeMap`), `tests/e2e/ux-gltf-material-dag.spec.ts`, commit `b9e6baa`. Branch `ux-overhall`. Lesson: a lint warning that names a *correctness* failure mode outranks a green typecheck — read what the warning actually says.

**S4 sibling (2026-06-16, the SHARED-DEV-SERVER false-green) — a SECOND lying-green of the same family.** During #178 S4, the existing `ux8-gltf-material-inspect` "GltfChild shows readout" test PASSED on the FIRST run right after the NPanel routing change — then FAILED on a clean re-run. Cause: the e2e drives the shared `:5180` dev server (the task's warned shared instance); on the first run HMR had NOT yet applied the NPanel edit, so the test exercised STALE code and the OLD assertion still held. The tell: my change SHOULD have changed that test's outcome (the child now routes to the editor, not the readout), yet it stayed green — a green that contradicts the intended behavioural delta is a stale-build smell, not a pass. Real fix: re-run any regression test whose outcome your change is SUPPOSED to flip; trust only the clean re-run. This is the runtime-cache analogue of the `.tsbuildinfo` stale-cache above (both: a cached artifact serves yesterday's code under today's green). General rule promoted to memory `gltf_materials_openpbr_dag.md`: **a first-run e2e green that should have gone red is suspect — observe the clean re-run.** REF: `tests/e2e/ux8-gltf-material-inspect.spec.ts` (updated to the S4 contract: a child with `materials` now asserts the editor), commit `b0072c9`.

## H98 — A SHARED producer helper bakes in a convention correct for consumer A but WRONG for consumer B in a different coordinate space; a solid-colour / 1×1 test can't reveal it

**Symptom:** an asset built by a shared helper renders subtly wrong only for ONE of its consumers — vertically flipped, mirrored, wrong-handed, washed-out — while the same helper is correct for its original consumer. No error; the artifact loads and displays, just oriented/encoded wrong. A unit/e2e using a degenerate fixture (1×1, solid colour, symmetric mesh) passes because the defect is invisible at that resolution.

**Root cause (Basher, #178 S5, 2026-06-16):** `attachMapFromFile` stamps `flipY=true` — the image-UPLOAD orientation correct for native Box/Sphere (three's default geometry UVs). S5 reused it to bake a REPLACEMENT texture for a glTF mesh, whose UVs are authored for the glTF convention (`flipY=false`, what GLTFLoader sets on the imported textures the replacement sits beside on the SAME UVs). So a real replacement texture would render upside-down. The 1×1 red e2e fixture could not reveal it (a solid colour has no orientation).

**Detection signal:** a shared baker / loader / converter consumed by ≥2 surfaces, where one surface lives in a different coordinate space (UV origin, color space, winding, axis order, units). Ask: "this helper encodes a convention (flipY / colorSpace / wrap / handedness) — is that convention the SAME for THIS consumer, or did I inherit the other consumer's default?" The test trap: a degenerate fixture (1×1, solid, symmetric, identity) hides every orientation/encoding defect — so a green test on such a fixture proves nothing about convention.

**The trap (wrong reactions):** trusting a passing 1×1/solid-colour test as proof the map "works"; re-baking with a different flip on the SOURCE bytes (double-work + still wrong for the other consumer) instead of correcting the per-consumer METADATA.

**The real fix:** correct the convention at the CONSUMER boundary, as metadata, not by re-encoding bytes — override `flipY=false` on the BakedTextureRef before committing it for a glTF slot (`loadBakedTexture` restores flipY from the ref, so the overlay applies it right). Deductively: the replacement sits on the SAME UVs as the imported texture it replaces → it must carry the SAME orientation. To OBSERVE convention bugs, the fixture must be ASYMMETRIC (a non-1×1, non-solid texture; an L-shaped / lettered image) — a degenerate fixture is blind to them. REF: `src/app/NPanel.tsx` (`GltfMapRow.onPick` → `{...ref, flipY:false}`), `src/app/material/attachMapFromFile.ts` (the flipY=true upload default), commit `3184eaf`. Branch `ux-overhall`. Sibling of [[V44]] (a re-derived value diverges across a producer/consumer boundary) and [[H40]] (verify the CONSUMER side, not just the producer). Lesson: a shared helper's defaults are part of ITS consumer's contract — re-using it imports those defaults; verify each one fits the new consumer's coordinate space, and test with an asymmetric fixture.

**Second occurrence (2026-06-16, #178 S6 Part A — the SAME degenerate-fixture trap, a producer/consumer KEY-SHAPE mismatch + an H77 leak).** The `.basher` bundle silently dropped EVERY baked texture (glTF map edits, BakedMesh maps, primitive maps). `collectAssetRefs` collected the FULL `BakedTextureRef.hash` — which carries the extension (`<hash>.<ext>`, e.g. `7b7cb53d.png`, what `persistTexture` stamps) — into `bakedTextureHashes`, but `resolveAssetFiles` built its OPFS-file lookup map keyed by the BARE hash (stripping the ext off each dir child) and then looked up by the ext-BEARING ref hash → permanent MISS → the file was never embedded. No error: the bundle wrote, opened, and rendered mapless. **Why it shipped:** the `collectAssetRefs` unit fixture used a degenerate BARE `'deadbeef'` hash that never matched the real `<hash>.<ext>` shape (the SAME degenerate-fixture blindness as the flipY case — a fixture that can't exhibit the convention can't reveal its violation), AND `resolveAssetFiles` (the side where the two shapes must agree) had ZERO unit coverage. The two halves of one mechanism — the COLLECT side (emits the ref hash) and the RESOLVE side (matches it to a file) — disagreed on the key shape, and no test exercised the realistic shape end-to-end. **Real fix:** key the resolve lookup by BOTH the full OPFS filename AND the bare hash (`src/app/sceneBundle.ts`), so the current ext-bearing refs match via the filename while a legacy bare-hash ref still resolves via the dir listing; updated the collect fixture to the real `<hash>.<ext>` + a cleared-sentinel case; added `resolveAssetFiles` unit coverage; added e2e `ux-gltf-material-bundle-roundtrip.spec.ts` (import → edit + replace + clear → export → DELETE the OPFS bytes → open → all survive + clone repaints — the V41/H77 portability falsifier). **Detection signal (reusable):** when one mechanism has a PRODUCER half that emits an identifier and a CONSUMER half that matches it, assert they agree on the EXACT key shape (ext present? prefix? case?) with a REALISTIC fixture — a synthetic id that omits the production-side decoration (here, the extension) passes the producer test and the consumer test independently while the JOIN between them is broken. This is also an [[H77]] instance (a "portable" bundle silently dropping a referenced asset) — the leak V41/H77 exists to forbid, re-opened by an untested resolve path. REF: `src/app/sceneBundle.ts` (`resolveAssetFiles` dual-key), `src/app/sceneBundle.test.ts`, `src/app/asset/bakedTextureStore.ts:188` (the `<hash>.<ext>` ref shape), `tests/e2e/ux-gltf-material-bundle-roundtrip.spec.ts`, commit `9e321a5`. Cross-ref [[H77]] (substrate leak), [[V41]] (the complete-span bundle invariant this restores), [[V53]] (glTF material serialization).

## H99 — A per-iteration allocation that is fine ONE-SHOT crashes the context when LOOPED; observe at scale, and reuse the heavy buffers across iterations

**Symptom:** an action that works perfectly as a single shot (a still render, one export, one decode) crashes the page — "Target page closed", a lost WebGL context, an OOM, no JS error — when the SAME work is run in a loop (every animation frame, every batch row). The crash is FRAME-COUNT-dependent, not size-dependent: a few iterations succeed, dozens crash, and shrinking each iteration's payload does NOT help (so it's not one big allocation — it's many).

**Root cause (Basher, #189 render animation, 2026-06-16):** `renderSceneToImageCanvas` (the #168 still) allocated, per call, a 1920×1080 MSAA `WebGLRenderTarget` + an 8MB readback `Uint8Array` + an 8MB `ImageData` + a 2D canvas. As a one-shot (the still) that's fine — allocate, read, dispose. The animation render called it PER FRAME in a tight loop; the per-frame GPU target churn + JS heap churn exhausted the context. Observed (Lokayata, not inferred): a 4-frame render returned `ok:true` with zero errors; a 31-frame render crashed the page with the playhead barely advanced. Shrinking the render to 320×180 STILL crashed at 31 frames — proving it was the per-iteration allocation count, not the per-frame size.

**Detection signal:** a function written for a single invocation (allocates + uses + disposes a heavy GPU/heap resource internally) is newly called inside a loop. Ask: "does each iteration allocate a render target / large typed array / canvas / decoder it then throws away? Over N iterations, is the runtime/GC/GPU expected to reclaim between iterations fast enough?" The tell that it's THIS class: few iterations pass, many crash, and reducing per-iteration size doesn't move the threshold.

**The trap (wrong reactions):** assuming the crash is the per-frame RESOLUTION and lowering it (it isn't — it's the allocation COUNT); assuming it's a memory LEAK and hunting for an undisposed handle (the one-shot already disposes correctly — the problem is churn rate, not a leak); blaming the test environment for "Target page closed" without separating it from the timeout-teardown sibling (see below).

**The real fix:** hoist the heavy allocations OUT of the loop body into a REUSABLE scratch created once and disposed once at the end; the per-iteration function takes the scratch and overwrites it in place (`readRenderTargetPixels(target,…,readBuf)` into the same buffer, `imageData.data.set(...)` into the same ImageData, draw into the same canvas). Keep the one-shot path allocating its own scratch (so the still is unchanged) — pass the scratch only on the looped path. Basher: `createRenderScratch` + `clampRenderSize`, `renderSceneToImageCanvas(opts, scratch?)`, the manual + composer paths read into `scratch.readBuf`; `renderAnimationToFile` creates one scratch for the whole render, disposes in `finally`. Gate: the looped e2e renders N frames to completion without "Target page closed" (`p189-render-animation.spec.ts`), the one-shot still e2e stays green (`p168`).

**Sibling trap — the rAF-throttle TIMEOUT masquerading as the same crash.** In the SAME investigation a SECOND "Target page closed" had a different cause: the per-frame `waitForApply` awaits 2 `requestAnimationFrame`s, but headless chromium THROTTLES rAF on a "hidden" page to ~1/sec, so a long render (601 frames at the default 10s duration) exceeded the 30s Playwright test timeout → the harness tore down the page → "Target page closed", identical surface text to the GPU crash. Disambiguator: the GPU-churn crash fires with FEW iterations at full size and ignores the timeout; the rAF-throttle one is purely a function of total wall-time vs the test timeout and vanishes with a tiny frame count. Fix for the test: keep the e2e frame count small (a real 60fps FOREGROUND browser renders at speed — the throttle is a headless artifact). Lesson: "Target page closed" is a SURFACE, not a cause — separate GPU-resource exhaustion from harness-timeout teardown before fixing. REF: `src/render/renderToImage.ts` (`createRenderScratch`/`clampRenderSize`/`RenderScratch`, the manual+composer reuse), `src/app/renderAnimationAction.ts` (one scratch per render, `waitForApply`), `tests/e2e/p189-render-animation.spec.ts`, commit `3115a11`. Branch `ux-overhall`. Cross-ref [[H68]] (the still's preserve-drawing-buffer blank — same file, sibling render-correctness trap), [[V37]]/[[V51]] (the one-render-path parity the scratch must not break). Sibling of [[H48]] (O(scene) vs O(changed) cost — same "fine once, quadratic/linear-blowup at scale" family, there in eval cost, here in allocation).

---

## H100 — A "gate green" claim carried in memory is INFERENCE; only a fresh `npm run typecheck` on the actual tip is observation — and a passing vitest does NOT imply a passing tsc

**Symptom:** the session/handoff notes say the branch tip is "fully gated — tsc 0 / eslint 0 / vitest N", yet running `npm run typecheck` on that exact (clean, unmodified) tip reports real, deterministic type errors. The committed code never compiled clean; the green claim was assumed, not freshly observed.

**Root cause (Basher, ux-overhall tip `ce6948a`, 2026-06-16):** 5 deterministic tsc errors from the prior session's #189/#178 work were committed under a "tsc 0" memory note (`renderAnimationAction.ts` `severity:'warning'` ∉ ToastSeverity; `const effects = [dofEffect]` inferred `DepthOfFieldEffect[]`; `GltfNode`/`GltfJson` missing `mesh`/`meshes`/`materials`; `params:{}` `.materials` read). Two compounding reasons a prior session can ship a red tsc while believing it green: (1) **vitest ≠ tsc** — vitest transpiles via esbuild, which STRIPS types without checking them, so a fully-green 1601-test run says NOTHING about type correctness; (2) the `tsc 0` line gets copied forward through handoff/memory as a remembered fact rather than re-run each session. (`tsc -b` incremental buildinfo in gitignored `node_modules/.tmp/` was NOT the cause — a fresh `npm run typecheck` caught all 5 on the first run; the masking was process, not tooling.)

**Detection signal:** any session-start handoff that asserts a gate result you did not personally just run. The tell: the claim is about a PAST state ("tip was gated") but you're acting on the PRESENT tip. Also: a green vitest cited as evidence the build is sound.

**The trap (wrong reactions):** trusting the memory note and proceeding to feature work on a red baseline (every subsequent slice's gate is now contaminated — you can't tell your error from the inherited one); assuming a node_modules/TS-version drift and reinstalling (versions matched the lockfile exactly); treating `npm test` green as "the gate passed".

**The real fix:** at session start, before any new work, run the FULL gate fresh on the actual tip — `npm run typecheck && npm run lint && npm run test` (+ prettier) — and treat THAT, not the handoff note, as ground truth. If red, the first slice is "restore green baseline" before picking feature work. Memory/handoff gate claims are leads to verify, not facts to trust (Lokayata: running the gate is observation; reading "gate green" is inference — observation wins). REF: commit `83a7f31` (the baseline-restore fix), `tsconfig.app.json`/`tsconfig.node.json` (`tsBuildInfoFile` → `node_modules/.tmp/`), `package.json` scripts (`typecheck` = `tsc -b --noEmit`, `test` = `vitest run`). Branch `ux-overhall`. Cross-ref [[H97]] (a wrong-identifier dep passes tsc yet is a silent no-op — there tsc is necessary-but-insufficient; here tsc was never consulted) — both say: the gate you didn't run is the gate that fails.

## H101 — Setting `OrbitControls.minDistance/maxDistance` SILENTLY re-frames the camera: the controls dolly the eye to satisfy the limit on the next `update()`, so a "we only touched the clip planes, never the pose" change can still move the view

**Symptom:** a code path that claims to be POSE-PRESERVING (restore a saved orbit view, then only refresh near/far + dolly limits) lands the camera at the right DIRECTION but the WRONG distance. Observed (#191, `ux-overhall`, 2026-06-16): a saved view injected at `[4,3,4]` (dist 6.40) on a 4000-unit box restored as `[21.64,16.23,21.64]` — same direction, dist 34.64 — while `far` was correctly bounds-derived. The eye was ejected straight out along its own view ray.

**Root cause:** the planes-only settle set `controls.minDistance = clipPlanesForView(...).minDistance = max(radius*0.01, …)` = `3464*0.01` = **34.64**, far larger than the restored camera's 6.40 distance to target. OrbitControls enforces `minDistance` by clamping the camera-to-target distance on its next `update()` — so it dollied the eye OUT to 34.64. Setting a dolly LIMIT is not a passive annotation; it is an active constraint OrbitControls applies to the live camera. "I never called `applyView` / never touched `position`" is therefore NOT sufficient to claim the pose is preserved — the limits you set are a second, indirect way to move it.

**Detection signal:** camera lands on the correct view ray (direction matches the intended pose) but at a distance equal to `minDistance` (or `maxDistance`). The far/near planes being CORRECT while the position is wrong is the tell that the planes math is right but a *limit* moved the eye. Diagnosed by reading the live `__basher_view_camera()` position and noticing dist == the radius-derived minDistance.

**The trap (wrong fixes):** re-applying the saved pose every frame in the settle (fights OrbitControls, reintroduces a look-at pin — the very thing #186 V54 rejected); dropping the limit refresh entirely (reopens the stale-limits half of #191); lowering `radius*0.01` globally (breaks the full-fit dolly range for huge models).

**The real fix (`EditorViewCamera.tsx`, #191):** clamp the refreshed limits so they never EXCLUDE the live camera distance — `controls.minDistance = min(planes.minDistance, liveDist)`, `controls.maxDistance = max(planes.maxDistance, liveDist)` where `liveDist = cam.position.distanceTo(center)`. This keeps the restored pose strictly inside `[min,max]` so OrbitControls has nothing to clamp, while still refreshing the limits to bounds-appropriate values. No-op for the full-fit path (the eye sits at the fit distance, already far above `minDistance`), so the clamp can be applied uniformly to both branches. REF: `src/viewport/EditorViewCamera.tsx` (settle `useFrame`, the `controls.minDistance/maxDistance` clamp), `clipPlanesForView` (`cameraFit.ts`), `p191-saved-view-clip-planes.spec.ts`. Cross-ref [[V54]] (the planes-only settle this protects), [[H69]] (the prior camera-boot silent-failure class). General principle: any property a controls/physics system READS each tick to constrain an object is a write-path to that object — verify the object's actual state after setting it (Lokayata), don't assume "I didn't touch X directly" means X is unchanged.

## H102 — An affordance CO-LOCATED in a component deleted for an unrelated reason vanishes as collateral damage; a test still asserting it goes red and `grep` of `src/` finds ZERO references — the tell that the element was deleted-with-its-host, not relocated

**Symptom:** an acceptance e2e asserts a UI element (`getByTestId('camera-view-badge')`) that simply does not exist — `element(s) not found`. The feature it indicates still WORKS (look-through adopts the camera pose), but its visible indicator is gone. The test has been red for many sessions and gets carried forward as a "known pre-existing red" instead of fixed.

**Root cause (Basher #165, 2026-06-16):** the `camera-view-badge` was added in Wave D (`c6e29ec`) INSIDE `src/viewport/ModeBadge.tsx`. Later, `b5af221` ("dissolve the operational mode enum fully") deleted `ModeBadge.tsx` wholesale — that component existed to show the edit/run/animate MODE, an orthogonal concern. The camera-view badge had been parked there for convenience, so deleting the host took the badge with it. Two unrelated affordances shared one file; removing one removed the other. The chrome was restructured several times during the UX overhaul (mode-enum dissolution, then floating-islands), and each restructuring is an opportunity for a co-located affordance to be dropped silently.

**Detection signal:** a failing `getByTestId(X)` where `grep -rn X src/` returns NOTHING (not "it moved" — it's GONE). Contrast with a relocated element (grep finds it under a new path/parent). Confirm via `git log -S "X" --all --diff-filter=D` → the commit that deleted the host file, whose message is about something ELSE entirely (the tell that it was collateral, not intentional). A long-standing "known red" e2e asserting a missing element is the higher-level smell — known-reds accrete exactly these dropped-affordance regressions.

**The trap (wrong reactions):** deleting/skipping the assertion to "make the suite green" (erases the acceptance contract — the affordance was REQUIRED); re-creating the now-deleted host component just to rehome the element (resurrects the orthogonal concern that was correctly removed); placing the restored element back where it used to live (that layout/row no longer exists post-restructuring).

**The real fix (`Viewport.tsx`, #165):** restore the affordance in a CURRENTLY-valid location, decoupled from the deleted host — re-add the `camera-view-badge` as a Viewport overlay gated on `lookThroughCamera`, placed to respect the current layout invariants (top-center, clear of the floating islands, [[V46]]). Subscribe to the state it needs in the component that now owns the surface. REF: `src/viewport/Viewport.tsx` (the lookThrough overlay), `tests/e2e/p165-blender-camera.spec.ts` (Numpad-0 badge assertion). Cross-ref [[H100]] (a "known-green" memory claim is inference) — its sibling: a "known-RED" carried in a handoff is ALSO inference; some known-reds are real dropped-feature regressions, not inert noise. Re-run and triage them, don't inherit them. General principle: when a feature and its indicator live in one file for convenience, a future deletion of that file for one of them silently kills the other — affordances belong with the surface/state they reflect, not parked in a neighbor.

## H103 — An `overflow-hidden` ancestor silently CLIPS a child that's positioned outside its box (a submenu flyout / popover / tooltip opening beyond the container): invisible AND not hit-testable, yet DOM-presence tests stay GREEN — only a real pointer hit-test reveals it

**Symptom:** a flyout/popover that opens OUTSIDE its container (a submenu to the right of a fixed-width menu panel, a tooltip above a clipped row) does not appear and cannot be clicked. The user reports "I click X and nothing happens." Yet the e2e suite is GREEN: `locator.count()===1`, `toBeVisible()` passes, and even Playwright `.click()` (via `.hover()`+`.click()` teleporting) succeeds — so automated tests assert the feature works while real users can't reach it.

**Root cause (Basher menus, 2026-06-17):** the MenuBar `Menu` panel had `overflow-hidden` (for rounded-corner clipping of the item list) and a fixed `w-[260px]`. Every `Submenu` flyout opens to the RIGHT via `left: 100%` (`useFlyoutSide`), i.e. at the panel's right edge and beyond. `overflow:hidden` clips ALL descendants whose containing block is inside the overflow element — and the flyout's containing block (the `relative` submenu container) is inside the panel, so the flyout does NOT escape. Result: the flyout paints to nothing past the panel edge and is removed from the hit-test region. `document.elementFromPoint(flyoutCenter)` returned `<canvas>` (the 3D viewport behind), so pointer events never reached the flyout, its `onMouseEnter` never fired, and it was both unseen and unclickable. Affected EVERY submenu (the shared panel), which is why "same with any other submenus."

**Detection signal:** the decisive probe is `document.elementFromPoint(cx, cy)` at the element's own center → if it returns an ANCESTOR/sibling/background (not the element or its descendant), the element is occluded or CLIPPED, not reachable. Walk the ancestor chain for `overflow` ∈ {hidden, clip, auto, scroll} while the child's bounding box lies outside that ancestor's padding box. `getBoundingClientRect` reporting a sane on-screen rect does NOT mean the element is visible — rect ignores ancestor overflow clipping. The tell that a passing test is FALSE-GREEN here: it asserts `count`/`toBeVisible`/`.click()` (DOM presence + Playwright actionability, neither of which models ancestor overflow clipping) instead of a real pointer hit-test or a human/screenshot.

**The trap (wrong reactions / treating symptoms):** I first chased the secondary bugs — a click-toggle that closed the flyout, and a missing hover close-delay (the seam between trigger and flyout). Both were REAL and worth fixing, but neither was why the flyout was invisible; fixing only them would have left it clipped. The lesson: when an element is unreachable, FIRST confirm it is hit-testable (`elementFromPoint`) before theorizing about event handlers/timing — a clipped element makes all hover/click logic moot.

**The real fix (`MenuBar.tsx`):** `overflow-hidden` → `overflow-visible` on the menu panel (and the submenu flyout, for nested cases) so the flyout escapes the clip — it now paints and hit-tests to its own item. Keep the secondary fixes too (click OPENS not toggles; 300ms close-delay cancelled on flyout re-entry) — they make the now-reachable flyout pleasant to use. REF: `src/app/MenuBar.tsx` (Menu panel + Submenu flyout `overflow-visible`, `SUBMENU_CLOSE_DELAY_MS`, onClick openNow), `src/app/menu/useFlyoutSide.ts` (the `left:100%` placement that opens beyond the panel), `tests/e2e/ux5-submenu-reachable.spec.ts` (real-pointer regression). Cross-ref [[H102]] / [[H100]] (the false-green family: a test that passes while the real artifact is broken — here DOM-presence vs pointer-reachability). General principle: a popover/tooltip/menu that must extend beyond its parent CANNOT live inside an `overflow:hidden` ancestor — either remove the clip on that chain or portal the popover out; and verify reachability with `elementFromPoint`, never with bounding-box presence.

## H104 — A node type whose inspector is a CUSTOM control (not generic ParamRows) silently bypasses the shared keyframe diamond + autoKey routing; its params are NON-animatable even when the channel/resolver machinery fully supports them

**Symptom:** you wire up animation for a param (resolver overlays it, render + viewport follow it, the keyframe machinery is in place), and an e2e that clicks the inspector keyframe diamond fails with `getByTestId('inspector-diamond-<node>-<param>')` → element not found. The param genuinely cannot be keyed from the UI even though everything downstream works. (#190: camera `fov` — the resolver + viewport follow were done, but the fov diamond didn't exist.)

**Root cause (Basher, 2026-06-17):** the generic inspector renders a `ParamDiamond` per `NumericField`/`VectorComponent` AND routes value commits through `routeAnimatedGrab`→`autoKeyCommit` — so MOST node params are animatable for free. But some node types route their section to a **custom control** instead of raw ParamRows: `NPanel.tsx` suppresses the generic rows for `sectionId==='camera'` (→ `CameraLensControls`) and `'environment'` (→ `SceneEnvironmentControls`). Those custom controls dispatch `setParam` DIRECTLY (no diamond, no autoKey). So a camera's fov/near/far had no keying affordance at all, while position/lookAt (the `transform` section, still generic ParamRows) did. The diamond's mere existence on generic fields hides this: you assume "all params get a diamond," but a custom-control section is a silent exception.

**Detection signal:** `grep -n "sectionId === '<section>'" src/app/NPanel.tsx` returning a custom control component (and `? null` suppressing `grouped.get(sectionId)`) → that section's params do NOT get the generic diamond/autoKey. The failing-diamond e2e + a `grep -rn inspector-diamond-<node>-<param>` that finds the testid only for OTHER sections confirms it.

**The trap (wrong reactions):** assuming the diamond is missing because of a collapsed section or a selection bug (it's neither — the field is a custom control with no diamond at all); adding the diamond import into the custom control via the file that RENDERS it (`NPanel` renders `CameraLensControls`) → a circular import (NPanel↔control). 

**The real fix (#190):** extract the shared affordance (`ParamDiamond`) into its own module so any control can render it without an import cycle, then wire the custom control to the SAME spine the generic fields use — render `<ParamDiamond>` per keyable field + route its commits through `routeAnimatedGrab`→`setParam`→`autoKeyCommit` (a small `commitParam` helper). REF: `src/app/ParamDiamond.tsx` (extracted), `src/app/CameraLensControls.tsx` (diamonds + commitParam for fov/near/far), `src/app/NPanel.tsx:~1817` (the custom-control suppression). General principle: when a node type opts OUT of the generic inspector rows, it also opts out of every cross-cutting affordance those rows carry (keyframing, override decorators, read-only-while-playing) — re-wire each one explicitly into the custom control, or it's silently absent.

**SECOND occurrence (#188, v0.7 Phase 3, 2026-06-17) — `GltfMaterialEditor`.** The glTF material editor (`NPanel.tsx`) is the OTHER custom inspector control (it renders OpenPBR lobe rows, not generic ParamRows), so it had the SAME silent gap: glTF material scalars animated by the resolver (the new per-frame overlay) had no keying affordance. Fixed by the SAME template: render a `ParamDiamond` per lobe field (`paramPath = materials.<slot>.<lobe>.<field>`, value = current) + make the editor's `commit` autoKey-aware (route an ANIMATED field through `routeAnimatedGrab` and SKIP the whole-`materials`-array `setParam` — H36 single-write: the channel owns the value; an un-animated field keeps the whole-array replace + `autoKeyCommit` first-key). The field components (`GltfMatNumberField`/`GltfMatColorField`) gained a `diamond` slot. NOT a new H-entry — the SAME H104 class, now with TWO catalogued custom-control consumers (CameraLensControls + GltfMaterialEditor). The detection signal recurred exactly: the first-key path (`dispatchFirstKeyComposite`) also needed a node-specific branch (GltfChild is not a scene producer → free-floating channel, not addLayer — the camera precedent, generalized to `dispatchDirectFirstKey`). REF (#188): `src/app/NPanel.tsx` (GltfMaterialEditor diamonds + commit), `src/app/animate/dispatchMutator.ts` (`dispatchDirectFirstKey` GltfChild branch), `tests/e2e/p188-gltf-material-authoring.spec.ts`, [[V57]] (the direct-channel road), [[V53]] (the material IR).

**THIRD occurrence + the structural FIX (#198, v0.7 Phase 4, 2026-06-17) — converge the two custom material editors so the affordance is wired ONCE.** #190+#188 fixed H104 by re-wiring the diamond/autoKey spine into EACH custom control by hand (CameraLensControls, then GltfMaterialEditor) — two copies of the same wiring, plus a THIRD cross-cutting affordance (the [[H40]] evaluated read-side / read-only-while-playing) was STILL absent on BOTH material editors (the field showed the static base while the viewport animated). The Phase-4 convergence is the general remedy to the H104 class for materials: extract ONE shared `MaterialRows` (the OpenPBR lobe rows) that BOTH the native `MaterialEditor` and the glTF `GltfMaterialEditor` render; MaterialRows wires the diamond + Auto-Key chokepoint (`routeAnimatedGrab`→caller `commitSource`→`autoKeyCommit`) + the evaluated read-side (`resolveEvaluatedParam` → `effective = resolved ?? authored` + read-only-while-playing) ONCE, and each caller supplies only the closures that genuinely differ (`fieldPath`/`readValue`/`commitSource`/`testids`). The bespoke per-editor field components (`ColorField`/`GltfMatColorField`/`GltfMatNumberField`) are deleted. GENERAL LESSON sharpened: when N node types share a custom-control inspector for the SAME underlying data (here: one OpenPBR material IR, [[V53]]), do NOT re-wire each cross-cutting affordance per control — extract the shared rows so the diamond/autoKey/read-side spine has ONE home; the convergence both fixes the present gap AND prevents the next affordance from being added N times. REF (#198): `src/app/NPanel.tsx` (`MaterialRows`/`MaterialNumberRow`/`MaterialColorRow`), `src/app/resolveEvaluatedParam.ts` (the read-side, now a material consumer too), [[V57]] #198 enforcement, [[H40]] (the read-side gap this closes for both editors). The camera (`CameraLensControls`, #194) is the remaining custom control whose read-side is still static — it reuses this exact `resolveEvaluatedParam` template when closed.

**FOURTH occurrence + H104 CLOSED (#194, v0.7 unification follow-up, 2026-06-18) — `CameraLensControls` read-side, the LAST custom-control instance.** The camera authoring spine (diamond + autoKey via `commitParam`) was already wired in #190 (the FIRST occurrence's fix), but its READ side stayed static: `CameraLensControls` read `node.params.fov/near/far` directly, so during playback/scrub the focal-length / field-of-view / near / far fields froze at the authored value while the look-through render followed the keyed channel (`resolveActiveCameraPoseAt`, [[V56]]) — the [[H40]] displayed≠rendered half of H104, the same gap #198 closed for the two material editors. Fixed by the SAME `resolveEvaluatedParam` template the #198 `MaterialRows` use: subscribe `CameraLensControls` to the time store, resolve the animatable scalars (fov/near/far) per-node through `resolveEvaluatedParam` (its channel `.sample()` bottoms out in the SAME `sampleScalarKeyframes` as `resolveActiveCameraPoseAt`, so inspector == look-through — verified by reading `KeyframeChannelNumber.evaluate().sample` before choosing the resolver), display `effective = resolved?.value ?? authored`, gate `readOnly = playing && resolved !== null`. Because `resolveEvaluatedParam` layer-1 is the transient, the held-transient preview comes for FREE (no extra work). The camera is NOT a material so it did NOT converge into `MaterialRows` — but it consumes the identical read-side helper, so there is ONE evaluated-read mechanism (`resolveEvaluatedParam`) across every custom control. With this, H104 is CLOSED: all custom-control inspectors (camera + both material editors + environment is not animatable) carry the full diamond/autoKey/evaluated-read/read-only-while-playing spine. REF (#194): `src/app/CameraLensControls.tsx` (evaluated read + readOnly gates), `src/app/resolveEvaluatedParam.ts` (now a camera consumer too), `tests/e2e/p194-camera-read-side.spec.ts` (the read==render boundary-pair). NOTE (resolved #200, 2026-06-18, commit `2169e88`): the read-side equality holds because both paths sort+sample the same keyframes. Originally `resolveActiveCameraPoseAt`'s SCALAR branch read `params.keyframes` UN-sorted while `resolveEvaluatedParam`'s evaluate sorts defensively, so agreement was only guaranteed for in-time-order keyframes (always true via the ops; an out-of-order injection would diverge). #200 closed that latent gap: the scalar branch now sorts before `sampleScalarKeyframes` (matching `KeyframeChannelNumber.evaluate`; the vec3 branch already sorted via `buildVec3Sampler`). The two surfaces now agree for ANY keyframe order — gated by a falsifiable unit test (`activeCamera.test.ts`, out-of-order fov keys → correct interpolation).

## H105 — A channel wired into an `AnimationLayer.animation` socket ALSO carries `params.target === <wrapped node>`, so a NEW by-target "direct channel" enumerator silently double-overlays that node (the layer path applies it AND the direct path applies it) unless it excludes layer-wired channels

**Root cause:** the v0.7 unification (#197) adds a direct-channel road — a free-floating `KeyframeChannel*` found by scanning `params.target === nodeId`, overlaid by `overlayChannels`. But `addChannel` (the legacy layer path) sets the SAME `params.target` to the wrapped node when it wires the channel into a layer's `animation` socket (so the read-side `resolveChannel`/`paramAnimationState` can find it by target). So a naive by-target scan picks up BOTH free-floating channels AND layer-wired ones. During coexistence (before the Phase-5 retirement) a layer-wired channel would then be applied TWICE: once by `AnimationLayerR` (via the layer's evaluated `sampleTarget`) and again by the new `DirectChannelsR` / read-side overlay — a double-transform (e.g. position applied twice, or a blend fighting itself).

**Detection signal:** a node that is keyframed via the OLD layer path renders at the wrong (doubled / fighting) value after the direct-channel road is added, while a freshly-injected free-floating channel renders correctly. The tell is "the layer-animated thing broke when I added direct channels" — a coexistence regression, not a bug in either path alone.

**The trap (wrong reactions):** "just scan all KeyframeChannels by target" (the obvious enumerator — silently double-counts); blaming `overlayChannels` or the layer's `patchTarget` (both are correct in isolation — the fault is feeding the SAME channel to both); trying to distinguish by `paramPath` or value shape (they're identical — a layer-wired position channel and a direct position channel are byte-identical except for the layer edge).

**The real fix (#197):** the direct-channel enumerator EXCLUDES any channel id referenced by an `AnimationLayer.animation` input — `layerWiredChannelIds(nodes)` builds the set once, `directChannelNodesForTarget` / `directChannelTargetSet` skip those ids (`src/app/nodeChannels.ts`). The two paths are then disjoint by construction: layer-wired → `AnimationLayerR`; free-floating → `DirectChannelsR` + read-side overlay. Locked by a unit test (`nodeChannels.test.ts` "EXCLUDES channels wired into an AnimationLayer"). Once the wrapper is retired (Phase 5), no channel is ever layer-wired and the guard becomes a no-op (removable). General principle: when you add a SECOND consumer that discovers work by a shared key (`target`), audit whether the FIRST consumer also claims items by that key — if so, the new consumer must subtract the first's claim or both fire. REF: [[V57]] (the road), `src/app/nodeChannels.ts`, `docs/UNIFICATION-DESIGN.md` §3.3.

**#188 corollary (2026-06-17) — when the guard is provably a NO-OP, document WHY rather than copy it blindly.** The glTF material-channel path (`GltfAssetR`'s `materialChannelsByChild` memo, `SceneFromDAG.tsx`) enumerates `materials.*` channels by `target === childDagId` straight from the narrow `depNodeMap` WITHOUT the `layerWiredChannelIds` exclusion — because a `GltfChild` is NOT a scene producer (no `out` socket), so `addLayer` can never wrap it and no material channel is EVER layer-wired. Applying the guard would force scanning the WHOLE node table (the [[H48]]/B13 storm `depNodeMap` exists to avoid). The discipline: the H105 audit still RAN (is the FIRST consumer — the layer path — able to claim this `target`? No, structurally) and the conclusion (guard unnecessary here) is documented at the call site, not assumed. The trap would be the inverse — copying the guard reflexively and re-introducing the full-table scan.

**#199 status (2026-06-18, Slices A+B) — the guard is now a runtime NO-OP, removable in Slice C.** After Slice A (native authoring mints direct channels, no layer) + Slice B (`migrateAnimationLayers` retires every layer at LOAD), no channel is ever wired into an `AnimationLayer.animation` socket at runtime — so `layerWiredChannelIds(nodes)` always returns ∅ and the exclusion is inert. It is RETAINED until Slice C (the physical node removal) because the transitional `dispatchFirstKeyComposite` branch can still add a band into a legacy layer in an UN-migrated in-session state; once the node type is deleted the guard (and the whole `layerWiredChannelIds` scan) is dead code → delete it with the node.

**#199 RESOLVED (2026-06-18, Slice C, `ux-overhall` `bd8f7e2`).** The `AnimationLayer` node type is physically gone, so a channel can NEVER be layer-wired — `layerWiredChannelIds` was DELETED from `nodeChannels.ts` along with the `wired.has(node.id)` filter in `directChannelNodesForTarget` / `directChannelTargetSet`. Every channel is free-floating by construction; the two-paths-disjoint problem this guard solved no longer exists (there is only ONE path). The re-introduced `mutator.timeline.addChannel` (Slice-C agent authoring, `1c829e3`) emits NO `→layer.animation` connect, so it can't re-create the hazard. The DISCIPLINE the entry teaches stays live (the #188 corollary): when a second consumer discovers work by a shared key, audit whether the first consumer also claims it — here the audit's answer became "there is no other consumer," which is the strongest possible resolution. The `nodeChannels.test.ts` "EXCLUDES … coexistence guard" cases were removed (they tested a behaviour that no longer exists).

## H106 — Deleting a registered node type breaks BOTH `ProjectSchema.parse` and `migrateNodes` on any saved file that still contains it; a per-node migration cannot fix it (it runs AFTER the registry lookup that throws) — the only safe host is a FORMAT migration that strips the type from raw JSON BEFORE the schema parses

**Root cause:** the load path is `migrateProjectFormat(raw)` → `ProjectSchema.parse(raw)` → `migrateNodes(project)` (`io.ts`). `migrateNodes` → `migrateOneNode` calls `getNodeType(node.type)` and THROWS "unknown type" when the type is unregistered (`migrations.ts`). So if you retire a node type (delete its registration) while old `.basher` files on disk still contain it, those files throw on load — and a per-node `def.migrations[]` entry cannot rescue it (there's no `def` to hang it on, and it would run too late anyway). A graph-shape retirement (re-wire edges, delete the node) is also not a single-node param migration.

**Detection signal:** "unknown type X — register the type before loading" on opening an older project right after you deleted X's registration; or a `z.literal` / enum schema rejecting the old node shape. Bundled examples pass (they never used X) but a user's saved file dies.

**The trap (wrong reactions):** add `def.migrations[v]` to the (now-deleted) node — there's no node to attach it to, and it runs post-parse; keep the node registered "just for migration" forever (leaves dead code + a zombie type in the union/registry); bump only the NODE version (per-node migrations don't remove a node or re-wire its edges).

**The real fix (#199 Slice B):** host the retirement as a PROJECT-FORMAT migration (`formatMigrations[N]`, `PROJECT_FORMAT_VERSION` bumped) that runs on the RAW untyped JSON BEFORE `ProjectSchema.parse`. `migrateAnimationLayers` walks `raw.state.nodes`, reverses the wrapper's graph surgery (re-target channels, re-point consumer edges, delete the layer node) and returns the object with `formatVersion` bumped. After it runs there is NO instance of the retired type, so neither the schema nor `migrateNodes` ever sees it — the type can be fully deleted from the registry. Gate with a byte-identical-render fixture (`migrations.test.ts`): load a serialized OLD-format project through the production path and assert the resolved render equals the pre-migration render. General principle: a node-type RETIREMENT is a whole-file graph transform → format migration (pre-parse, raw); a node-type EVOLUTION (new param, widened shape) is a per-node migration (post-parse, typed). Pick the host by whether the type SURVIVES. REF: [[V57]], `src/core/project/migrations.ts` (`migrateAnimationLayers`), `src/core/project/schema.ts` (`PROJECT_FORMAT_VERSION`), `docs/UNIFICATION-DESIGN.md` §4, krama [[K5]] step 7.

## H107 — A free-floating direct channel's animation overlay lives ONLY in the renderer + read-side resolver; NO node's `evaluate()` carries it, so any consumer/test that reads the animated value off `evaluate(node)` (or the node's evaluated `SceneChild`) silently gets the RAW authored value

**Root cause:** post-#199 ([[V57]]) a `KeyframeChannel*` is FREE-FLOATING — it carries `params.target` + `paramPath` and is NOT wired into any input socket, so it is never an input to the target node's `evaluate`. The animated value is produced ONLY by `overlayChannels`, invoked at two places: the renderer (`DirectChannelsR` in `SceneFromDAG`, per-frame useFrame) and the read-side resolver (`resolveEvaluatedTransform` / `resolveEvaluatedParam`, at `ctx.time`). `evaluate(state, targetId, ctx).value` returns the node's STATIC authored params — the channel overlay is nowhere in it. This is sharper than the legacy [[H40]]/B1.1 trap: pre-#199 the `AnimationLayer.evaluate` DID carry the patched value (`sampleTarget`), so reading `evaluate(layer)` worked; now there is no wrapper node whose evaluate carries it — the overlay exists purely in the resolver/renderer band.

**Detection signal:** a test/consumer reads `evaluate(node).position` (or the box's evaluated `SceneChild.position` off the Scene value) at two playhead times and gets the SAME static value — the animation "doesn't apply." The tell is "I added the channel, the DAG has it, but the value never moves when I read it." Caught 3–4 e2e specs migrating off the layer path this session (p3-observe, p7.1/p7.3/p7.4 all read the animated value the OLD way — `evaluate(layer).sampleTarget(s)` — which no longer exists).

**The trap (wrong reactions):** "the channel didn't get created / isn't wired" (it is — free-floating channels have no wire by design); adding a fake input edge from the channel to the node (re-introduces the wrapper coupling V57 removed); reading the Scene aggregator's evaluated child value (still raw — the Scene passes children through untouched, it is NOT the overlay site); concluding `overlayChannels` is broken (it's correct — it just isn't called by `evaluate`).

**The real fix:** read the animated value THROUGH the resolver, never `evaluate()`. In app code use `resolveEvaluatedTransform` / `resolveEvaluatedParam` (the SAME band the renderer consumes — one band, two callers, [[H40]]). In e2e use the `__basher_evaluated_transform(nodeId, ctx)` boot seam (`boot.ts:508`, which runs `resolveEvaluatedTransform`). RELATED migration gotcha: a node that was reachable in the scene ONLY via the old layer→`scene.children` edge becomes ORPHANED when the layer is removed — it must be connected directly to `scene.children` (the box IS its own scene child now), else the resolver returns null. General principle: when an overlay is applied by a CONSUMER (renderer/resolver) rather than baked into a producer's `evaluate`, "read the producer" gives you the un-overlaid value — read through the same consumer band the render uses. REF: [[V57]], [[H40]], dharana [[B1.1]], `src/app/resolveEvaluatedTransform.ts`, `src/app/nodeChannels.ts` (`overlayChannels` callers), `src/app/boot.ts:508` (`__basher_evaluated_transform`), `docs/UNIFICATION-DESIGN.md` §3.1. Provenance: ORIGIN = #199 Slice C e2e rewrites (2026-06-18) — observed when 3–4 migrated specs read static values; recurrence within one session → catalogued.

## H108 — A perf gate that asserts ABSOLUTE ms thresholds calibrated on ONE machine, driven through DEV-only seams, false-reds on every other machine and can never measure shipped perf

**Symptom:** a frame-budget e2e (`p95 ≤ 16.6ms`) that passed when authored on the baseline machine starts FAILING on a different (often FASTER) machine, with no code change to the path under test. On an M4 Pro, `p6-w9-perf` measured dev p50≈17.7 / p95≈21.5 / max≈35.9 against a 16.6/33ms budget — a red that looks like a regression but isn't.

**Root cause (Basher, 2026-06-18):** two compounding non-portabilities. (1) The harness drives the scene through `__basher_dag`/`__basher_time` — DEV-only seams STRIPPED from the production build ([[H65]]), so the test can ONLY run against `vite dev` (unminified React + StrictMode double-render), never the shipped bundle. (2) The thresholds are ABSOLUTE ms calibrated on one M1 dev machine; they bake in that machine's CPU, the display's vsync period (1000/60≈16.67ms — already ABOVE the 16.6 p95 floor, so a clean 60Hz display can't pass), and the test's own competing rAF collector loop. None of those transfer to another machine, so the budget is meaningless off-baseline.

**Detection signal:** a perf test fails on machine B but the path under test is provably unchanged (e.g. the new code loops the SAME data through the SAME function as the old — here post-#199 `DirectChannelsR` and the retired `AnimationLayerR` both loop the same channels through `overlayChannels`). The tell: "faster hardware, slower number." Confirm DEV-only by checking the harness reads `__basher_*` (absent in `vite preview`).

**The trap (wrong reactions):** treating the red as a regression and bisecting the animation road (there's no logic delta); weakening the threshold (16.6→18) to make it pass on the new machine (silently destroys the gate's meaning on the baseline — the test's own header forbids this); deleting the test (loses the baseline signal). Also: trying to measure production to "confirm" — impossible, the seams don't exist there.

**The real fix:** keep the threshold UNTOUCHED but stop APPLYING it where it can't hold — gate the test behind an explicit opt-in (`PERF_BASELINE=1`, same posture as the existing CI skip) so the default suite skips it and only the calibrated baseline runs it. Document WHY (dev-only seams + absolute-ms calibration) in the header and the re-calibration procedure. General principle: an absolute-threshold perf gate is a MACHINE-CALIBRATED BENCHMARK, not a portable correctness gate — either make it opt-in/baseline-scoped, or make the assertion RELATIVE (measure an idle-rAF baseline first and assert the scrub adds < Δ). REF: [[H65]] (DEV-only seams absent in prod), `tests/e2e/p6-w9-perf.spec.ts`, commit `8bb4701`, issue context #194/#199 handoff. Provenance: ORIGIN = #194 follow-up (2026-06-18) — the env-red flagged in the #199 handoff, root-caused by building a prod bundle and observing the seams are stripped.

## H109 — Comparing RAW half-float (Uint16) texel bits across a boundary-pair gives a WRONG match: half-float storage is non-linear in its bits, so the chroma/ratio of raw uint16 ≠ the chroma of the decoded floats — a "render == resolver" check silently fails (or worse, silently passes near gray)

**Symptom:** a boundary-pair e2e that compares a rendered light's color to its source HDR texture's color fails by a stubborn offset (here ~0.19 on a unit-luminance chroma, precision-1 → expected <0.05) even though the reduction logic is correct. The render side decoded the texture properly (`THREE.DataUtils.fromHalfFloat`), but the TEST read the texture's `image.data` (a `Uint16Array` of half-floats) and compared the RAW bits.

**Root cause (Basher #205, 2026-06-19):** an IEEE-754 half-float's 16 bits are sign(1)·exponent(5)·mantissa(10) — the integer value of those bits is NOT proportional to the represented real number. So `rawBits[r] / rawBits[g]` ≠ `decoded[r] / decoded[g]`; any ratio/chroma/average computed on the raw `Uint16` is meaningless. `RGBELoader`/`EXRLoader` return `HalfFloatType` DataTextures, so `texture.image.data` is `Uint16Array` — the trap fires whenever a test (or any consumer) reads HDR texel data without decoding.

**Detection signal:** an HDR-texture boundary-pair check is off by a fixed-ish amount that doesn't track the inputs; the comparison value looks "almost right" (often biased toward gray, since mid-range half-float bit patterns cluster). The tell: one side calls `fromHalfFloat`/uses a sampler, the other indexes `image.data` directly.

**The trap (wrong reactions):** loosening the tolerance until it passes (destroys the boundary-pair's meaning — a near-gray false-match would slip through); comparing a single texel "because the fixture is flat" (still raw-vs-decoded — the bug is the decode, not the averaging); blaming the reduction math (it was correct — observation: the unit test on decoded data passed, only the e2e raw read failed).

**The real fix:** decode half-float on BOTH sides before any arithmetic. In a Playwright `page.evaluate` (no bundler import of THREE's DataUtils), inline three's exact `fromHalfFloat` (sign/exp/mantissa → `(s?-1:1)·2^(e-15)·(1+f/1024)`, with the e==0 subnormal + e==0x1F inf/nan branches) and detect storage via `data.constructor.name === 'Uint16Array'` (half) vs `Float32Array`. General principle: HDR texel data is an ENCODED buffer — never do math on `image.data` without matching the texture's `type`. REF: `tests/e2e/p205-studio-light.spec.ts` (the in-test `fromHalf`), `src/app/averageRadiance.ts` (`readChannel` via `THREE.DataUtils.fromHalfFloat`), [[V61]] (the reduction it gates). Provenance: ORIGIN = #205 increment A — the studio-light boundary-pair e2e failed 0.19 on first run; root-caused by observing the unit test (decoded) passed while the e2e (raw) failed.

---

## H110 — An e2e that clicks the 3D viewport by projecting world→screen can land on a floating DOM island (agent chat) or an editor HELPER (camera frustum) layered over the canvas — the click never reaches the mesh's `onClick`, so a viewport feature looks broken while its wiring is fine

**Symptom:** A Playwright spec drives a real viewport interaction (click a mesh → selection / brush / drill) by projecting a node's world position through the live camera to a screen pixel, then `page.mouse.click(x, y)`. The handler never fires — the feature "does nothing." No console log from the handler, no selection change (or the WRONG thing gets selected — a camera), and the DAG is untouched. Re-checking the pure cores, they're all correct and unit-green; only the live click fails.

**Root cause:** the computed pixel sits over something OTHER than the target mesh: (a) a floating DOM island painted over the full-bleed canvas — the agent-chat `<textarea>` sits at viewport centre (the post-#2 floating-islands layout), so a centre-ish click hits the DOM input and the canvas never sees a pointer event at all; (b) an editor HELPER with its own `onClick` — the camera-frustum wireframe (CameraHelpers) crosses the world origin on screen and selects `n_camera`, and light/area-light helpers (LightHelpers) likewise — these are chrome, NOT `SceneChildNode`s, so a brush/drill branch that lives only on scene-child meshes never runs; (c) the projected point is sky just off the mesh → `onPointerMissed` (deselect), not a hit.

**The trap (wrong reactions):** concluding the feature is broken and "fixing" working wiring; nudging the click by a few px and re-running until green (fragile — the occluder moves with framing/layout); loosening to `locator('canvas').first()` (grabs the WRONG canvas — the timeline 2D `TimelineCanvas` is also a `<canvas>`).

**The real fix:** OBSERVE what's under the point before trusting the click — `document.elementFromPoint(x, y)` in a `page.evaluate` names the occluder immediately (TEXTAREA.agent-input vs CANVAS). Then place the target mesh in CLEAR screen space: move it OUT of the centre (where the chat island floats) and OFF the world origin (where the camera frustum crosses) — e.g. lift the cube to `[0, 4, 0]` and enlarge it — and project THAT point. Always select the viewport canvas specifically (`[data-testid="viewport"] canvas`), never `canvas.first()`. General principle: a click pixel over a full-bleed canvas is only a viewport click if nothing is layered above it there — verify the hit target, don't assume the canvas is on top. REF: `tests/e2e/p207-light-brush.spec.ts` (`clickCube` — projects `n_box` moved to `[0,4,0]`, viewport-scoped canvas), `tests/e2e/p6-w5-first-run.spec.ts` (the world→screen projection pattern), `src/app/Layout.tsx` / the agent-chat island (the centre occluder), `src/viewport/CameraHelpers.tsx` + `LightHelpers.tsx` (the helper `onClick`s). Provenance: ORIGIN = #207 Light Brush e2e — three failed runs (centre click hit the agent `<textarea>`; a near-origin click selected `n_camera` via the camera frustum; an upper-offset click hit sky) before `elementFromPoint` named the occluders and moving the cube to clear space fixed it. Recurrence-worthy: every future viewport-click e2e shares this surface.

## H111 — A derived geometry built by recursing into a CACHED source (a modifier `build`, an apply, an instancer) MUST clone each copy before transforming it; mutating the source in place silently corrupts every other ref sharing that cached instance

**Symptom:** Two meshes that share a geometry (same `GeometryRef.key` — e.g. two `ArrayModifier`s over identical boxes, or a box rendered directly AND arrayed) render WRONG together: one is displaced/scaled by the other's transform, or both show the merged/translated result. Each in isolation is correct; only with the shared source present does it corrupt. The geometry-registry cache (`src/app/geometryRegistry.ts`) is a singleton keyed by deterministic key (§48), so a `build` that reaches `get(source)` gets the SAME `BufferGeometry` instance every other consumer holds.

**Root cause:** the derived build applied a transform (translate/mirror/scale) directly to the cached source geometry (`source.applyMatrix4(m)` / `source.translate(...)`) instead of to a CLONE. `BufferGeometry.applyMatrix4` mutates in place; the registry handed out a shared reference, so the mutation leaks into every ref keyed to that source — and into the NEXT `get(source)` (which returns the now-corrupted cached instance, not a fresh build). The recursion makes it worse: an `array` of an `array` mutates the inner cached array, poisoning any other consumer of the inner handle.

**The trap (wrong reactions):** "fix" it by NOT caching the source (kills the whole point — every consumer rebuilds heavy geometry); deep-copy the source eagerly on every `get` (defeats the cache); assume the bug is in the merge/descriptor math (the math is right — the inputs were mutated under it). The tell that it's THIS class: correct in isolation, wrong when a sibling shares the source; the corruption survives across renders (it's baked into the cached buffer).

**The real fix:** in the derived `build`, `source.clone()` each copy BEFORE `applyMatrix4`, and `dispose()` the temporary clones after `mergeGeometries` copies their buffers out (the merged result is the new cached instance; the source stays pristine). The registry's cache invariant — "same key → same UNMODIFIED instance, shared safely" — holds only if every derived builder treats `get(source)` as READ-ONLY. REF: `src/app/geometryRegistry.ts` (`build('array')` — clones + disposes), `src/app/geometryRegistry.test.ts` ("array build … does not mutate the source"), `src/app/modifierGeometry.ts` (the recursive descriptor). Sibling of [[V64]] (the modifier substrate this guards), [[V43]] (the registry is a derived cache — shared by key, never mutated). Provenance: ORIGIN = #209 ArrayModifier — caught at authoring (the clone+dispose was written defensively) and LOCKED by a unit test asserting the cached source's bounding box is unchanged after an array build; promoted to a pattern because EVERY future modifier (Mirror/Subdivide/Solidify) and any instancer/apply that recurses into a cached source reopens the class.

## H112 — A geometry op with a determinant−1 transform (mirror / negative scale / reflection) MUST reverse the reflected copy's triangle WINDING, or the reflected half renders inside-out (back-faces front) even though its normals are correct

**Symptom:** A Mirror (or negative-scale) modifier's reflected half renders WRONG — dark, hollow, the inside of the surface showing, or faces missing under default front-face culling — while the original half is fine. The vertex count is right (2× source), the bounds are right, the normals LOOK reflected; only the shading/visibility of the mirrored half is broken. A flat-lit/unlit material can mask it; lighting + back-face culling expose it.

**Root cause:** `BufferGeometry.applyMatrix4(M)` with a det−1 matrix (e.g. `makeScale(-1,1,1)`) reflects the POSITION attribute and reflects the NORMAL attribute (via the normal matrix = inverse-transpose), but does NOT touch the index/triangle order. A reflection reverses orientation, so the geometric winding implied by the unchanged index order now DISAGREES with the (correctly reflected) normals: the face's front (by winding, used for back-face culling) points opposite to its lit front (by normal). Result: the reflected triangles are back-facing on screen and get culled / lit from behind.

**The trap (wrong reactions):** set the material `side: DoubleSide` to "make it show" (papers over culling, still mislit on the dark side, doubles overdraw); flip the NORMALS instead of the winding (now BOTH winding and normals are wrong-vs-each-other in the other direction); recompute normals after merge (`computeVertexNormals` re-derives from winding → smooths/destroys hard edges and only accidentally helps); blame `mergeGeometries`. The tell that it's THIS class: a reflecting/negative-scale op, half the result inside-out, normals numerically reflected but visibly wrong under culling.

**The real fix:** after `clone().applyMatrix4(reflect)`, REVERSE the reflected copy's winding — swap the 2nd & 3rd index of every triangle (indexed geometry) or the 2nd & 3rd vertex of every triplet (non-indexed) — so winding agrees with the reflected normals again; THEN merge. REF: `src/app/geometryRegistry.ts` (`build('mirror')` + `reverseWinding`), `src/app/geometryRegistry.test.ts` ("mirror reverses the reflected half winding — winding agrees with the normals everywhere": the decisive per-triangle `dot(geometricNormal, vertexNormal) > 0` check). Sibling of [[H111]] (clone-don't-mutate — same `build` recursion) and [[V64]] (the modifier substrate). Provenance: ORIGIN = the Mirror modifier (`582a327`, the 2nd geometry operator) — Array (det+1 translate) never hit this; Mirror is the first det−1 build. Caught at authoring (the winding reversal + the face-orientation unit test were written together) and confirmed by a render PNG of two solid correctly-lit boxes; promoted because every future reflecting/negative-scale op (Symmetrize, negative-scale Apply, mirror-Array) reopens the class.

## H113 — A multi-entry asset folder silently auto-picks ONE entry (shallowest / first-enumerated) → the user gets the WRONG model (often a stripped/untextured variant) with no error and no choice

**Symptom:** Importing a model folder "works" (no error, geometry appears) but renders untextured / with the wrong materials — and the user concludes "the textures didn't import." In fact a DIFFERENT glTF in the same folder was imported. Classic shape: an export pack ships `model.gltf` (1 material, 0 textures — a stripped variant) AND `model_Textured.gltf` (N materials, N textures) side by side; the importer loads the former.

**Root cause:** `locateEntryFile` returns the SHALLOWEST `.gltf`/`.glb`, and when several sit at the same depth it keeps the FIRST one in `input.files` / drop order — which is browser/OS enumeration order, NOT sorted, NOT deterministic. With >1 entry at the folder root the "winner" is effectively arbitrary, and there is no UI surfacing that a choice was even made.

**The trap (wrong reactions):** assume the textures failed to load and go debugging the sibling-resolution / OPFS path (the textures are fine — the wrong .gltf that doesn't reference them was loaded); sort entries by name and pick `[0]` (still silent, and name-sort ≠ "the one the user wants" — `_Textured` may sort after the stripped one); prefer the entry with the most materials silently (a better heuristic, but still no choice when two are genuinely different models). The tell that it's THIS class: import succeeds, geometry is right, materials/textures are wrong, and the folder contains more than one `.gltf`/`.glb`.

**The real fix:** when a granted folder has >1 glTF entry, PROMPT the user to choose (show per-entry material/texture counts so the real model is obvious; richest-first default); one entry → no prompt. REF: `src/app/asset/gltfEntryChoice.ts` (`resolveGltfEntryChoice` → the chooser), `src/app/asset/importGltf.ts` (`locateGltfEntries`/`summarizeGltfEntry` + `preferredEntryRelativePath`), `src/app/GltfEntryChooser.tsx`. Sibling of [[V66]] (the browser file-access boundary this lives at). Provenance: ORIGIN = a real ViktorTselikov toon-cars pack (`b11bf284…00.gltf` 1-mat-0-tex vs `…_Textured.gltf` 13-mat-14-tex) imported the untextured one; promoted because every multi-model / variant export pack reopens the class.

## H114 — A glTF mesh primitive with NO `material` renders the DEFAULT (white, no maps) material even though the file DEFINES a textured material — an exporter (3dripper) leaves the material ORPHANED, never bound to the geometry

**Symptom:** a single-mesh, single-material glTF imports WHITE / untextured even though the `.gltf` clearly contains a material with a `baseColorTexture` (and the texture file is present + valid). The captured IR material reads `name:"default"` (not the file's material name); the rendered clone shows `color=#ffffff map=false side=FrontSide`. Often the file is the `_Textured` variant of a pair, and the PLAIN variant binds its material correctly but has no texture — so "use the other file" doesn't recover the texture either.

**Root cause:** the mesh primitive has no `material` index (`primitives[0].material === undefined`), while the file's material is ORPHANED (defined in `materials[]` but referenced by no primitive). Per glTF 2.0 §3.7.2.1, an unbound primitive MUST render with the DEFAULT material — so three.js GLTFLoader assigns a default white `MeshStandardMaterial` and never even loads the (referenced-only-by-the-orphan) texture; Basher's capture then reads that default material. This is a producer bug (3D rippers like 3dripper emit it), NOT a Basher loader/capture bug — every spec-compliant viewer (Blender, gltf-viewer, three editor) shows it white too. Distinct from [[H113]] (which is the WRONG entry being picked; here the RIGHT entry is loaded but its geometry isn't wired to its material).

**The trap (wrong reactions):** debug the texture/OPFS sibling-resolution path (the texture is fine — it's just never referenced by a bound primitive); "fix" it by reading the render-time clone's material back into the DAG (a renderer→DAG write, boundary violation, V53/V34); auto-bind aggressively in the ambiguous multi-orphan case (you can't know which orphan belongs to which unbound primitive — guessing wrong is worse than the spec default). The tell that it's THIS class: import succeeds, geometry is right, the file defines a textured material, BUT `primitives[].material` is undefined and the material is orphaned.

**The real fix:** a BOUNDED producer-side repair at the ingest seam (the one-point-before-both-readers place spec/gloss converts) — when primitives are unbound AND exactly ONE material is orphaned, bind the unbound primitives to it; ambiguous cases (>1 orphan, or none) are left verbatim (spec-compliant default). Warn (no-silent-drop, [[V38]]) — it's a guess at intent. render == capture for free (both re-parse the repaired bytes). REF: `src/core/import/rebindOrphanMaterials.ts` (pure `rebindOrphanMaterials` + container dispatch `rebindOrphanMaterialsInEntry`), `src/app/asset/importGltf.ts` (`ingestGltfFolder` runs it before `convertSpecGlossEntry`), fixture `public/assets/orphan-material-quad.gltf`, e2e `gltf-orphan-material-rebind.spec.ts`. Sibling of [[V53]] (producer-side material capture at ingest) + [[H113]] (the other "imports untextured" class at the same boundary). NOTE the clustering: this is the SECOND producer-side document-repair at ingest (after spec/gloss conversion) — at a third, consolidate the container parse/serialize into ONE shared repair harness (currently below the restructure threshold, kept separate). Provenance: ORIGIN = a real 3dripper OmabuartsStudio Horse `_Textured.gltf` whose lone primitive had `material:undefined` while `M_Horse` (with baseColor+emissive textures) sat orphaned; observed white-on-import, fixed, re-observed textured (clone `map=true side=DoubleSide`, IR `M_Horse`).

## H115 — Selecting a wrapper/parent node shows NO transform gizmo because the wrapper carries no transform params; the transform lives on a DIFFERENT (nested) node

**Symptom:** a user selects the obvious "parent" of an imported model (the top node in the outliner) and no move/rotate/scale gizmo appears — yet selecting a child mesh DOES show one. The parent can be selected (it's in the outliner, has an inspector) but is not manipulable.

**Root cause:** the gizmo gate `getManipulable` (`Gizmo.tsx`) returns null unless `node.params.position` is a vec3; `resolveEvaluatedTransform` likewise reads `value.position`. A wrapper node that has no transform params (pre-#222 `Group` — params `{}`, only `{children}`; `GltfAsset` — no TRS) is therefore non-manipulable. The transform may live on a SEPARATE nested node (the import chain was `Group → Transform → GltfAsset`, so the transformable `Transform` sat one level UNDER the selected `Group`). The org boundary split "the parent" (Group) from "the transform" (Transform) — an organizational mismatch, not a gizmo bug.

**The trap (wrong reactions):** debug the gizmo mount / TransformControls (it's fine — there's just nothing manipulable to mount on); re-add the removed `evalForSelection` synth that fabricated a manip for a positionless node (#194 deleted it as dead — a positionless value resolves to null, so the synth can never fire); add a transform to GltfAsset AND keep the Transform (two transform owners → V20 one-writer violation). The tell: the parent is selectable but gizmo-less while its children/the nested wrapper ARE manipulable, and the file defines a multi-node wrapper chain.

**The real fix (Blender-aligned):** make the import root ONE transformable node — give the `Group` its own position/rotation/scale (+ a bbox-centre `pivot`) and wire `GltfAsset → Group → Scene` with no separate Transform, so the node the user selects IS the transformable one (Blender's parent/Empty: one object per node, each carries its own TRS — `io_scene_gltf2/blender/imp/node.py:50-101`; no synthetic non-transformable wrapper). Then `getManipulable` + the resolver light up automatically (both read `position`) → render==gizmo==inspector ([[V37]]/[[H40]]) for free; the pivot is render-only (rotation is about `position` in world either way). Watch the [[V10]]/[[H14]] back-compat trap: adding params additively (no version bump) means `migrateOneNode` does NOT re-parse old saved nodes through the schema, so the zod `.default` never fills them — an OLD `Group` reaches evaluate with raw `{}` and the renderer destructures `undefined` → guard at the evaluator AND the consumer. REF: `src/nodes/Group.ts`, `src/viewport/SceneFromDAG.tsx` (`GroupR`), `src/core/import/gltfImportChain.ts` (`computeGltfBoundsCenter` + Group-root wiring), `src/app/asset/dropChain.ts`, e2e `gltf-import-group-gizmo.spec.ts`. Sibling of [[V67]] (the transformable-Group invariant), [[H40]] (render==gizmo). Provenance: ORIGIN = user reported "can't select the parent group and see the gizmo" on every glTF import; grounded against Blender's importer.

## H116 — A manipulator (gizmo) seeded from a node's LOCAL transform sits DETACHED from the rendered object when the node is NESTED under a transformed ancestor — and writing the proxy's world value back as LOCAL params double-transforms it

**Symptom:** select an object nested under a transformed Group/Transform and the move/rotate/scale gizmo appears OFFSET from the object (at roughly the origin, or anywhere except on the object) by exactly the parent's transform. Dragging it makes the object jump. Selecting a TOP-LEVEL object works fine. Confirmed by observation: a cube whose own local position is `[0,0,0]`, nested under a Group at `[5,1,0]`, RENDERS at world `[5,1,0]` (real three `matrixWorld`) but the gizmo proxy sat at `[0,0,0]` (the local pose).
