**Root cause:** the gizmo proxy lives at the render-root (identity parent), so its transform IS world space, but it was seeded from the node's LOCAL transform (`resolveEvaluatedTransform`, which returns local and only resolves top-level scene-children / GltfChild) and its drag was written back verbatim as LOCAL params. For a TOP-LEVEL child local == world (parent is the identity scene root) so both directions are correct; for a NESTED child local ≠ world, so the seed is offset and the write double-applies the parent transform. This is the [[H40]] displayed≠rendered class on the manipulator's SEEDING side. Went LIVE for glTF when [[V67]]/#222 made the import root a *translated* Group (every imported model's children are now under a non-identity ancestor).

**The trap (wrong reactions):** "fix" only the SEED (anchor the proxy at world) without fixing the WRITE-BACK → display looks right but dragging a nested child now writes world-as-local and jumps WORSE (the two halves must move together); attach the gizmo to the real rendered three object instead of the synthetic proxy (breaks the evaluated/animated-clone decoupling the proxy exists for); recompute the parent world on every `onObjectChange` frame (a full render-root eval per drag-frame — capture it once at seed time in a ref instead). The tell: the gizmo is detached by *exactly* a parent transform, and a top-level object of the same kind works.

**The real fix:** resolve the node's PARENT world matrix (`resolveParentWorldMatrix`, mirroring the SceneFromDAG composition incl. Group pivot + channel/transient overlay) and (a) SEED the proxy at `parentWorld · localMatrix(node)` so it sits where the object renders, (b) on drag CONVERT the proxy's world transform back to local params via `parentWorld⁻¹ · proxyWorld` (stripping a dragged Group's own `-pivot`). Return null for top-level / flat (light·camera) / unresolvable (GltfChild) → the manipulator keeps the local path, BYTE-IDENTICAL. One principle: **a manipulator must operate in the space the object RENDERS in, and convert back to the authored (local) param space on write** — render==gizmo==inspector ([[V37]]/[[H40]]) extends to the manipulation round-trip, not just the read. REF: `src/app/resolveWorldTransform.ts` (`resolveParentWorldMatrix`), `src/app/Gizmo.tsx` (world-anchor seed + `worldToLocalTRS` write-back), `src/app/resolveWorldTransform.test.ts`, e2e `tests/e2e/p230-nested-gizmo-world.spec.ts`. Sibling of [[H40]] (two callers, one band), [[V67]]/[[H115]] (the transformable Group that made it live), [[V37]] (viewport==render). KNOWN-LIMIT: a glTF child's world is name-addressed inside a GltfAsset (not a scene-child edge `resolveParentWorldMatrix` walks) → it keeps the local path (#230 follow-up). Provenance: ORIGIN = #230, confirmed by direct observation (gizmo proxy `[0,0,0]` vs rendered world `[5,1,0]`) during the Blender-parity study; promoted because every nesting/parenting feature (the parity epic #232) reopens this class.

## H117 — Picking the click-selected object by NEAREST ORIGIN (closest pivot to the cursor) instead of nearest SURFACE — the cursor is a RAY, not a 3D point, so origin-proximity selects empty space and loses the overlap-depth winner

**Symptom (the proposed-but-wrong design):** "to skip drilling group→individual, just select the object whose ORIGIN is closest to the cursor." Sounds simpler than raycasting, but it mis-selects: clicking EMPTY SPACE near an object's pivot selects it (no surface is under the cursor); with two overlapping parts the winner is whichever PIVOT is nearer in screen space, not the one visibly in front; a car body whose origin sits at world-origin (or a wheel sharing the body pivot) gets picked over the small part whose geometry you're actually pointing at.

**Root cause:** a screen click defines a RAY through the scene, not a point — "closest origin" has to project every pivot to 2D and pick nearest, which is decoupled from whether any geometry is under the cursor and from depth. Origins are authoring handles; they are routinely far from (or shared across) the geometry they govern. Selection-by-origin answers "which pivot is near the mouse," not "what did I click on."

**The trap (wrong reactions):** reach for closest-origin because "we already project origins for box-select, reuse it" — but [[V71]] box-select tests origin-in-REGION on PURPOSE (Blender object-center marquee), a different operation than click; conflating them imports the marquee rule into the click. Also tempting: keep broad-first (select the asset/group) and make the user drill — the very friction being removed.

**The real fix:** click selection is nearest-SURFACE occlusion picking — the frontmost ray intersection (`e.intersections[0]`, already depth-sorted by R3F) mapped to its addressable LEAF node; selecting a parent/asset is an EXPLICIT affordance (Alt+click up, Select Hierarchy, outliner), and a repeat-click cycles overlaps front-to-back. Mirrors Blender Object Mode GPU ID-buffer picking (`gpu_select`); origin-in-region stays the BOX-select rule ONLY. One principle: **a click selects what its RAY hits in front, not which pivot is nearest; origin proximity is a region/marquee test, never a pick test.** REF: `src/viewport/SceneFromDAG.tsx` (SceneChildNode onClick — the leaf-map target), `src/viewport/gltfDrillChain.ts` (`buildGltfDrillChain` already maps the hit → `chain[last]` leaf), [[V75]] (the target invariant), [[V71]] (the deliberate origin-for-box contrast). Provenance: ORIGIN = 2026-06-22 selection design discussion; the user proposed closest-origin to kill the drill friction — half-right (drop broad-first) but the mechanism is nearest-surface, grounded against the bundled Blender manual. Captured so the #233 build doesn't re-derive closest-origin.

## H118 — A camera pose with an undefined/NaN `roll` poisons the WHOLE orientation quaternion with NaN (the camera vanishes), because the forward math applies `degToRad(roll)` unguarded

**Symptom:** after adding a camera `roll` param (#229), a code path that builds a pose WITHOUT roll (a partial/legacy object, a test fixture, an old `.basher`) makes the camera disappear from the viewport/render — `cameraOrientationQuat` returns a quaternion of all-NaN, the camera's matrix is NaN, nothing renders, no error thrown.

**Root cause:** the forward orientation math rolls by `setFromAxisAngle(dir, THREE.MathUtils.degToRad(rollDeg))`. When `rollDeg` is `undefined` (a pose missing the field) or NaN, `degToRad` yields NaN → the roll quaternion is NaN → it premultiplies the (valid) aim quaternion → the whole orientation is NaN → `compose`/`decompose` propagate NaN through position+scale too. Silent: NaN doesn't throw, it just renders nothing.

**The trap (wrong fix):** "the production path defaults roll to 0 (`cameraPoseFromNode`), so it can't happen" — but the math is a PUBLIC pure helper with four callers + tests + the gizmo inverse; ANY caller that hands it a partial pose triggers it. Defaulting at one source does not protect a shared pure function.

**The real fix:** finite-guard the roll branch at the math itself: `if (Number.isFinite(rollDeg) && rollDeg !== 0)` — a non-finite roll falls back to no-roll (identity) rather than poisoning the quaternion. The guard lives where the NaN would be INTRODUCED (the pure helper), not at each call site. One principle: **a pure math primitive must defend its own inputs against non-finite values — NaN propagates silently through matrix composition, so guard at the point of introduction, not at one upstream default.** REF: `src/app/cameraOrientation.ts` (`cameraOrientationQuat` finite-guard), [[V77]] (the bijection it protects), [[V56]] (the pose authority whose `cameraPoseFromNode` defaults roll at the production source). Provenance: ORIGIN = 2026-06-23 #229 slice 1 — the `renderToImage.test.ts` PERSP fixture (no roll) failed with NaN forward; caught by OBSERVATION (the unit test), fixed at the helper + the fixture.

## H119 — A "depth pass" built the obvious way renders a useless image twice over: MeshDepthMaterial is near-black, and frustum-normalized linear depth is a flat white silhouette — both only visible by EYEBALLING the PNG

**Symptom:** ComfyUI Inc 1 depth control pass. Attempt 1 (`THREE.MeshDepthMaterial` override) → the cube renders near-BLACK (cube-grid luminance max ≈ 3). Attempt 2 (custom linear eye-depth normalized over the camera near/far) → the cube renders as a FLAT WHITE silhouette on black — a mask with no front-to-back gradient. Both "pass" a naive non-blank assertion; both are worthless as ControlNet depth. The defect is only visible by reading the actual PNG, not from logs or a uniform-color check.

**Root cause (two stacked):** (1) `MeshDepthMaterial` with the default `BasicDepthPacking` writes `1 − gl_FragCoord.z`, and perspective `gl_FragCoord.z` saturates to ~1 for everything past the near plane → `1−z ≈ 0` everywhere not glued to the near plane → near-black. (2) Linear eye-space depth is correct, but normalizing over the CAMERA frustum (`near`..`far`, e.g. 0.1..1000) maps a small object's ~1.5-unit depth span into <1 of 255 → every cube pixel rounds to the same white → a silhouette, not a ramp.

**The trap (wrong fix):** "use `MeshDepthMaterial`, it's literally the depth material" (attempt 1), then "normalize over the camera near/far" (attempt 2). Each looks principled and each renders SOMETHING — so without eyeballing you'd ship a black or flat-white pass and only discover it when the ControlNet output is garbage three increments later.

**The real fix:** compute LINEAR eye-space depth in a custom shader (`vViewZ = -mvPosition.z`), and normalize over the VISIBLE CONTENT's depth range — the bounding sphere of the visible meshes as seen from the camera (`dist(cam, centre) ± radius`), clamped to camera near — NOT the camera frustum. Invert so near = white (ControlNet convention). This is relative/MiDaS-style depth: a small object fills the 0..1 ramp. One principle: **a depth (or any normalized geometry) pass must be normalized over the data's own extent, not the container's — and "is it non-blank?" is not "is it correct?"; eyeball the actual pixels (Lokayata), a render that produces an image still produces the WRONG image.** REF: `src/render/renderToImage.ts` (`renderViaPass` / `makeLinearDepthMaterial` / `visibleContentSphere` / `depthRange`), `tests/e2e/p-comfy-inc1-control-passes.spec.ts` (the `cubeLumSpread > 25` gradient assertion that falsifies the flat silhouette), design `docs/COMFYUI-KEYFRAME-COMPILER-DESIGN.md` §9, [[V80]] (the Render Result view that made the eyeballing possible). Provenance: ORIGIN = 2026-06-24 ComfyUI Inc 1 — both defects were found ONLY by dumping the depth PNG to disk and looking at it after the e2e went green; the normal pass (MeshNormalMaterial) was correct first try, the depth pass took two observed iterations.

## H120 — Basher (browser) → ComfyUI fails with 403 / "Failed to fetch" even though `curl` works, because ComfyUI's origin-validation middleware rejects cross-origin requests without `--enable-cors-header`

**Symptom:** ComfyUI runs, `curl http://127.0.0.1:8188/system_stats` returns 200, but the same request FROM the Basher browser app (a fetch from `http://localhost:5180`) fails — `isAvailable()` returns false, Test Connection shows "○ Unreachable", the capability silently falls back to the stub. With an `Origin` header the server returns **403 Forbidden** (not just a missing ACAO).

**Root cause:** ComfyUI ships an origin/host-validation middleware (CSRF protection). A cross-origin browser request is rejected (403) unless the server is started with `--enable-cors-header [ORIGIN]`, which adds `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` (+ `Allow-Headers: Content-Type, Authorization`). `curl` has no `Origin` header by default → it isn't treated as cross-origin → it works, masking the problem. This is a BOTH-SIDES boundary failure: Basher's code is correct; the OTHER side (the server's launch flags) is misconfigured.

**The trap (wrong fix):** "the server is up (curl proves it), so the bug is in Basher's fetch / URL / capability code" — and you go hunting in HttpComfyUICapability while the real fix is a server launch flag you don't control from Basher. The asymmetry (curl 200, browser 403) is the tell.

**The real fix:** run ComfyUI with `--enable-cors-header '*'` for local dev (lock to the Basher origin if exposed). Capture it in the launch script (`../projects/comfyui/run-basher.sh`). On the Basher side, make the failure LEGIBLE rather than a silent stub-fallback: `probeComfyUI` surfaces the error string so the Settings "Test Connection" badge shows WHY (the boundary-pair observation — verify the SERVER side, not just your own). One principle: **when a service works from `curl` but not the browser, suspect CORS/origin policy on THEIR side before debugging YOUR client; `curl`'s missing `Origin` header makes it a non-representative probe.** REF: `src/core/comfy/index.ts` (`probeComfyUI` surfaces the reason), `../projects/comfyui/run-basher.sh` (`--enable-cors-header`), design `docs/COMFYUI-KEYFRAME-COMPILER-DESIGN.md` §10, [[V81]]. Provenance: ORIGIN = 2026-06-24 ComfyUI Inc 2 — observed the 403 with an `Origin` header during the connection-layer grounding, before wiring the settings (caught BEFORE shipping a silent stub-fallback).

## H121 — A stored `globalThis.fetch` (or any built-in) called as a METHOD (`this.fetchImpl(...)`) throws "Illegal invocation" — the browser binds `this` to the holder object, not Window; dormant until the first real (non-injected) call

**Symptom:** a capability that wraps `fetch` works in unit tests (which inject a mock `fetchImpl`) and works via a SIBLING code path that calls fetch as a free variable, but the wrapped path silently fails in the real browser: every call throws `Failed to execute 'fetch' on 'Window': Illegal invocation`, the `catch` swallows it, and the capability falls back to a stub/default with no surfaced reason ("the server is reachable — I curl it, I probe it from the page — but the app says stub").

**Root cause:** `this.fetchImpl = opts.fetchImpl ?? globalThis.fetch` stores the UNBOUND built-in, then calls it as `this.fetchImpl(...)`. A method call sets `this` to the receiver (the capability instance). Browser `fetch` (and many Web/DOM built-ins: `setTimeout`, `localStorage.*`, `crypto.subtle.*`) REQUIRE their original receiver (Window) and throw "Illegal invocation" when `this` is anything else. It stays DORMANT because: (a) tests inject a plain function (no receiver requirement); (b) a parallel path may call the SAME global as a free variable `fn(...)` (this=undefined → allowed); so the bug only fires on the first real method-dispatched call.

**The trap (wrong fix):** because a direct `fetch(url)` from the page console/DevTools works AND the probe URL is correct, you conclude "the server probe is just flaky / a race / the cache is stale" and add retries or cache-busting — while the real cause is the receiver rebind on the stored reference. Reading the code (`this.fetchImpl(...)` looks fine) is INFERENCE; the throw message is OBSERVATION — instrument the `catch` and read it.

**The real fix:** bind the built-in to its owner when storing it — `opts.fetchImpl ?? globalThis.fetch.bind(globalThis)` (or call it as a free function: `const f = this.fetchImpl; await f(...)`). One principle: **a built-in stored on an object and invoked as a method loses its required Window receiver — `.bind()` it (or keep it free) at the storage site.** Diagnostic: an `isAvailable()`/probe that returns false while a manual fetch succeeds, and a `catch` that hides the reason → instrument the catch. REF: `src/core/comfy/HttpComfyUICapability.ts` (constructor `globalThis.fetch.bind(globalThis)`); sibling that masked it: `probeComfyUI` (free-variable fetch). Provenance: ORIGIN = 2026-06-25 ComfyUI Inc 3 Slice E (first REAL browser /prompt submit); the live decode logged the Illegal-invocation throw — the bug had shipped dormant since the P5 capability was written (tests injected fetch, prod never exercised the HTTP path). [[H120]] (sibling browser↔ComfyUI boundary), [[H64]] (capability probe correctness), [[V6]] (the capability boundary).

### H122 — A top-bar dropdown z-index BELOW a mode's full-bleed editor overlay → menu opens behind it (occluded), clicks fall through; `isVisible()` ≠ not-occluded

**Symptom:** "none of the menus work in <mode>." The dropdown opens (DOM present, `isVisible()` true) but is invisible and unclickable — only in ONE editor mode.

**Root cause:** a global top-bar dropdown (e.g. MenuBar FILE/EDIT/…) opens downward from its row INTO the viewport region, where a mode-specific overlay slot is mounted (the Video space's compositor at `zIndex:45`, `Layout.tsx`). Both resolve in the SAME root stacking context, so the higher z wins: the slot (45) painted over the dropdown (z-40). In the OTHER modes the slot is `display:none`, so the menu works — the breakage is mode-scoped, which misdirects toward "stale state / HMR" rather than z-index.

**The trap (wrong fix):** because a FRESH load "passes" (Playwright `isVisible()` / a quick reload) you conclude it's accumulated HMR state and restart the dev server. `isVisible()` reports DOM visibility, NOT occlusion — it is GREEN on an element painted under another. Reading "the menu element exists + isVisible" is INFERENCE; `document.elementFromPoint(cx,cy)` returning the OVERLAY (not the menu item) is the OBSERVATION. (First diagnosed this as HMR — wrong; the user re-framed to "look at the z-index.")

**The real fix:** lift global-chrome dropdowns ABOVE the editor-overlay tier. `MenuBar.tsx` dropdown `z-40` → `z-50` (the established global-chrome dropdown tier — sibling ProjectTabs/ProjectsMenu were already z-50, which is why THEY worked; below the modal tier z-[100]). Principle: **a global-chrome popover must out-rank every mode's content-overlay slot in the shared stacking context; assert it by hit-test (`elementFromPoint`), never by `isVisible()`.** Guard: `tests/e2e/p-menubar-video-zindex.spec.ts` (hit-test the item is top + a click fires its action in video mode). Provenance: ORIGIN = 2026-06-26, user report "menus dead in video mode" → re-frame "look at the z-index." [[V83]] (the video-slot overlay), [[H95]] (overlay-clipped-but-present sibling), dharana B24.

**2nd occurrence — the GENERAL form (surface SELECTION, not just z-order, 2026-06-26).** Same boundary: a VIDEO-space action (workflow-JSON import parse failure) reported to `useAssetErrorStore`, whose `AssetErrorBanner` is mounted IN the view3d slot (`zIndex:20`) — which the compositor (z45) covers, so the user never sees the error in video mode. This is not a z-index *tweak* (the banner is correctly scoped to the 3D viewport); it is **wrong surface choice**: a transient *user-action* outcome must go to the **app-root toast** (`useNotificationStore` → `ToastViewport`, mounted in `App.tsx` ABOVE every mode slot), NOT the view3d-scoped banner. Rule: **pick the notify surface by where it's MOUNTED relative to the active editor space — view3d-slot chrome (AssetErrorBanner, DiffBar, gizmo, helpers) is invisible in VIDEO/2D space; only the app-root toast spans all spaces.** Two clusters at this boundary now (dropdown z-order + report-surface mounting) → the unifying diagnostic: "in which editor space does this surface render, and is it covered there?" (`src/app/video/addLayer.ts` + `importPicker.ts` route to `notify`; `tests/e2e/p-compositor-comfy-import.spec.ts` asserts `toast-error` visible in video). REF: `src/app/ToastViewport.tsx` (app-root) vs `src/app/AssetErrorBanner.tsx` (view3d slot); [[V38]] (surface-the-outcome).

**3rd occurrence — the runtime/decode path (2026-06-26, `f115e26`).** Same boundary, same wrong-surface choice, now NOT a user-triggered action but a RUNTIME failure: `decodeComfy` reported a live ComfyUI submit error to `useAssetErrorStore` — the view3d-covered banner — so a live-generate failure was invisible in VIDEO mode exactly where the comfy layer lives. This made [[H125]]'s submit-storm look fully silent (the storm WAS surfacing errors, to a covered surface). Fix: `decodeComfy` → `useNotificationStore.getState().notify` (app-root toast; dedups on (severity,message) so a per-frame retry doesn't spam). The rule now spans three triggers at this boundary — dropdown z-order, user-action report, runtime decode error — confirming it's structural, not incidental: **ANY surface that conveys outcome/state must be chosen by which editor space it renders in; in VIDEO/2D space, only the app-root toast (and modal tier) is visible — every view3d-slot surface is occluded.** dharana B24.

**STRUCTURAL ROOT CLOSED — #237 (2026-06-30, `d43c41f`).** The first three occurrences each PATCHED a symptom (lift the dropdown z; re-home the notify surface) while the underlying organizational fault persisted: the 3D-editor chrome (FloatingViewportToolbar, outliner/inspector side islands, the bottom agent/3D-TimelineDrawer stack) stayed MOUNTED AND VISIBLE under the `video-slot` (z-45) — merely *covered*, never *hidden*. A covered affordance still occupies the DOM hit-region, so the bug class can recur at any new covered surface (the [[H129]] dopesheet probe "broke the page" = a click intercepted by the covered 3D timeline). Fix: gate that chrome with `chromeHidden = isPresent || space === 'video'` and apply `display:none` (`src/app/Layout.tsx`) so in VIDEO space the 3D chrome is GONE, not layered-under. **Principle: don't cover mode-foreign chrome with a higher z — UNMOUNT-via-display:none it. Two surfaces sharing a hit-region in the same stacking context is the defect; raising z only fixes the painting, not the click-interception. `display:none` (not unmount) keeps mount-once state, same discipline as the view3d/uv/video slots.** This converts the family from "find-and-patch each covered surface" to "the foreign chrome isn't there at all." The notify-surface rule (3rd occ) still holds for app-root toasts (correct regardless), but new covered-CLICK regressions in the compositor are now structurally prevented. Guard: screenshot parity (view3d full chrome vs video clean) + Add-Layer-menu click-reachable in video. [[H129]] (the dopesheet probe this unblocks); [[V83]]; dharana B24.

### H123 — Test-environment codec support ≠ production: Playwright's bundled Chromium has no proprietary H.264, so an H.264 mp4 fixture won't decode in CI

**Symptom:** a video e2e passes locally (macOS Chromium uses the platform H.264 decoder) but the same `.mp4` fixture fails to decode on CI (Linux bundled Chromium), or you wrongly conclude "video decode is broken."

**Root cause:** open-source / bundled Chromium ships only royalty-free codecs (VP8/VP9/AV1); H.264 (and AAC) are proprietary and absent unless the platform provides them or you run `channel:'chrome'`. The decode code is codec-agnostic (HTMLVideoElement uses whatever the browser ships), so PRODUCTION (real Chrome/Safari) decodes H.264 fine — only the TEST browser is the constraint.

**The trap (wrong fix):** picking an `.mp4` fixture encoded with H.264 (the obvious "an mp4 is H.264") and, when it fails on CI, either disabling the test or adding `channel:'chrome'` (CI may lack Chrome). **The real fix:** encode the fixture with a royalty-free codec — **VP9-in-MP4** (a genuine `.mp4` that decodes in every Chromium incl. CI) — and document why. `ffmpeg -f lavfi -i testsrc2=...:rate=30 -c:v libvpx-vp9 clip.mp4` (use `testsrc2` so frames differ → frame-change is observable). Principle: **verify codec support empirically in the actual test browser (a throwaway `elementFromPoint`/createImageBitmap probe) before committing a media fixture; never assume container==codec.** REF: `public/fixtures/video/clip-vp9.mp4`, `tests/e2e/p-compositor-video-layer.spec.ts`, `src/core/media/WebCodecsMediaDecode.ts`. Provenance: ORIGIN = 2026-06-26 video-layer e2e (slice 1b.2) — probed vp9/av1/h264 in Playwright Chromium; all decoded locally, VP9 chosen for CI portability. [[V6]] (decode capability boundary).

### H124 — A custom animatable control that keys via the GENERIC first-key road (`inferValueType`) silently MIS-TYPES a non-transform value: a ComfyUI `string` prompt mints a `KeyframeChannelColor`, not a `KeyframeChannelText`

**Symptom:** a keyframed ComfyUI prompt (or any domain param whose JS type collides with a transform type) animates wrongly or not at all — the channel exists but is the wrong KeyframeChannel\* kind. The diamond turns filled (a channel WAS created), so it looks wired; only inspecting the node type (or the broken sampling) reveals the mismatch.

**Root cause:** `dispatchFirstKeyComposite` → `dispatchDirectFirstKey` picks the channel type with `inferValueType(value)`, which is keyed to the 3D-transform domain: `string → 'color'` (a hex), `number → 'number'`, `[a,b] → 'vec2'`, etc. It was DELIBERATELY not taught `'text'`/`'image'` (comment in `dispatchMutator.ts`). A ComfyUI prompt is a `string` but must be a STEP `KeyframeChannelText`; an image-ref `string` must be `KeyframeChannelImage`. JS-type inference cannot distinguish "a colour hex" from "a prompt" from "a filename" — only the DOMAIN's declared kind can.

**The trap (wrong fix):** teaching `inferValueType` a `'text'` guess (e.g. "a string that isn't a hex is text") — fragile (a hex-looking prompt mis-types; collides with the colour field) and pollutes the generic seam with domain knowledge. **The real fix:** dispatch the channel type from the DOMAIN MANIFEST, not the JS value. Add a producer-specific branch BEFORE the generic road: `dispatchFirstKeyComposite` detects a `ComfyUIWorkflow` target + a `comfy:<nodeId>.<input>` paramPath, reads the param's `valueKind` from `importComfyGraph` (the manifest, never stored → can't go stale), and maps it EXPLICITLY (`float|int → Number`, `string → Text`, `image → Image`; bool/enum → reject). The generic `inferValueType` road is left byte-unchanged for native/camera/glTF. **Principle: when a value's JS type underdetermines its animation channel, the channel type must come from the domain's declared kind, not a runtime type guess — add a domain branch at the dispatch seam, don't widen the generic inference.** REF: `src/app/animate/dispatchMutator.ts` (`dispatchComfyFirstKey` / `comfyChannelNodeFor`), `src/core/comfy/comfyGraph.ts` (`ComfyValueKind` + `importComfyGraph`), `src/app/video/ComfyControlsSection.tsx`, `tests/e2e/p-compositor-controls-comfy.spec.ts` (asserts `KeyframeChannelText` NOT `…Color`). Provenance: ORIGIN = 2026-06-26 Inc-3 Slice D — wiring the Controls-panel prompt diamond; observed the design's "do NOT use inferValueType" warning was load-bearing (string→color). Sister to the ≥4-value-shape-gate channel traps. [[H104]] (custom-control diamond wiring); [[V57]] (free-floating channels); [[V81]] (ComfyUI epic).

### H125 — A decode that drives a SLOW async resource with NO in-flight dedup, fired from a high-frequency re-render, storms the resource until every request starves past its own timeout — the result never displays though the producer SUCCEEDS

**Symptom:** a live ComfyUI compositor layer stays on the STUB even though the ComfyUI server reports `execution_success` for the job. The real frame is produced server-side but never appears in-app. (Generalizes: any "submit → poll → fetch" decode behind a render loop.)

**Root cause:** `ensureBitmap` had a result cache (`bitmapCache` by `path#frame`) but **no in-flight dedup**. The composite re-renders many times while one `decodeComfy` is mid-submit (a submit takes SECONDS: upload → `/prompt` → poll `/history` → `/view`). Each re-render is a cache MISS (the first decode hasn't resolved yet) → fires ANOTHER `decodeComfy` → ANOTHER `/prompt`. On a SERIAL GPU the jobs queue FIFO; by the time any given client submit's job reaches the front of the backlog, >30s (the `HttpComfyUICapability` submit timeout) has elapsed → the client `AbortController` fires → submit throws → stub fallback. The server keeps churning the backlog (a job is still "running" after the test ends), so server-side SUCCESS and client-side STUB coexist — the contradiction that names the bug.

**The trap (wrong fix):** the obvious reads all misdirect — "the server is slow" (no: one clean job is ~18s, under timeout), "model load" (folded into the 18s), "bump the timeout" (treats the symptom; the storm still grows the backlog unboundedly under any finite timeout), "the upload failed" (no: the job referenced `basher_img_*.png` and SUCCEEDED). The decisive OBSERVATION that cuts through: query `/history` + `/queue` — a job `execution_success` while the app shows stub ⇒ the failure is on the CLIENT submit/display side, not the round-trip. (Compounded by [[H122]]: the submit error went to the view3d-covered `assetErrorStore` banner → invisible in video mode → looked silent.)

**The real fix:** dedup in-flight decodes by the cache key — `const inFlight = new Map<key, Promise>()`; `ensureBitmap` returns the pending promise if one exists, else starts ONE `decodeBitmap` and `.finally(() => inFlight.delete(key))`. Concurrent callers await the same promise, then hit the result cache. One clean submit per `path#frame`; the storm cannot form. (Covers media decodes too — same starvation shape, just cheaper.) **Principle: any decode that (a) calls a slow async resource AND (b) is invoked from a high-frequency re-render MUST dedup in-flight requests by its cache key — a result cache alone is insufficient because the misses pile up before the first result lands; an unbounded request fan-out against a serial backend starves itself past its own timeout.** Also route the failure to the app-root toast, not the covered banner ([[H122]] 3rd occ). REF: `src/app/video/compositeDecode.ts` (`inFlight` map + `ensureBitmap`/`decodeBitmap` split + `decodeComfy` → `useNotificationStore`), `src/core/comfy/HttpComfyUICapability.ts` (the 30s `submit` timeout it was starving past). Provenance: ORIGIN = 2026-06-26 live observation (user chose "observe the live round-trip"); the depth-pass→img2img green-cube frame fetched from `/view` (~100k colours) proved the server side WORKS while the composite showed stub → diagnosed the storm; after fix the composite showed the real frame (151 colours), ONE submit, ~6s. [[H122]] (covered-surface notify); [[V81]]/[[V82]] (ComfyUI epic / control passes); dharana B24.

### H126 — A BATCHED submit reusing the SINGLE-FRAME timeout aborts client-side while the server keeps SUCCEEDING — the same H125-family "server execution_success while the app shows nothing" contradiction, but the cause is a too-short budget, not a request storm

**Symptom:** "Render coherent clip" against a real ComfyUI never produces a clip; the app shows an error/nothing. But `/history` reports the prompt `execution_success`. (Inc 4 batched path; sibling of [[H125]] — same observable contradiction, different root cause.)

**Root cause:** `HttpComfyUICapability.submitBatch` reused the 30s single-frame `timeoutMs`. A BATCH runs N frames through ONE `/prompt` and is inherently long — a 3-frame SD1.5 batch on MPS already takes ~43s (seconds/frame × N + model load). The `AbortController` fired at 30s while the server was still executing → submit threw "timed out" → error toast → no clip. The server finished the batch regardless (`execution_success` ~13s later) → server-SUCCESS + client-NOTHING coexist.

**The trap (wrong fix):** "the workflow was rejected" (no — `/history` shows success), "the batch is too big" (no — 3 frames), "fall back to the stub on failure" (papers over a real, completable render). The decisive OBSERVATION (the H125 method, now a reflex at this boundary): `curl /history` — `execution_success` while the app shows nothing ⇒ a CLIENT-side abort, not a round-trip failure. The 43s server time vs the 30s client budget is then the obvious culprit.

**The real fix:** give `submitBatch` its OWN, generous budget — `batchTimeoutMs` (default 600_000 = 10 min), separate from the 30s single-frame `timeoutMs`. Batches are long (design §16 Q-F: "batched runs need progress + cancel"); the single-frame budget is simply the wrong unit. **Principle: a timeout is a per-OPERATION-shape budget, not a global constant — when one method does fundamentally more work than another (a batch vs a frame), it needs its own budget, or the abort fires on success.** (Distinct from [[H125]]: there the fix was dedup — bounding the NUMBER of in-flight requests; here it is the BUDGET of a single legitimately-long request. Both surface as the same server-success/client-nothing contradiction, both diagnosed by `/history`.) REF: `src/core/comfy/HttpComfyUICapability.ts` (`DEFAULT_BATCH_TIMEOUT_MS` + `batchTimeoutMs` opt used in `submitBatch`). Provenance: ORIGIN = 2026-06-26 Inc 4 slice 3 live obs — the un-animated batched render timed out twice at 30s; `/history` showed `4b77c204 status_str success` (43s server time) → diagnosed the budget mismatch; after the fix a real 3-image SD1.5 batch produced a 62KB MP4 clip (ftyp). [[H125]] (the in-flight-dedup sibling); [[V81]] (the epic); dharana B24.

### H127 — Baking EVERY schedulable param into a schedule node (even constants) needlessly requires the bridge extension AND gets the un-animated batch rejected by a server that lacks it

**Symptom:** an un-animated (or flat-channel) coherent render fails on a real server with an opaque `/prompt` 400, even though nothing was keyframed.

**Root cause:** the batched baker samples ALL schedulable params over the range (mirroring the preview path), so even a param with no bound channel becomes a `BatchedTrack` of constant values. The compiler then inserted a `BasherValueSchedule` node for it → the compiled workflow referenced the custom node → a server without the BasherSchedule extension rejected it. So an un-animated render — which should be a plain workflow — gained a hard dependency on the bridge node.

**The trap (wrong fix):** "always require the extension" (wrong — an un-animated batch needs no schedule at all), "don't bake unbound params" (possible, but the baker stays simple if it bakes everything and the COMPILER decides). 

**The real fix:** in `compileBatchedWorkflow`, a CONSTANT track (`values.every(v => v === values[0])`) substitutes the literal and emits NO schedule node (and is NOT a demotion — it's just a constant). Only a genuinely-VARYING param requires the bridge node. So an un-animated render is a plain workflow that runs WITHOUT the extension installed; the extension is needed only when something actually animates (design §16 Q-E). **Principle: the in-graph machinery should scale with what's actually animated, not with what COULD be animated — a constant is a literal, not a degenerate schedule.** REF: `src/core/comfy/comfyGraph.ts` (`compileBatchedWorkflow` constant-track branch). Provenance: ORIGIN = 2026-06-26 Inc 4 slice 3 — the live un-animated batch was being rejected because every float param got a schedule node; the un-animated path only worked once constants stopped emitting nodes. Paired with the presence-detect+fallback (`comfyHasNodeTypes`, §16 Q-E). [[V81]]; dharana B24.

### H128 — Deriving a ComfyUI batch's frame count N from a project video's MediaClip `srcFrames` is wrong: Basher's media probe is 30fps-RESAMPLED, not the container's native count

**Symptom:** a `basher_controller` kind=video bound to a 6-frame / 1-second / 6fps clip, combined with a keyframed scalar controller whose count Basher derived from the clip's `srcFrames`, rendered **30** frames, not 6. (Pure video-controller-only renders were CORRECT at 6 — the bug only appears when Basher tries to compute N itself.)

**Root cause:** Basher's `WebCodecsMediaDecode` re-samples every video to a FIXED 30fps (a known decode limit), so a MediaClip's `srcFrames` = `round(durationSeconds * 30)` — NOT the container's native frame count. The extension's `basher_controller` kind=video decodes the container with PyAV (`VideoFromFile.get_components().images`) → the NATIVE frame count. For any non-30fps source the two diverge (6 native vs 30 resampled). So `boundVideoFrameCount(...) → srcFrames` fed the scalar bake the wrong N, and the video controller still emitted its own native count → ComfyUI ran `max(scalarN, videoN)`.

**The trap (wrong fix):** "derive N from the bound MediaClip srcFrames" (what I tried — only correct when the source happens to be ~30fps; silently wrong otherwise, and it MASKS the real boundary). A second workaround ("pick max / pad") would compound it.

**The real fix (✅ SHIPPED + LIVE-OBSERVED 2026-06-29):** make BOTH sides use Basher's authoritative 30fps count. (1) The EXTENSION `basher_controller` kind=video now RESAMPLES its PyAV-decoded native frames to a Basher-supplied `frame_count` (nearest-floor index map `_resample_indices`; `frame_count=0` = the standalone "use native" sentinel — input default changed 1→0/min 0). (2) Basher Mode-A (`compileComfyBatch`): when a video controller is BOUND, `N = mediaClipFrameCount(boundClip)` = the MediaClip `srcFrames` (Basher's 30fps count); it `writeBasherControllerFrameCounts(N)` onto every bound video controller (→ the extension resamples to N) AND bakes the scalar controllers over `[0, N-1]` (`bakeStart=0, bakeEnd=N-1`). Both sides now measure N the SAME way (Basher's 30fps), never `max(scalarN, videoN)`. **Principle (held): never compute a count for one side of a boundary from a probe that measures it differently than the other side — let the authoritative side (here Basher's 30fps media model) drive BOTH.** OBSERVED LIVE (SD1.5/MPS): a 3-native-frame / 0.2s RGB clip → Basher `srcFrames=6` → a 6-frame combo clip (NOT native 3, NOT a mismatch); output hue steps R,R,G,G,B,B (the 3→6 resample, measured) and `/history` shows ComfyUI received node 10 (cfg) `values_json=[2,4.4,6.8,9.2,11.6,14]`+`frame_count=6` AND node 14 (video) `frame_count=6` — both N=6, aligned (boundary-pair: Basher wrote it, ComfyUI executed it). The cfg ramp's pixel effect was masked by the saturated solid-colour fixture, but the submitted-graph payload proves it baked over N. REF: `src/app/video/compileComfyBatch.ts` (Mode-A N coordination + `boundBindingPath`); `src/app/video/comfyImageBinding.ts` (`mediaClipFrameCount`); `src/core/comfy/basherControllers.ts` (`writeBasherControllerFrameCounts`); the extension `basher_controller` (`_resample_indices`). Provenance: ORIGIN = 2026-06-29 slice 2b self-review (combo produced 30 not 6); RESOLVED same day by resampling the video side. [[V81]]; dharana B24.

---

### H129 — A keyframe channel that TARGETS a node OTHER than the timeline's row owner is invisible: the dopesheet enumerates by a FIXED prop list / by row-owner id, never by "all channels feeding this row's subject"

**Symptom:** keying a ComfyUIWorkflow SOURCE param (Mode B `comfy:<id>.<input>` or Mode A `controller:<id>`) lit a filled red `ParamDiamond` in the Controls panel, but the compositor `LayerTimeline` twirl-down showed NO keyframe dots for it — only Opacity/Rotation/Position/Scale + effect props. The animated param was real in the DAG but absent from every timeline surface. (Observed, not inferred: a `tmp` e2e keyed `comfy:3.cfg`+`comfy:6.text`, twirled the layer open, queried the rows → `[]`; the screenshot confirmed the Controls diamonds present, the timeline rows absent.)

**Root cause:** `collectChannelKeyframes(state, rowOwnerId, paramPath)` matches `channel.target === rowOwnerId`. The comfy/controller channels TARGET the ComfyUIWorkflow **source** node (the V57 `target` is the workflow node id), NOT the Layer. AND the twirl's `visualRows` were built from a FIXED list (`LAYER_PROPS`/`LAYER_VEC2_PROPS`/`EFFECT_PROPS`) — there was no enumeration of "channels feeding this layer's source." Two compounding facts: (a) the channel's target ≠ the row owner the timeline asks about; (b) the timeline never asked about the source node's channels at all. Either alone hides the dots.

**Adjacent finding (why the 3D dopesheet was the WRONG surface to probe):** the task framed it as "open the 3D `timeline-drawer`," but in VIDEO space the compositor `video-slot` (z-45, `absolute inset-0`, Layout.tsx) covers the bottom-center 3D-editor `TimelineDrawer` (z-20). A Playwright click on `timeline-drawer-toggle` is intercepted by the video-slot subtree → "the probe broke the page." The comfy layer is a VIDEO-space concept, so its keyframe surface is the compositor `LayerTimeline`, not the 3D dopesheet (H122 family: VIDEO covers 3D chrome). Don't probe the 3D dopesheet for a video-layer's channels.

**The trap (wrong fix):** (a) adding the comfy channel types to the 3D dopesheet's `collectChannelRows` CHANNEL_TYPES (TimelineCanvas) — that surface is covered in VIDEO and would show an ugly `ComfyUIWorkflow — comfy:3.cfg` label for a node you can't even reach; (b) re-targeting the comfy channel onto the Layer node so `collectChannelKeyframes(layerId,…)` matches — that would break the render bake + decode, which read the channel by its `comfy:`/`controller:` paramPath on the SOURCE.

**The real fix (✅ SHIPPED + LIVE-OBSERVED 2026-06-30, `9e9d934`):** enumerate the source's channels on the correct surface. `collectComfySourceChannelRows(state, layerId)` resolves the layer's BASE source (through any effect chain), and IF it's a `ComfyUIWorkflow`, scans the SAME `(target===sourceNode, paramPath, keyframes)` shape `collectChannelKeyframes` reads, filtered to `comfy:`/`controller:` paths. `LayerTimeline` adds a read-only `'comfy-prop'` visualRow per channel (`OutlineComfyPropRow` label = `class_type.input` / declared controller name, mirrored from the Controls panel; derived from the workflow `apiJson`, no full graph import) whose `TrackKeyframeRow` draws the dots with `nodeId = sourceNodeId` (NOT the layer). ONE enumeration covers BOTH modes (V81 unified transport) and is channel-type-agnostic (so TEXT prompt channels render too — they were never in the 3D CHANNEL_TYPES set). Authoring stays in Controls; the timeline only MIRRORS (V81: one channel, every surface). OBSERVED LIVE (SD1.5 vanilla): keyed `comfy:3.cfg`+`comfy:6.text` → twirl shows "KSampler.cfg"+"CLIPTextEncode.text" rows, each a ◆ at the keyed frame (screenshot eyeballed; testids `layer-comfy-keyframe-<layer>-<path>` count 1 each). **Principle: a dopesheet must enumerate channels by the SUBJECT the row represents (here the layer's SOURCE), not assume `channel.target === rowOwnerId`; when a row's subject is a different node than the row owner, pass the subject's id to the keyframe lookup.** REF: `src/app/video/videoLayers.ts` (`collectComfySourceChannelRows`); `src/app/video/LayerTimeline.tsx` (`'comfy-prop'` row + `OutlineComfyPropRow`); `src/app/Layout.tsx` (video-slot z-45 covers TimelineDrawer z-20). Provenance: ORIGIN = 2026-06-30 task-3 follow-up #1 ("see animated params of both modes in the timeline keyframes"); the comfy diamond was visible in Controls but not the timeline. [[V81]]; dharana B24.

### H130 — A drag handler that swallows its trailing synthetic click via a "suppress" ref leaks the flag when the drag is far enough to emit NO click — the flag then eats the NEXT genuine click on that element

**Symptom:** an element supports BOTH drag (a gesture) and click (a discrete action) and uses a `suppressClickRef` so a drag doesn't also fire the click. It works for SHORT drags, but after a LONG drag the very next genuine click on that element is silently ignored (does nothing once, then works again). Observed: a compositor dopesheet diamond dragged ~220px to retime, then Alt-clicked to delete → the delete no-op'd; a second Alt-click worked.

**Root cause:** the suppress pattern is "set `suppressClickRef=true` at pointerup-after-move; the trailing `click` reads it, resets to false, and returns early." This assumes a `click` ALWAYS follows the drag. But the browser only synthesizes a `click` when pointerdown+pointerup land on the same element within a small movement budget; a far drag (pointer ends well away from the press point, even back over the same element) emits NO `click`. So the flag is set but never consumed → it lingers `true`. The NEXT independent press → pointerup(no move, early-return, doesn't touch the flag) → genuine `click` sees the STALE `true` → resets + returns → the action is eaten.

**The trap (wrong fix):** decide "the diamond didn't get the click" and add a second listener / a setTimeout to re-arm, or move the delete onto pointerup (entangling it with the drag gesture). Both compound the state machine. **The real fix:** CLEAR the suppress flag at the START of every fresh press (`onPointerDown: suppressClickRef.current = false`), not only when a suppressed click consumes it. The same-gesture synthetic click still fires BEFORE the next pointerdown, so it is still correctly swallowed; only the STALE cross-gesture leak is cured. **Principle: a "suppress the trailing click" flag must be reset at the next gesture's start, never relied on to be consumed — the consuming event is not guaranteed to fire (a far drag emits no click), so a consume-only reset leaks across gestures.** REF: `src/app/video/LayerTimeline.tsx` (`TrackKeyframeRow` `onDiamondPointerDown` clears `suppressClickRef`; `onUp` sets it on `moved`). Provenance: ORIGIN = 2026-06-30 #2 (interactive dopesheet keyframes); a `tmp` e2e dragged a key then Alt-clicked to delete → delete no-op'd; the count-stayed-1 observation (not inference) named the lingering flag. Sister to the bar-drag `suppressClickRef` in the same file (which is safe ONLY because bars always emit a click). [[H129]]; dharana B24.

### H131 — A continuous drag that dispatches a real op on EVERY pointer move floods the undo history: one Cmd+Z reverts a single sub-pixel step, not the whole drag

**Symptom:** "Ctrl+Z barely does anything." Dragging an object from x:1 → x:1.2 with the gizmo, then pressing undo, steps back incrementally (1.2 → 1.15 → 1.1 → …) instead of snapping back to x:1 in one press. The activity log is likewise flooded with N identical "gizmo translate" lines for one gesture.

**Root cause:** the gizmo's `onObjectChange` fires on every TransformControls pointer move and calls `dispatch({setParam position})` each time — and every `dispatch` pushes its own undo entry (and clears redo). A drag is dozens of moves → dozens of undo entries. The history is recording the INTERMEDIATE frames of a continuous gesture as if each were a committed user action. (All three gizmos leaked: Single via `.dispatch`, Multi/Camera via `dispatchAtomic`. `dragScrub` was already correct — it previews locally and commits ONE setParam on pointer-up, the model the gizmo should have followed but didn't because the gizmo drives the live object through the DAG so render==gizmo holds mid-drag.)

**The trap (wrong fix):** (a) coalesce in the component — capture the start value on mousedown, suppress per-move dispatch, dispatch once on mouseup — but then the live viewport stops following the drag (the DAG is the render source), OR you bolt on a parallel transient-preview path (a second source of truth, drift risk); (b) debounce the dispatch — still N entries, just fewer; (c) collapse adjacent same-param undo entries at undo time — fragile heuristic, breaks mixed-param drags (a rotate also writes position) and the autoKey/override sub-writes.

**The real fix:** a store-level DRAG TRANSACTION. `beginInteraction()` opens a buffer; while open, `dispatch`/`dispatchBatch`/`dispatchAtomic` still mutate state (so the viewport follows live) but DEFER their undo + activity records into one flat buffer instead of pushing per-op; `endInteraction(description)` flushes the whole gesture as ONE `AtomicGroup` undo entry + ONE activity line. Undo of that group replays all buffered inverses in reverse → restores the pre-drag value in one step; redo replays the forwards. Bracket the gesture at the drag boundary (gizmo `onMouseDown`/`onMouseUp` → begin/end), NOT per move. A click with no move flushes an empty buffer (no spurious entry). Because the bracket wraps the STORE dispatch layer, every sub-path a move takes — raw setParam, the animated-keyframe re-route, the GltfChild override atomic — coalesces automatically. **Principle: the undo history must record COMMITTED ACTIONS, not the intermediate frames of a continuous gesture; coalesce a drag at the store's dispatch layer (a begin/end transaction) so the live-follow per-move writes stay but collapse to one entry — don't move the coalescing into the component (it costs you the live render) or into undo-time heuristics (fragile).** REF: `src/core/dag/store.ts` (`beginInteraction`/`endInteraction` + the `interaction` buffer guards in dispatch/dispatchBatch/dispatchAtomic), `src/app/Gizmo.tsx` (`startGizmoDrag`/`endGizmoDrag` + SingleGizmo `onDraggingChanged`). Provenance: ORIGIN = 2026-06-30 user report "history should register the committed action, not the in-betweens"; OBSERVED via the dev `__basher_gizmo_grab` seam under a bracket — a 3-move drag (x 0→1.2) produced undoStack +1 (not 3), one Ctrl+Z → x:0, redo → 1.2. Note the dev grab seam itself is UNbracketed (one grab = one entry), so existing gizmo e2e are unaffected. Sister to `dragScrub` (already commits once on up). dharana: editor-transform boundary.

**AUDIT (2026-06-30, after the gizmo fix) — OTHER instances of this leak, found by sweeping every per-move/onChange→DAG-dispatch surface:**
- **🔴 CONFIRMED unfixed — `LightStudioPanel` puck drag** (`src/timeline/LightStudioPanel.tsx:118-134`): `onPuckMove` dispatches `setParam position` on EVERY pointer-move, no draft buffer. The comment there FALSELY claims "consecutive same-path setParams coalesce into one undo entry (the EditableCurve drag pattern)" — but the store NEVER auto-coalesced; EditableCurve actually uses draft+commit-on-release, this one does not. So a puck drag = N undo entries. **A false belief about store behavior is the second-order bug here: the author thought same-path setParams auto-merge; they don't.** FIX (next session) = bracket `onPuckDown`→`beginInteraction()`, `onPuckUp`→`endInteraction('place studio light')` + delete the false comment. Trivial with the new transaction.
- **🟠 LIKELY unfixed — color swatch inputs** (`src/app/NPanel.tsx:1146-1149` ColorField, shared by material + glTF-material rows; + the light color field): `<input type="color">` maps React `onChange` to the DOM `input` event, which fires REPEATEDLY while dragging inside the OS picker → each tick `commit→onEdit→dispatch` → N undo entries. Not observed live (couldn't get a color field on screen in the probe), flagged by code + browser event semantics. FIX = a PICKER-SESSION bracket (`beginInteraction()` on first onChange, `endInteraction()` on blur/picker-close) — keeps the live viewport preview during the drag but collapses to one entry; the native picker has no clean drag start/end so the gizmo mouse bracket doesn't apply directly.
- **🟢 VERIFIED CLEAN** (no per-move DAG dispatch): `EditableCurve` (draft+commit-on-release), `dragScrub`, compositor `LayerTimeline` bar+keyframe drags, `TimelineCanvas` keyframe retime — all commit ONCE on pointer-up; `Timebar` slider / `usePanZoomCanvas` / `BoxSelectOverlay` write timeStore/UI selection, NOT the DAG. See [[V84]] for the invariant this audit promotes.
